Salah — Prayer

The Essential Elements of Sujud
Defines the reality of sujud and its obligatory parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the essential elements of sujud and distinguish between the fard (forehead) and wajib (nose) with their consequences.

Core Idea
Sujud requires the forehead and the hard part of the nose on a firm, pure surface; the nose alone does not suffice.

In this lesson, we examine the definition of sujud from the Hanafi school. The passage establishes that the forehead is the primary pillar, while the nose is an obligatory element. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct prayer and knowing when compensation is needed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Sujud is a pillar (rukn) of prayer. The passage states it is performed 'obligatorily' (wujuban).
2
List the required body parts
The text mentions forehead (jabhah), hard part of nose (sulb al-anf), toes, and mentions hands and knees as sunnah.
3
Determine fard vs wajib
The forehead is fard (essential for realization); the nose is wajib (obligatory but not fundamental).
Omitting the fard invalidates the prayer; omitting a wajib requires sujud al-sahw but does not invalidate.
4
Examine the minimal sujud scenario
The text says sujud is realized by placing the forehead, not the nose alone, plus at least one hand, one knee, and some toes.
Prostration on nose only is not valid except for an excuse like a forehead wound.
5
Identify the consequence of omission
If the forehead is missing, the prostration (and prayer) is invalid. If the nose is missing, the prayer is valid but deficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والركوع والسجود على ما يجد حجمه وتستقر عليه جبهته ولو على كفه أو طرف ثوبه إن طهر محل وضعه وسجد وجوبا بما صلب أنفه من وبجبهته، ولا يصح الاقتصار على الأنف إلا من عذر بالجبهة وعدم ارتفاع محل السجود عن موضع القدمين بأكثر من نصف ذراع، وإن زاد على نصف ذراع لم يجز السجود إلا لزحمة والارتفاع القليل لا يضر سجد فيها على ظهر مصل صلاته، ووضع اليدين والركبتين في الصحيح، ووضع شيء من أصابع الرجلين حالة السجود على الأرض، ولا يكفي وضع ظاهر القدم، وتقديم الركوع على السجود، والرفع من السجود إلى قرب القعود. والركوع وهو الانحناء بالظهر والرأس جميعاً، وكماله بتسوية الرأس بالعجز. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٢٨] والسجود: السجدة إنما تتحقق بوضع الجبهة لا الأنف وحده مع وضع إحدى اليدين وإحدى الركبتين وشيء من أطراف أصابع إحدى القدمين على طاهر من الأرض، وإلا فلا وجود لها، ومع ذلك البعض تصح على المختار مع الكراهة، وتمام السجود بإتيانه بالواجب فيه، ويتحقق بوضع جميع اليدين والركبتين والقدمين والجيهة والأنف. مراقي الفلاح: ۲۲۹، ۲۳۱] على ما يجد إلخ أي بحيث لو بالغ لا يتسفل رأسه أبلغ مما كان حال الوضع، فلا يصح السجود على القطن والثلج والتبن والأرز والذرة إلا إذا وجد اليبس مراقي الفلاح، حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٣١] ولو على كفه: أي ويصح السجود لو كان على كفه أي الساجد في الصحيح أو كان السجود على طرف ثوبه أي الساجد، ويكره بغير عذر مراقي الفلاح: ۲۳۱] على ظهر مصل: قيد بقيدين: أحدهما: أن يكون المسجود عليه مصلياً، والآخر اتحاد صلاة الساجد والمسجود عليه، فإن انتفى كلاهما أو أحدهما بأن لم يكن ذلك المسجود عليه مصلياً أو كان في صلاة أخرى لا يصح السجود ووضع وضع إحدى اليدين، وإحدى الركبتين. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٣٢]
And bowing and prostration are upon what remains firm and his forehead settles on it, even if upon his palm or the edge of his garment, provided the place of placing is pure. And he prostrates obligatorily with the hard part of his nose and his forehead. It is not valid to confine to the nose except due to an excuse of the forehead. And the place of prostration should not be elevated from the place of the feet by more than half a cubit. If it exceeds half a cubit, prostration is not permitted except due to crowding, and slight elevation does not harm. He prostrated on the back of a praying person in his prayer, and placing the hands and knees in the correct manner, and placing something from the toes of the feet during prostration on the ground, and it is not sufficient to place the outer part of the foot. And the precedence of bowing over prostration, and raising from prostration to near sitting. And bowing is bending with the back and head together, and its perfection is equalizing the head with the buttocks. [Maraqi al-Falah: 228] And prostration: the prostration is only realized by placing the forehead, not the nose alone, together with placing one of the hands, one of the knees, and something from the tips of the toes of one of the feet on pure ground; otherwise it has no existence. However, some of that is valid according to the chosen view with dislike. And the completion of prostration is by performing the obligatory duties therein, and it is realized by placing all the hands, knees, feet, forehead and nose. [Maraqi al-Falah: 229, 231] 'Upon what remains firm' etc. means such that if he exerts, his head does not sink more than it was at the time of placement, so prostration on cotton, snow, straw, rice, and corn is not valid unless there is hardness. [Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 231] 'Even if upon his palm' means: and prostration is valid if it is upon his palm, i.e. the palm of the one prostrating, or if prostration is upon the edge of his garment i.e. the edge of the prostrator's garment, and it is disliked without excuse. [Maraqi al-Falah: 231] 'On the back of a praying person' is restricted by two restrictions: one: the one prostrated upon must be praying, and the other, the union of the prayer of the prostrator and the one prostrated upon. If both or one of these is absent, such as if the one prostrated upon is not praying or is in another prayer, prostration is not valid. And placing one of the hands and one of the knees. [Maraqi al-Falah: 232]
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage defines the essential rules of prostration (sujud) and bowing (ruku') in prayer. It begins by describing that prostration must be on a firm surface that retains its shape, so the forehead can settle. It is permissible to prostrate on one's own hand or the edge of one's garment provided that part is pure. The obligatory part of prostration is placing the hard part of the nose along with the forehead. Confining prostration only to the nose is not valid except when there is an excuse involving the forehead. The place of prostration should not be raised more than half a cubit above the level where the feet rest; if it exceeds that, prostration is not valid unless there is overcrowding. A slight elevation does not harm. Regarding prostration on the back of another worshipper, it is valid only if the person being prostrated upon is himself performing the same prayer; otherwise, it is invalid. The passage then explains the reality of prostration: it is achieved by placing the forehead (not the nose alone), along with at least one hand, one knee, and some toes on the ground. If any of these are omitted, the prostration is not properly realized, though some scholars deem it valid with dislike. Completing prostration requires fulfilling its obligatory elements, which are placing all the hands, knees, feet, forehead, and nose. The commentary clarifies that 'upon what remains firm' means the material must be hard enough that the head does not sink further. Therefore, prostration on cotton, snow, straw, rice, or corn is invalid unless they are hard (e.g., dried). Prostration on one's palm or the edge of one's garment is valid but disliked without a valid excuse. The ruling on prostration on another praying person is subject to two conditions: the person must be praying, and both must be in the same prayer. If either condition is unmet, the prostration is invalid.

Key Terms
سجود (sujud): Prostration; placing the forehead and the hard part of the nose on a pure, firm surface.
جبهة (jabhah): The forehead, which must be placed on the ground for sujud to be valid.
أنف (anf): The nose; its hard part (sulb al-anf) must touch the ground in sujud as a wajib element.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi prayer, what is the minimum requirement for a valid prostration (sujud)?
A) Placing only the forehead on the ground
B) Placing the forehead and the hard part of the nose on a firm surface
C) Placing the nose alone on the ground
D) Prostrating on any surface, even soft cotton

Key Takeaway
Sujud is realized by the forehead (fard) and the hard part of the nose (wajib) on a firm, pure surface; the nose alone does not suffice.

Resolving the Tartib Dispute: Is Order Between Ruku' and Sujud Fard or Wajib?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tartib and its resolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi classification of tartib as fard, distinguish its practical consequences from a mere wajib, and cite the resolution by Ibn Qadi Simawwah.

Core Idea
Tartib between ruku' and sujud is fard: the second pillar is invalid without the first.

This lesson addresses a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute: is the order between bowing and prostration an integral (fard) or merely an obligation (wajib)? The source presents a seeming contradiction in al-Kafi, then resolves it with a precise distinction from Ibn Qadi Simawwah. Understanding this resolution is key to knowing when the prayer becomes invalid versus when it requires only compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
What is exactly being disputed? The order (tartib) between ruku' and sujud in prayer: is it fard (integral) or wajib (obligatory but not integral)?
2
State the two conflicting positions from al-Kafi
One passage says breaking tartib invalidates prayer (implies fard). Another passage says it only requires sajdat al-sahw (implies wajib). Recognize the apparent contradiction.
The contradiction arises from different implications of the same text.
3
Follow the resolution by Ibn Qadi Simawwah
He distinguishes farziyyah (tartib as fard means second depends on first) from wujub (violation does not invalidate prayer if repeated). The meaning of fard here is that the second element is not valid without the first, so it must be repeated.
This resolution harmonizes the two statements.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If intentionally prostrating before bowing: according to fard view, the prostration is invalid and must be repeated, potentially invalidating the prayer if not corrected. According to wajib view, the prayer is valid but requires sajdat al-sahw.
The practical difference lies in whether the prayer becomes invalid or not.
5
Identify the mufta bihi view
The relied-upon view (al-ashahh) is that tartib is fard. The prayer is invalid if the order is intentionally violated and not corrected.
This is the position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتقديم الركوع إلخ: أي ويشترط لصحة الركوع والسجود تقديم الركوع على السجود. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٣٢] ومقتضاه أنه إذا ركع قبل أن يقرأ أو سجد قبل أن يركع فسدت، وفي "الكافي" ما يفيده، وفيه من سجود السهو: لو قدم ركنا عن ركن سجد للسهو، وهذا يقتضي وجوب رعاية الترتيب دون فرضيته، وفيه تناقض، وأجاب صاحب جامع الفصولين" العلامة ابن قاضي سماوة في شرح التسهيل" بأن معنى فرضية الترتيب توقف صحة الثاني على وجود الأول، حتى لوركع بعد السجود لا يكون السجود معتدا به، فيلزمه إعادته، ومعنى وجوبه: أن الإخلال به لا يفسد الصلاة إذا أعاده حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٣٣] على الأصح، والعود إلى السجود والقعود الأخير قدر التشهد، وتأخيره عن الأركان، وأداؤها مستيقظا
And the precedence of bowing etc.: meaning it is required for the validity of bowing and prostration that bowing precede prostration. [Maraqi al-Falah: 232] Its implication is that if he bows before reciting or prostrates before bowing, the prayer becomes invalid. In 'al-Kafi' there is something that supports this. And in it (al-Kafi) concerning prostration of forgetfulness: if one brings a pillar before another pillar, he makes prostration of forgetfulness. This implies the obligation (wujub) of observing the order, not its being an integral (farziyyah). There is contradiction. And the author of 'Jam' al-Fusulayn', the scholar Ibn Qadi Simawwah, in 'Sharh al-Tashil' answered: The meaning of farziyyah of order is that the validity of the second is dependent on the existence of the first, such that if he bows after prostration, the prostration is not considered valid and he must repeat it. And the meaning of wujub is that violating it does not invalidate the prayer if he repeats it. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 233] According to the most correct view, and returning to prostration and the final sitting to the extent of tashahhud, and delaying it from the pillars, and performing them while awake.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage addresses the crucial issue of the order (tartib) between bowing and prostration in prayer. The starting point is the requirement that bowing must precede prostration. The text then notes a seeming contradiction in Hanafi sources. One source (al-Kafi) indicates that if someone bows before reciting or prostrates before bowing, the prayer is invalidated, suggesting that tartib is an integral (farz). However, another passage from the same book states that if one brings one pillar before another, the worshipper should perform the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw). This latter point implies that tartib is only wajib (obligatory but not integral), because a missing integral would require repeating the prayer, not just sajdat al-sahw. To resolve this, the author of 'Jam' al-Fusulayn' (Ibn Qadi Simawwah) provides a precise distinction: the 'farziyyah' of tartib means that the second element's validity is contingent on the first having been performed. For example, if someone bows after having already prostrated, that prostration is not counted, and he must repeat it. The prayer is not invalidated outright, but the element is not valid and must be redone. On the other hand, if the order is violated unintentionally and the worshipper repeats the missed element in sequence, the prayer is not invalidated. This is the meaning of it being wajib rather than farz in the sense of being an indispensable condition. The relied-upon view (al-ashahh) is that tartib is farz, meaning the second element depends on the first, but the practical difference is that if forgotten, sajdat al-sahw is required. The passage then mentions other related conditions: returning to prostration (if missed), the final sitting to the extent of tashahhud, delaying it from the pillars, and performing the acts while awake.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartib): The order of pillars, specifically that bowing (ruku') must come before prostration (sujud).
الفرضية (al-farziyyah): The status of being an integral (fard) whose omission invalidates the element or prayer.
الوجوب (al-wujub): Obligation but not to the extent of invalidating the prayer; violation requires sajdat al-sahw.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling regarding the order (tartib) between ruku' and sujud in Hanafi fiqh?
A) Tartib is sunnah, so violation does not affect the prayer.
B) Tartib is fard, meaning the validity of the second pillar depends on the first, and intentional violation invalidates the prayer.
C) Tartib is wajib, so violation only requires sajdat al-sahw and does not invalidate the prayer.
D) Tartib is not required at all; the pillars can be performed in any order.

Key Takeaway
The order between ruku' and sujud is fard in Hanafi fiqh, meaning the second pillar is invalid without the first, but unintentional violations can be corrected without restarting the prayer.

Conditions of Being Awake and Knowledge of Obligatory Acts
States that pillars must be performed awake, and the worshipper must know the obligatory acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for the validity of obligatory prayer: being awake during pillars and having knowledge of the obligatory nature of the prayer, and apply them to scenarios of sleep and ignorance.

Core Idea
Performing a pillar while asleep invalidates it; you must know which prayers are fard to discharge your obligation.

This lesson clarifies two subtle conditions that affect the validity of prayer: the requirement to be awake for the pillars, and the requirement to have basic knowledge that the prayer being performed is fard and not sunnah. These conditions prevent the prayer from being nullified due to unintentional sleep or confusion between fard and sunnah prayers. The passage also touches on a dispute regarding the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) and gives examples of what knowledge is sufficient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Read the passage and list the two conditions stated for the validity of obligatory prayer: being awake during the pillars, and having knowledge of the obligatory nature of the prayer.
The condition of being awake applies to each pillar individually.
2
Analyze the condition of being awake
Understand what happens if sleep occurs during a pillar (not counted) versus after a pillar (valid). Pay attention to the final sitting dispute.
The final sitting is disputed: some say it is a pillar, others a condition.
3
Examine the knowledge condition
Determine what knowledge is required: general belief that a specific prayer (e.g., Fajr is 2 fard rak'ahs) is fard, and distinguishing fard from sunnah prayers in general. Note that specific distinctions within the prayer are not required.
An alternative view: believing all prayers performed are fard also suffices.
4
Summarize external conditions
List the external conditions mentioned at the end of the passage: purification, covering awrah, facing qiblah, time, intention, and opening takbir.
These are standard conditions assumed known from earlier lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستيقظاً : فإذا ركع أو قام أو سجد نائماً لم يعتد به، وإن طرأ فيه النوم صح بما قبله منه، وفي القعدة الأخيرة خلاف، قال في "منية المصلي: إذا لم يعدها بطلت، وفي "جامع الفتاوى": يعتد بها نائماً؛ لأنها ليست بركن ومبناها على الاستراحة فيلائمها النوم قلت: وهو ثمرة الاختلاف في شرطيتها وركنيتها. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٣٥] ومعرفة كيفية إلخ أي ويشترط لصحة أداء المفروض إما "معرفة كيفيته" يعني صفة الصلاة، وذلك بمعرفة حقيقة "ما فيها أي ما في جملة الصلوات من الخصال" أي الصفات الفرضية، يعني كونها فرضا فيعتقد افتراض ركعتي الفجر وأربع الظهر، وهكذا باقي الصلوات المفروضة" فيكون ذلك على وجه يميزها عن "الخصال" أي الصفات "المسنونة" كالسنن الرواتب وغيرها باعتقاد سنية ما قبل الظهر وما بعده ،وهكذا و ليس المراد ولا الشرط أن يميز ما اشتملت عليه صلاة الصبح من الفرض والسنة، مثل اعتقاد فرضية القيام وسنية الثناء و والتسبيح، "أو اعتقاد" المصلي "أنها" أي أن ذات الصلوات التي يفعلها كلها "فرض" كاعتقاده أن الأربع في الفجر فرض، ويصلي كل ركعتين بانفرادهما ويأتي بثلاث، ثم ركعتين في المغرب معتقداً فرضية الخمس. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٣٥] حتى لا يتنفل إلخ معنى هذا التفريع أنه إنما حكم بصحة الفرض في هذه الصورة؛ لأنه نوى الفرض، فيسقط عنه، ولا يكون نفلا، بل النفل ما زاد وإن نواه فرضاً؛ لأن النفل يتأدى بنية الفرض [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٣٦] ما كان خارجها وهو الطهارة من الحدث والخبث وستر العورة واستقبال القبلة والوقت، والنية، والتحريمة. مراقي الفلاح: ٢٣٦] وغيره : كإيقاع القراءة في القيام، وكون الركوع بعده، والسجود بعده، والاستيقاظ. حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٣٧]
Awake: so if he bows, stands, or prostrates while sleeping, it is not counted. And if sleep occurs in it, what preceded it is valid. Regarding the last sitting, there is disagreement. It is said in 'Munyat al-Musalli': if he does not repeat it, the prayer becomes invalid. And in 'Jami' al-Fatawa': it is counted while sleeping because it is not a pillar and its basis is rest, so sleeping suits it. I say: This is the fruit of the difference in it being a condition (shartiyyah) or a pillar (rukn). [Maraqi al-Falah: 235] And knowledge of the how etc. meaning: it is required for the validity of performing the obligatory prayer either 'knowledge of its modality' meaning the description of the prayer, by knowing the reality of 'what is in it, i.e. in the totality of prayers, of characteristics' i.e. the obligatory attributes, meaning that they are fard, so he believes in the obligation of the two rak'ahs of Fajr and four of Dhuhr, and so on for the rest of the obligatory prayers. So that is a way to distinguish them from 'the characteristics' i.e. the attributes that are 'sunnah' such as the regular sunan and others, by believing in the sunnah nature of what is before Dhuhr and after it, etc. And the intent is not nor the condition that he distinguish what the morning prayer comprises of fard and sunnah, such as believing in the obligation of standing and the sunnah of thana' and tasbih. 'Or belief' of the worshipper 'that they' i.e. that the prayers themselves that he performs are all 'fard', like his belief that the four in Fajr are obligatory, and he prays every two rak'ahs individually and comes with three, then two rak'ahs in Maghrib believing in the obligation of the five. [Maraqi al-Falah: 235] 'So that he does not perform supererogatory' etc. The meaning of this reasoning is that the ruling of validity of the fard in this case is because he intended the fard, so it discharges it, and it becomes not supererogatory. Rather, supererogatory is what is extra, even if he intends it as fard, because supererogatory prayer is performed by the intention of fard. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 236] What is outside it: that is, purification from hadath and khabath, covering the awrah, facing the qiblah, time, intention, and the opening takbir. [Maraqi al-Falah: 236] And other things: like performing recitation in standing, and that bowing is after it, and prostration is after it, and being awake. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 237]
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage establishes two important conditions for the validity of the obligatory prayer. First, the worshipper must be awake while performing the pillars. If someone performs bowing, standing, or prostration while asleep, those actions are not counted. However, if sleep occurs after an action, that action is valid. There is a difference of opinion regarding the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah). According to Munyat al-Musalli, if one does not repeat it (meaning if it was performed while sleeping and not repeated while awake), the prayer is invalid. According to Jami' al-Fatawa, it is counted even if done while asleep because the final sitting is not a pillar; it is based on rest, so sleep does not invalidate it. The author notes that this difference stems from whether the final sitting is considered a condition (shart) or a pillar (rukn). Second, the worshipper must have a general knowledge of the obligatory nature of the prayer and must be able to distinguish between what is obligatory (fard) and what is recommended (sunnah). The text explains that it is sufficient for one to know, for example, that Fajr consists of two obligatory rak'ahs, Dhuhr of four, etc., and to believe that the regular sunnan (like those before and after Dhuhr) are sunnah. It is not necessary to distinguish which specific actions within the prayer are fard and which are sunnah (e.g., that standing is fard and thana' is sunnah). Alternatively, if the worshipper simply believes that all the prayers he performs are fard (even if he adds extra rak'ahs), the obligation is discharged as long as he intended the fard. This prevents him from accidentally performing a supererogatory prayer instead of the obligatory one. The passage concludes by listing the external conditions for prayer: purification from hadath and najas, covering the awrah, facing the qiblah, correct time, intention, and the opening takbir. Internal conditions include performing recitation in standing, ensuring ruku' follows recitation, sujud follows ruku', and being awake.

Key Terms
مستيقظاً (mustayqizan): Being awake; a condition that pillars of prayer must be performed while conscious.
معرفة كيفية الصلاة (ma'rifat kayfiyyat al-salah): Knowledge of the modality of prayer; knowing which prayers are fard and which are sunnah.
الخصال الفرضية (al-khisal al-fardiyyah): The obligatory characteristics or elements; the specific acts that are fard in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required regarding a person's knowledge while performing an obligatory prayer?
A) He must know exactly which specific actions are fard and which are sunnah within the prayer.
B) He must have a general belief that the prayer he is performing is fard and distinguish it from sunnah prayers.
C) He must have memorized all the conditions of prayer.
D) He does not need any knowledge; intention alone suffices.

Key Takeaway
Two conditions must be met for the obligatory prayer to be valid: pillars must be performed while awake, and the worshipper must have a general belief that the prayer he is performing is obligatory.

The Four Pillars of Prayer and the Status of the Final Sitting
Explaining the pillars and the dispute over the final sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four pillars of prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain why the final sitting is considered wajib, not rukn.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school identifies four pillars of prayer; the final sitting is a wajib, not a rukn, and its omission can be compensated by sajdah al-sahw.

This lesson focuses on the fundamental components of prayer known as pillars (arkan). The Hanafi school firmly holds that the pillars are four: standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. A debated issue is the final sitting (al-qu'ud al-akhir): some scholars consider it a pillar, but the relied-upon Hanafi view is that it is a wajib. Understanding this distinction is essential for determining the validity of prayer and the need for corrective prostration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four pillars
Read the passage and list the four pillars explicitly mentioned as 'al-arkan min al-madhkoorat arba'ah'.
The passage states: al-qiyam, al-qira'ah, al-ruku', al-sujud.
2
Distinguish rukn from wajib
Recall the Hanafi usul principle: a rukn is an integral part whose omission invalidates the prayer entirely; a wajib is obligatory but can be compensated with sajdah al-sahw if omitted forgetfully.
This distinction is key to understanding the dispute over the final sitting.
3
Analyze the dispute over the final sitting
Note that some scholars consider the final sitting a pillar. The passage cites conflicting fatwas: Munyat al-Musalli says if one sleeps during it and does not repeat it, the prayer is invalid; Jami' al-Fatawa says it is valid because it is not a pillar but a resting position.
The author concludes that this disagreement stems from whether it is a shart or a rukn.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The author states 'ala al-ashahh (on the most correct view) that the final sitting is not a pillar. The Hanafi mufta bihi is that it is a wajib, so omission requires sajdah al-sahw.
Later authorities like al-Haskafi and Ibn Abidin confirm this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على الأصح، والعود إلى السجود والقعود الأخير قدر التشهد، وتأخيره عن الأركان، وأداؤها مستيقظا ومعرفة كيفية الصلاة وما فيها من الخصال المفروضة على وجه يميزها من الخصال المسنونة أو اعتقاد أنها فرض حتى لا يتنفل بمفروض، والأركان من المذكورات أربعة: القيام والقراءة، والركوع والسجود، وقيل: القعود الأخير مقدار التشهد وباقيها شرائط بعضها شرط لصحة الشروع في وهو ما كان خارجها، وغيره شرط لدوام صحتها. الصلاة، على الأصح وذكر بعض المشايخ أنه إذا زائل جبهته عن الأرض، ثم أعادها جازت، ولم يعلم له تصحيح. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٣٣] مستيقظاً : فإذا ركع أو قام أو سجد نائماً لم يعتد به، وإن طرأ فيه النوم صح بما قبله منه، وفي القعدة الأخيرة خلاف، قال في "منية المصلي: إذا لم يعدها بطلت، وفي "جامع الفتاوى": يعتد بها نائماً؛ لأنها ليست بركن ومبناها على الاستراحة فيلائمها النوم قلت: وهو ثمرة الاختلاف في شرطيتها وركنيتها. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٣٥] ومعرفة كيفية إلخ أي ويشترط لصحة أداء المفروض إما "معرفة كيفيته" يعني صفة الصلاة، وذلك بمعرفة حقيقة "ما فيها أي ما في جملة الصلوات من الخصال" أي الصفات الفرضية، يعني كونها فرضا فيعتقد افتراض ركعتي الفجر وأربع الظهر، وهكذا باقي الصلوات المفروضة" فيكون ذلك على وجه يميزها عن "الخصال" أي الصفات "المسنونة" كالسنن الرواتب وغيرها باعتقاد سنية ما قبل الظهر وما بعده ،وهكذا وليس المراد ولا الشرط أن يميز ما اشتملت عليه صلاة الصبح من الفرض والسنة، مثل اعتقاد فرضية القيام وسنية الثناء والتسبيح، "أو اعتقاد" المصلي "أنها" أي أن ذات الصلوات التي يفعلها كلها "فرض" كاعتقاده أن الأربع في الفجر فرض، ويصلي كل ركعتين بانفرادهما ويأتي بثلاث، ثم ركعتين في المغرب معتقداً فرضية الخمس. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٣٥] حتى لا يتنفل إلخ معنى هذا التفريع أنه إنما حكم بصحة الفرض في هذه الصورة؛ لأنه نوى الفرض، فيسقط عنه، ولا يكون نفلا، بل النفل ما زاد وإن نواه فرضاً؛ لأن النفل يتأدى بنية الفرض [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٣٦] ما كان خارجها وهو الطهارة من الحدث والخبث وستر العورة واستقبال القبلة والوقت، والنية، والتحريمة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٣٦] وغيره : كإيقاع القراءة في القيام، وكون الركوع بعده، والسجود بعده، والاستيقاظ. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٣٧]
According to the most correct view, and returning to prostration and the final sitting to the extent of the tashahhud, and delaying it after the pillars, performing them while awake, knowing the manner of prayer and what it contains of obligatory characteristics in a way that distinguishes them from recommended characteristics, or believing that it is obligatory so that one does not perform a supererogatory act with an obligatory intention. The pillars from the mentioned are four: standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. It is said: the final sitting to the extent of the tashahhud. The rest are conditions: some are conditions for the validity of beginning, which are what is external to the prayer, and others are conditions for the continuity of its validity. [On the correct view] and some shaykhs mentioned that if he removes his forehead from the ground and then returns it, it is permissible, and he is not aware of any correction of that. [Awake:] If he bows, stands, or prostrates while sleeping, it is not considered. If sleep occurs during the prayer, what before it is valid. Regarding the final sitting, there is a disagreement. It is said in Munyat al-Musalli: If he does not repeat it, the prayer is invalid. In Jami' al-Fatawa: It is considered valid while sleeping because it is not a pillar and is based on resting, so sleep suits it. I say: This is the fruit of the difference regarding whether it is a condition or a pillar. [Knowing the manner, etc.] That is, for the validity of performing the obligatory, it is required either "knowing its manner," meaning the description of the prayer, by knowing the reality of "what is in it, i.e., in the entirety of prayers, of characteristics," i.e., the obligatory qualities, meaning that it is obligatory, so he believes the two rak'ahs of Fajr and four of Zuhr are obligatory, and likewise the rest of the obligatory prayers, so that distinguishes them from "characteristics" i.e., "recommended" qualities like the regular sunan and others by believing the pre- and post-Zuhr sunan are recommended, etc. The intent nor condition is to distinguish what the morning prayer contains of obligatory and sunnah, like believing standing is obligatory and the thana' and tasbih are sunnah, "or the worshiper's belief "that they" i.e., the very prayers he performs are all "obligatory," like his belief that the four in Fajr are obligatory, and he prays each two rak'ahs separately and then three, then two in Maghrib believing the five are obligatory. [So that he does not supererogate with obligatory etc.] The meaning of this sub-point is that the obligatory prayer is deemed valid in this case because he intended the obligatory, so it suffices him and is not supererogatory; rather supererogatory is what is extra even if he intends it as obligatory, because supererogatory is performed with the intention of obligatory. [What is external to it:] Purification from major and minor impurity and filth, covering the private parts, facing the qibla, time, intention, and the takbir. [And other:] Like performing recitation while standing, bowing after it, prostration after it, and being awake.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage from the section on conditions and pillars of prayer defines the arkan and shurut. The author, al-Shurunbulali, states that on the most correct view, the pillars are four: standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. Some scholars, however, consider the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) to the extent of the tashahhud as a pillar, but the preferred view is that it is not a pillar but a wajib. The discussion then covers the condition of being awake: if one prays while asleep, the actions are not valid. There is ikhtilaf regarding the final sitting if one falls asleep during it; the author quotes conflicting fatwas and notes the disagreement stems from whether it is considered a rukn or a shart. The passage also explains the condition of knowing the manner of prayer: the worshiper must have a general knowledge of the obligatory and recommended acts but does not need to distinguish every minute detail. Finally, the external conditions for the validity of prayer are listed: purification, covering awrah, facing qibla, time, intention, and takbir. The internal conditions are things like performing recitation while standing and orderly sequence. This exposition is typical of Hanafi fiqh, emphasizing the distinction between arkan (pillars that invalidate if omitted) and shurut (conditions that must be present).

Key Terms
ركن (rukn): An integral part of the prayer whose omission invalidates the prayer entirely.
شرط (shart): A condition required for the validity of the prayer, external to the act itself (e.g., taharah, time).
القعود الأخير (al-qu'ud al-akhir): The final sitting after the last prostration, to the extent of reciting the tashahhud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the four pillars of prayer?
A) Standing
B) Recitation
C) Bowing
D) Final sitting

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the prayer has four pillars; the final sitting is a wajib whose omission requires sajdah al-sahw, not invalidation.

Conditions for the Validity of Prayer: External, Internal, and the Requirement of Knowledge
Explaining the conditions for prayer validity including the knowledge requirement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the external and internal conditions for the validity of prayer according to the Hanafi school, and explain the condition that the worshiper must know the obligatory nature of the prayer.

Core Idea
Prayer validity requires external conditions (taharah, qibla, time, etc.) and internal conditions (order, recitation in standing, etc.), plus the worshiper's knowledge that the prayer is obligatory.

This lesson covers the conditions (shurut) that must be present for prayer to be valid. The passage distinguishes conditions for beginning (shurut al-sihha) from conditions for continuity (shurut al-dawam). It also stresses that the worshiper must have basic knowledge that the prayer being performed is obligatory, to avoid performing a supererogatory act with an obligatory intention.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish external and internal conditions
External conditions (shurut al-sihha) are those outside the prayer itself, like purification and time. Internal conditions (shurut al-dawam) ensure the prayer's continuity, like order and being awake.
The passage mentions: 'ba'duha shart li-sihhat al-shuru' fihi wa huwa ma kana kharijaha, wa ghayruhu shart li-dawam sihhatiha.'
2
List the external conditions
From the passage: purification from hadath and najasah, covering awrah, facing qibla, entry of time, intention, and the takbir (takbirat al-ihram).
These are explicitly mentioned at the end of the passage.
3
List the internal conditions
Internal conditions include performing recitation while standing, bowing after recitation, prostration after bowing, and being awake for the pillars.
The passage states: 'wa ghayruhu: ka-iqa' al-qira'ah fi al-qiyam, wa kawn al-ruku' ba'dahu, wa al-sujud ba'dahu, wa al-istiqadh.'
4
Explain the knowledge condition
The worshiper must know the manner (kayfiyya) of prayer, meaning he must believe the specific prayer is obligatory (fard). He does not need to distinguish every sunnah component.
The passage says: 'wa ma'rifat kayfiyat al-salat... bi i'tiqad anna al-salat fard.'
5
Understand the ruling on mistaken belief
If a person prays thinking it is fard when it is actually nafl, the prayer counts as the intended fard? The passage says if one intends fard, it suffices; if one intends nafl but mistakenly performs fard, it may not count.
The passage addresses this: 'inna al-nafl yata'adda bi-niyyat al-fard' – supererogatory can be performed with intention of obligatory? Actually, it says the obligatory is valid if one intended it; if one intended nafl, it is not fard.

Praying on Impure Objects: Thickness, Separation, and Movement
Rulings on impurity on prayer surfaces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which prayer is valid when impurity is on a thick object (libad), a double-layered garment (mudrib), or a turban, and apply the Hanafi rule regarding movement of impurity.

Core Idea
A thick object separates the worshiper from impurity; movement of impurity invalidates contact.

The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between different types of impure objects during prayer. Thick materials like felt act as barriers, while double-layered garments transfer impurity. Even a turban's moving impure end can break the prayer. Let's explore these distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Define libad and mudrib
Identify what qualifies as a thick object (libad) and what makes a garment double-layered (mudrib) from the definitions in the text.
Libad must be splittable into two halves; mudrib has sides and middle sewn.
2
State the ruling for each case
For libad with pure top and impure bottom: prayer is valid. For pure garment with impure lining: valid only if not mudrib. For pure edge on impure mat: valid even if the impure edge moves.
3
Apply the turban movement rule
If one end of the turban is impure, remove it and keep the pure part on the head. If the impure part moves with you, prayer is invalid; if still, valid.
Movement causes contact with impurity.
4
Analyze the thin mat ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad permits a thin cloth over wet impurity if it can be worn; al-Halwani requires folding to double layers. Understand the basis: thickness as barrier.
Intra-Hanafi disagreement on sufficiency of single layer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
فصل [ في متعلقات الشروط وفروعها ]
تجوز الصلاة على لبد وجهه الأعلى طاهر والأسفل نجس، وعلى ثوب طاهر وبطانته نجسة إذا كان غير مضرب، وعلى طرف طاهر وإن تحرك الطرف النجس بحركته على الصحيح، ولو تنجس أحد طرفي عمامته فألقاه وأبقى الطاهر على رأسه ولم يتحرك النجس بحركته جازت صلاته وإن تحرك لا تجوز وفاقد ما يزيل به النجاسة يصلي معها، ولا إعادة عليه ولا على فاقد ما يستر عورته ولو حريرا أو حشيشا أو طينا، أو أوراق شجر
لبد : المراد به كل ما كان له جرم غليظ يصلح للشق نصفين كحجر ولبنة وبساط. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۲۳۷] نجس أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان النجس بنجاسة مانعة أو غير مانعة أما إذا كانت النجاسة غير مانعة فطاهر، وأما إذا كانت مانعة فلأنه لثخانته كثوبين مضرب المراد بالمضرب ما كان جوانبه مخيطة ووسطه مخيطا مضربا [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۲۳۷]
على الصحيح: قال في "البحر": ولو صلى على بساط وعلى طرف منه نجاسة، فالأصح أنه يجوز كبيراً كان أو صغيراً؛ لأنه بمنزلة الأرض، فلا يصير مستعملا للنجاسة، وهو بالطريق الأولى؛ لأن النجاسة إذا كانت لا تمنع في موضع الركبتين واليدين فههنا أولى. وفي "الخلاصة : ولو بسط بساطا رقيقاً على الموضع النجس وصلى عليه، إن كان البساط بحال يصلح ساتراً للعورة بأن لا يصف ما تحته تجوز الصلاة وإن كانت رطبة فألقى عليها ثوباً وصلى، إن كان ثوباً يمكن أن يجعل من عرضه ثوباً يجوز عند محمد له، وإن كان لا يمكن لا يجوز، وكذا لو ألقى عليها لبداً فصلى عليه يجوز، وقال الحلواني: لا يجوز حتى يلقي على هذا الطرف الطرف الآخر فيصير بمنزلة ثوبين، وإن كانت النجاسة يابسة جازت، يعني إذا كان يصلح ساتراً. [البحر الرائق: ٥٢٩/١] لا تجوز: لأن المعتبر في الثوب هو الحمل، وهو حامله حكماً. [مراقي الفلاح: ۲۳۸] وفاقد ما يزيل إلخ أي من عدم ما يزيل به النجاسة من الماء والمائع والتراب لا يجب عليه غسل النجاسة، بل يصلي معها، ثم إذا وجد المزيل لا يجب عليه إعادة ما صلى معها وإن كان الوقت باقياً؛ لأن الله تعالى لا يكلف نفساً إلا وسعها. ولا على فاقد إلخ أي ولا يجب إعادة الصلاة على من فقد ما يستر به عورته ولو كان الساتر حريراً وغيره بما ذكره، أفاد أنه لو وجد الحرير ولم يجد غيره لزمه الصلاة فيه؛ لأنه مبتلى ببليتين: كشف العورة، وحرمة لبس الحرير، وفرض الستر أقوى من منع لبسه في هذه الحالة، ولا إثم عليه، ويأثم عند القدرة على غيره مع صحة الصلاة.
فإن وجده ولو بالإباحة وربعه طاهر لا تصح صلاته عاريا، وخُيّر إن طهر أقل من ربعه، وصلاته في ثوب نجس الكل أحب من صلاته عريانا، ولو وجد ما يستر بعض العورة وجب استعماله ويستر القبل والدبر فإن لم يستر إلا أحدهما قيل:
فإن وجده إلخ: أي فإن وجد مصل ثوبا ربعه طاهر وصلى عريانا، لا تصح صلاته، وإن كان أباح ذلك الثوب له أحد ولم يملكه إياه قيد بالوجدان؛ فإنه إن لم يجد تصح صلاته عاريا، ولا يجب عليه إعادتها ولا تأخيرها عن الوقت، قال في "البحر": وينبغي أن تلزمه الإعادة عندنا إذا كان العجز لمنع من العباد، كما إذا غصب ثوبه؛ لما صرحوا به في باب "التيمم أن المنع من الماء إذا كان من قبل العباد يلزمه الإعادة وبطهارة الربع؛ فإنه إن لم يكن ربعه طاهراً بل أقل من الربع، فهو مخير بين أن يصلي عارياً أو ساتراً عورته كما سيجيء بعد ذلك، ولو كان أكثر من الربع طاهراً فالحكم بعدم صحة صلاته بالأولى، وقوله: "بالإباحة" أي أعطاه أحد ثوبا لا بطريق التمليك، بل للانتفاع به مثلا، فإنه لو أعطاه أحد على سبيل التمليك فالحكم بعدم جوازها بالأولى. واعلم أن الفرق بين الإباحة والتمليك أن المباح له لا يجوز له إلا الانتفاع بذلك الشيء، ولا يدخل في ملكه، والمملك له يدخل الشيء في ملكه مثال الإباحة طعام الضيافة، فإنه يجوز للأضياف أكله، ولا يجوز أن لأحد؛ لأنهم لم يملكوه، ولم يملكهم صاحب المنزل، ولا يجوز أن يأخذ منه شيئاً ويعود به إلى بيته من غير إذن من المضيف، وإن فعل أثم ومثال التمليك كمال الزكاة فإنه يجوز للفقير أن يتصرف فيه تصرف الملاك من البيع والهبة والإجارة ونحوها.
ولو بالإباحة أما إذا لم يبح له لم تثبت قدرته عليه فيصلي عريانا؛ لعدم جواز الانتفاع بملك الغير بدون مسوغ شرعي. [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ۲۳۸] لا تصح صلاته إلخ ولا يخفى أن محله ما إذا لم يجد ما يزيل به النجاسة ولا ما يقللها، فإن وجد في الصورتين وجب استعماله، بخلاف ما إذا وجد ماء يكفي بعض أعضاء الوضوء، فإنه يتيمم ولا يجب استعماله البحر الرائق: ٥٣٩/١] وخير إن طهر إلخ حاصله: أنه بالخيار بين أن يصلي فيه، وهو الأفضل، وبين أن يصلي عريانا قاعدا يؤمي بالركوع والسجود، وهو يليه في الفضل؛ لما فيه من ستر العورة المغلظة، أو قائما عريانا بركوع وسجود، وهو دونهما في الفضل، أو مؤمياً وهذا دونهما، وظاهر "الهداية" منعه، فإنه قال في الذي لا يجد ثوباً: فإن صلى قائماً أجزأه؛ لأن في القعود ستر العورة الغليظة، وفي القيام أداء هذه الأركان، فيميل إلى أيهما شاء، قال الزيلعي: ولو كان الإيماء جائزاً حالة القيام لما استقام هذا الكلام. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۲۳۹] نجس الكل مجرور على أنه نعت لثوب، فإن الإضافة لفظية. قيل: قال في "النهر " : والظاهر أن الخلاف في الأولوية. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٤٢]
The book of prayer. Chapter on the attachments of conditions and their branches. Prayer is permissible on a felt whose upper side is pure and lower side impure, and on a pure garment with an impure lining if it is not stitched (as a double layer), and on a pure edge even if the impure edge moves with its movement according to the correct view. And if one end of his turban becomes impure, he throws it away and keeps the pure on his head and the impure does not move with his movement, his prayer is permissible; if it moves, it is not permissible. And the one who lacks something to remove impurity prays with it, and there is no repetition upon him, nor upon the one who lacks something to cover his private parts, even if it is silk, grass, mud, or tree leaves. Felt: meant by it everything that has a thick body suitable to be split into two halves like a stone, brick, or mat. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 237] 'Impure' is general and includes if the impurity is preventing or not preventing; if the impurity is not preventing, it is pure; if it is preventing, then due to its thickness it is like two garments. 'Stitched' (mudrib): meant by it what has its sides sewn and its middle sewn as a double layer. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 237] According to the correct view: He said in al-Bahr: If he prays on a mat and on one side of it there is impurity, the most correct is that it is permissible whether it is large or small; because it is like the ground, so it does not become a user of impurity, and it is a fortiori; because if impurity does not prevent at the place of the knees and hands, then here it is more fitting. And in al-Khulasa: If he spreads a thin mat over the impure place and prays on it, if the mat is such that it is suitable to cover the private parts, i.e., it does not show what is beneath, the prayer is permissible. And if [the impurity] is wet and he throws a garment on it and prays, if it is a garment that can be made from its width a garment, it is permissible according to Muhammad; if it cannot, it is not permissible. Similarly, if he throws a felt on it and prays on it, it is permissible. Al-Halwani said: It is not permissible until he throws the other edge on this edge, making it like two garments. And if the impurity is dry, it is permissible, meaning if it is suitable as a cover. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/529] It is not permissible: because what is considered in the garment is the carrying, and he is the carrier legally. [Maraqi al-Falah: 238] 'And the one who lacks something to remove etc.' i.e., the one who does not have something to remove the impurity with, from water, liquid, or earth, he is not obligated to wash the impurity, but rather he prays with it. Then when he finds the remover, he is not obligated to repeat what he prayed with it even if the time remains, because Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity. 'Nor upon the one who lacks etc.' i.e., there is no obligation to repeat the prayer upon the one who lacks something to cover his private parts, even if the cover is silk or other as mentioned. It indicates that if he finds silk and does not find other, he must pray in it, because he is afflicted with two trials: uncovering the private parts and the prohibition of wearing silk, and the obligation of covering is stronger than the prohibition of wearing it in this case, and there is no sin upon him, and he sins when he is able to get other while the prayer is valid. Then if he finds it even by permission (ibaha) and a quarter of it is pure, his prayer is not valid while naked, and he is given a choice if less than a quarter is pure, and his prayer in a completely impure garment is more beloved than his prayer naked. And if he finds what covers part of the private parts, he must use it and cover the front and back; if it covers only one of them, it is said: 'Then if he finds it etc.' i.e., if a praying person finds a garment whose quarter is pure and prays naked, his prayer is not valid, even if someone made that garment permissible (ibaha) for him and did not own it to him. The restriction by 'finds' is because if he does not find it, his prayer is valid while naked, and he is not obligated to repeat it nor delay it from the time. He said in al-Bahr: It is appropriate that he must repeat in our view if the inability is due to prevention by people, as if his garment was usurped; because they stated in the chapter of tayammum that prevention from water if it is from people necessitates repetition. And with the purity of the quarter: if its quarter is not pure but less than a quarter, he has a choice between praying naked or covering his private parts as will come later; and if more than a quarter is pure, the ruling of invalidity of his prayer applies a fortiori. And his saying: 'even by permission' means someone gave him a garment not by way of ownership but for use, for example. If someone gave him by way of ownership, the ruling of impermissibility applies a fortiori. Know that the difference between permission (ibaha) and ownership (tamlik) is that the permitted person may only use that thing, and it does not enter his ownership; the owned person enters the thing into his ownership. An example of permission is food of hospitality: it is permissible for the guests to eat it, but it is not permissible to give it to anyone because they do not own it and the host did not make them owners; and it is not permissible to take some of it and return to his house without permission from the host; if he does, he sins. An example of ownership is zakat money: it is permissible for the poor person to dispose of it as owners do in terms of sale, gift, lease, etc. 'Even by permission': if it is not permitted to him, his ability over it is not established, so he prays naked, because using the property of another without a legal justification is not permissible. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 238] 'His prayer is not valid etc.' It is not hidden that its place is when he does not find what removes the impurity nor what reduces it; if he finds in both cases, he must use it, contrary to if he finds water sufficient for some limbs of ablution, then he performs tayammum and is not obligated to use it. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/539] 'And he is given a choice if it is pure etc.' Its summary: he has a choice between praying in it, which is best, and praying naked while sitting with gestures for bowing and prostration, which comes next in merit, because it covers the major private parts; or standing naked with bowing and prostration, which is inferior to them; or with gestures, which is inferior to these. The apparent meaning of al-Hidayah prohibits it, as he said regarding the one who does not find a garment: if he prays standing, it suffices him, because sitting covers the thick private parts, and standing performs these pillars, so he inclines to whichever he wishes. Al-Zayla'i said: If gestures were permissible while standing, this statement would not be sound. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 239] 'Completely impure' is genitive as an adjective for garment, for the addition is verbal. It was said: He said in al-Nahr: The apparent is that the difference is in priority. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 242]
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school on conditions of prayer related to impurity and covering. It begins by stating permissible cases: prayer on a thick object (libad) with a clean surface and impure underside is valid because the thickness separates the worshiper from the impurity, treating it like two distinct layers. Similarly, a garment with a clean exterior and impure lining is permissible if the lining is not sewn as a separate layer (ghayr mudrib), meaning the garment is not double-layered. For a turban with one impure end, if the impure part is removed and the clean part remains on the head without causing the impurity to move, prayer is valid; if the impure part moves due to the worshiper's movement, it invalidates because contact with impurity is considered. The passage then addresses the one who lacks means to remove impurity (water, liquid, earth) or cover his private parts: such a person prays in that state and does not repeat the prayer even if the means become available later, based on the principle that Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity. If a person finds silk and no other cover, he must pray in it, as covering the private parts takes precedence over the prohibition of wearing silk. The commentary elaborates on the definitions of libad and mudrib, and provides a detailed discussion on the ruling of praying on a thin mat over impurity, noting the ikhtilaf between Muhammad al-Shaybani and al-Halwani. Then it discusses cases of finding a garment with some clean portion: if at least a quarter is clean, one must wear it and cannot pray naked; if less than a quarter is clean, one has a choice between praying in it (preferred) or praying naked with gestures; if the garment is entirely impure, praying in it is preferable to praying naked. The text also distinguishes between permission (ibaha) and ownership (tamlik), explaining that if a garment is made available through permission, it is considered as found, but if not permitted, one cannot use it and prays naked. The commentary further notes that the prohibition of wearing silk is overridden by the necessity of covering the private parts in the absence of other options.

Key Terms
لبد (libad): A thick object (like felt, stone, brick, or mat) that can be split into two halves, used as a barrier between the worshiper and impurity.
مضرب (mudrib): A garment whose sides and middle are sewn, making it a double layer; prayer on a garment with a dirty lining is not permissible if it is mudrib because the impurity effectively contacts the worshiper.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person prays on a thick felt mat (libad) whose upper surface is pure but the lower surface is impure, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The prayer is invalid because the felt is impure.
B) The prayer is valid because the upper surface is pure and the thickness separates the worshiper from the impurity.
C) The prayer is valid only if the felt is sewn like a double-layer garment.
D) The prayer is makruh but still valid.

Key Takeaway
Thickness or double-layering separates the worshiper from impurity; movement of impurity invalidates contact.

Salah — Prayer

Exposing a Quarter of a Limb Invalidates Prayer
Ruling on exposure of quarter of an awrah limb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exposure of the 'awrah in prayer and apply the rules of quarter measure, scattered exposure, and time duration to determine validity.

Core Idea
Exposure of a quarter of an 'awrah limb for the duration of a pillar invalidates prayer; scattered exposure is totalled against the smallest limb.

Covering the 'awrah is a condition for the validity of prayer. However, not every exposure invalidates the prayer. The Hanafi school has precise measures: only exposure of a quarter of a limb that lasts for the duration of one pillar (rukn) renders the prayer invalid. Furthermore, if exposure is scattered across multiple limbs, the total exposed area is compared to the smallest exposed limb. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is exposing a quarter of a limb of the 'awrah during prayer. The ruling is that the prayer is invalidated (batil) if the exposure lasts for the duration of performing one pillar.
2
Understand the quarter measure
The exposure must amount to one quarter (rub') of a single limb from the 'awrah. If less than a quarter, it does not invalidate.
Limbs are counted individually; e.g., arm, thigh, etc.
3
Apply the scattered exposure rule
If the exposure is spread across multiple limbs (e.g., part of arm and part of stomach), the total exposed area is summed. The sum is compared to the smallest limb that was exposed. If the sum equals or exceeds a quarter of that smallest limb, it invalidates; otherwise not.
The smallest limb is used as the benchmark.
4
Incorporate the time duration requirement
The exposure must last for the duration of performing one pillar (rukn), such as the time for one prostration or one ruku'. Brief exposure of less than that does not invalidate, due to necessity (darura).
Imam Abu Yusuf measures by actual time of the pillar; Imam Muhammad by estimated time. The mufta bihi is Abu Yusuf's view.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and the mufta bihi
Abu Yusuf holds that the measure is the actual performance time, while Muhammad holds it is the estimated duration. The relied-upon position is Abu Yusuf's, as preferred by later authorities like Maraqi al-Falah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكشف ربع عضو من مبتدأ أعضاء العورة يمنع صحة الصلاة، ولو تفرق الانكشاف على أعضاء من العورة، وكان جملة ما تفرق يبلغ ربع أصغر الأعضاء المنكشفة منع، وإلا فلا.

[commentary] أطلق الكشف، وهو مقيد بما إذا كان قدر أداء ركن للاحتياط. أبي يوسف يحظه، ومحمد محله اعتبار أداء الركن حقيقة والمختار قول أبي يوسف عند [page break] جملة ما تفرق يبلغ ربع أصغر الأعضاء المنكشفة منع، وإلا فلا أطلق المنع، وهو مقيد بما إذا طال زمن الانكشاف بقدر أداء ركن [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٤٣] وإلا فلا أي وإن لم يبلغ ربع أصغرها أو بلغ ولم يطل زمن الانكشاف فلا يمنع الصحة للضرورة، سواءً الغني والفقير. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٤٣]
Exposing a quarter of a limb from the beginning of the limbs of the awrah prevents the validity of prayer. If the exposure is scattered across limbs of the awrah, and the total of what is scattered amounts to a quarter of the smallest exposed limb, it prevents [validity]; otherwise not.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: if a person exposes a quarter (rub') of any single limb that is part of the awrah, the prayer becomes invalid. However, if the exposure is spread across multiple limbs (e.g., part of the thigh, part of the stomach), the total exposed area is measured against the smallest limb that was exposed. If the sum equals a quarter of that smallest limb, the prayer is invalid; otherwise not. The commentary specifies that this measure is tied to the duration of performing one pillar (rukn), such as the time needed for one prostration. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, the measure is the actual time of the pillar; according to Imam Muhammad, it is the duration needed to perform it. The chosen (muhtar) view is that of Abu Yusuf. Additionally, the ruling is limited to cases where the exposure lasts for the length of one pillar; if it is shorter, the prayer remains valid due to necessity (darura). This applies equally to rich and poor.

Key Terms
ربع العضو (rub' al-'udw): One quarter of a limb of the body that is part of the awrah.
التفرق في الانكشاف (al-tafriq fi al-inkishaf): Exposure that is scattered across multiple limbs of the awrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does scattered exposure of the 'awrah invalidate the prayer?
A) When the total exceeds half of the largest limb
B) When the total equals a quarter of the smallest exposed limb and lasts for the duration of one pillar
C) When any part of the 'awrah is exposed regardless of amount or time
D) Only when a full limb is exposed

Key Takeaway
Exposure of a quarter of an 'awrah limb for the duration of one pillar invalidates the prayer; scattered exposure is measured against the smallest limb.

Qiblah for the Incapacitated and Uncertain
Rulings on facing qiblah when unable or uncertain

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for facing qiblah when incapacitated or uncertain, and apply the conditions for performing taharri.

Core Idea
Facing qiblah is wajib; if impossible, face your direction of ability; if uncertain, investigate.

This passage from Nur al-Idah addresses two key exceptions to the general obligation of facing the qiblah: physical incapacity or fear, and uncertainty about the direction. The author explains that the requirement adapts to the person's capacity and safety, while for uncertainty, a specific investigation (taharri) is mandated. Understanding these rulings protects the validity of one's prayer in challenging circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of exception
The text first addresses those who cannot face qiblah due to illness, inability to dismount, or fear of enemy/drowning. Second, it addresses those who are uncertain of the qiblah direction.
These are two distinct situations with different rules.
2
Determine the ruling for each category
For the incapacitated/fearful, the qiblah is whatever direction they can face safely. For the uncertain, they must perform taharri (investigation) if no reliable source exists.
Taharri is an active effort, not guessing.
3
Understand the conditions for taharri
Taharri is only required when there is genuine uncertainty and no informant (knowledgeable person) or correctly placed mihrab exists. If either is available, taharri is not allowed.
The mihrab is considered authoritative in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Analyze the consequences of praying without taharri
If one prays without taharri and later discovers he was correct, his prayer is valid; otherwise, he must repeat. This exception only applies if he had no way to determine the qiblah.
This differs from the general rule that intention substitutes for certainty in some cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن عجز عن استقبال القبلة لمرض أو عجز عن النزول عن دابته أو خاف عدوا، أو خشية غرق فقبلته جهة قدرته وأمنه

[commentary] أطلق الخوف، فشمل ما إذا خاف على نفسه أو على دابته أو على ماله أو على أمانته [مراقي الفلاح ٢٤٣] عدوا أطلق العدو، فشمل ما إذا كان آدميا أو سبعا جهة قدرته إلخ فيه لف ونشر مرتب، فقبلة العاجز جهة القدرة، وقبلة الخائف جهة الأمن، حتى أنه لو خاف أن يراه العدو إن قعد صلى مضطجعاً بالإيماء إلى جهة أمنه.

ومن اشتبهت عليه القبلة و لم يكن عنده مخبر ولا محراب تحرى، أو سأله فلم يخبره ماض من التحري

[commentary] أي إذا عجز عن تعرف القبلة بأن انطمست أعلامها وتراكم الظلام وتضام الغمام لزمه التحري، وهو بذل المجهود لنيل المقصود قيد بالاشتباه؛ لأنه لو صلى في الصحراء إلى جهة من غير شك ولا تحر، إن تبين أنه أصاب أو كان أكبر رأيه أو لم يظهر من حاله شيء حتى ذهب عن الموضع فصلاته جائزة، وإن تبين أنه أخطأ أو كان أكبر رأيه فعليه الإعادة. وقيد بقوله: "ولم يكن إلخ" فأفاد أنه لو قدر على تعرف القبلة بسؤال لا يجوز التحري، وأراد بالمخبر من هو من أهل المكان أو من له علم، وقيد بقوله : ولا محراب، فإنه لا يجوز التحري مع وضع المحاريب؛ لأن وضعها في الأصل بحق، وقيد بالتحري؛ لأن من صلى ممن اشتبهت عليه بلا تحر فعليه الإعادة، إلا إن علم بعد الفراغ أنه أصاب؛ لأن ما افترض بغيره يشترط حصوله لا تحصيله.
Whoever is unable to face the qiblah due to illness, or inability to dismount from his animal, or fears an enemy, or fear of drowning, then his qiblah is the direction of his ability and safety. Whoever is uncertain of the qiblah and has no informant and no mihrab, he performs taharri (investigation). If he asks and is not informed, he proceeds with taharri.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage addresses two situations regarding the obligation of facing the qiblah. First, for those who are physically unable (ill, cannot dismount) or in fear (enemy, drowning), the direction of prayer is determined by their ability or safety. The fear includes fear for one's life, property, or even one's mount. If a person fears that the enemy will see him if he sits, he may pray lying down with gestures towards his safe direction. Second, if the qiblah is unknown (e.g., landmarks obscured, darkness, clouds), the person must perform taharri, which means exerting effort to determine the correct direction. This is required only if there is genuine uncertainty; if a person prays in the desert without any doubt or investigation, and later it becomes clear that he was correct, or he has a strong opinion, his prayer is valid; but if he was wrong, he must repeat. Taharri is not allowed if one can ask a knowledgeable person or if there is a properly placed mihrab. The condition of taharri is that the person must actually investigate; if he prays without it, he must repeat unless he later learns he was correct.

Key Terms
التحري (al-taharri): Exerting effort to determine the correct direction of the qiblah when it is unknown.
المحراب (al-mihrab): A niche in a mosque indicating the direction of the qiblah, installed correctly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a person do if the qiblah becomes uncertain and there is no available informant or mihrab?
A) Pray in any direction without investigation
B) Perform taharri (investigation) to determine the closest direction
C) Delay the prayer until the qiblah becomes clear
D) Face the direction of the nearest mosque

Key Takeaway
Facing qiblah is wajib but adapts to necessity: incapacitated/fearful face direction of ability/safety; uncertain must perform taharri, unless a reliable guide exists.

Conditions for Invalidity Due to Uncovered 'Awrah
Ruling on the minimum uncovered area that invalidates prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which uncovered 'awrah invalidates prayer and apply the Hanafi measurement rules for exposure spread over multiple limbs.

Core Idea
Exposure of 'awrah only invalidates prayer if it reaches one-quarter of the smallest limb and lasts for at least one pillar.

This passage from Nur al-Idah details the precise conditions under which uncovered 'awrah invalidates prayer. The Hanafi school uses a proportional measurement: if exposure is spread over several limbs, its total area matters relative to the smallest limb. The passage also clarifies what counts as a limb and adds a duration requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
The passage states that the 'awrah prevents the validity of prayer. This is the default principle.
The prevention is conditional on several factors.
2
Determine the measurement rule for spread exposure
If exposure is spread over multiple limbs, the total uncovered area must reach a quarter of the smallest exposed limb to invalidate.
This is the 'tfarruq al-inkishaf' rule.
3
Understand what constitutes a limb
The text defines 'limbs' for measurement: e.g., knee+thigh, ankle+shin, ear alone, etc. These definitions affect the threshold calculation.
For example, the knee and thigh together count as one limb.
4
Apply the duration condition
The exposure must last for the time it takes to perform one pillar (e.g., a rukn like bowing). Brief exposure is excused.
This is from the later commentary: 'إذا طال زمن الانكشاف بقدر أداء ركن'.
5
Recognize the exception for no covering
If no lawful covering is available at all, or only an impure one, exposure does not invalidate even if the area and duration conditions are met.
This exception applies to both rich and poor equally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة ٨٣ متعلقات شروط الصلاة العورة يمنع صحة الصلاة، ولو تفرق الانكشاف على أعضاء من العورة، وكان [؟] جملة ما تفرق يبلغ ربع أصغر الأعضاء المنكشفة منع، وإلا فلا، العورة فشمل ما إذا كانت العورة غليظة أو خفيفة من الرجل أو المرأة، وأردنا بالغليظة القبل والدبر وما حولها، والخفيفة ماعدا ذلك، وهذا التقسيم بالنظر إلى النظر، وإلا فالحكم في الصلاة واحد يمنع إلخ والمنع مقيد بما إذا وجد الساتر لا ما دون ربعه، فإنه إن لم يجد الساتر أصلاً أو وجد لكنه ليس بطاهر إلا أقل من الربع، فلا يمنع صحة الصلاة، واعلم أن الركبة مع الفخذ عضو واحد في الأصح، وكعب المرأة مع ساقها، وأذنها بانفرادها عن رأسها، وثديها المنكسر، فإن كانت ناهداً فهو تبع لصدرها، والذكر بانفراده، والأنثيين بلا ضمهما إليه في الصحيح، وما بين السرة والعانة عضو كامل بجوانب البدن وكل ألية عورة والدبر ثالثهما في الصحيح. تفرق الانكشاف كانكشاف شيء من فرج المرأة، وشيء من ظهرها، وشيء من فخذها، وشيء من ساقها حيث يجمع لمنع جواز الصلاة، لأن المانع في العورة انكشاف القدر المانع البحر الرائق: ٥٣٧/١] منع: أطلق المنع، وهو مقيد بما إذا طال زمن الانكشاف بقدر أداء ركن [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٤٣] وإلا فلا أي وإن لم يبلغ ربع أصغرها أو بلغ ولم يطل زمن الانكشاف فلا يمنع الصحة للضرورة، سواءً الغني والفقير. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٤٣]
Book of Prayer. 83. Matters related to conditions of prayer. The 'awrah prevents the validity of prayer, and if the exposure is spread over limbs of the 'awrah, and the total of what is spread reaches a quarter of the smallest uncovered limbs, it prevents; otherwise not. The 'awrah: it includes whether the 'awrah is thick or thin, for man or woman. By thick we mean the front and back private parts and what surrounds them; thin: everything else. This division is with respect to looking, otherwise the ruling in prayer is one: it prevents, etc. The prevention is conditioned upon the existence of a covering, not less than its quarter. If he does not find a covering at all, or he finds one but it is not pure except less than a quarter, then it does not prevent the validity of prayer. Know that the knee with the thigh is one limb in the most correct view, and the woman's ankle with her shin, her ear alone apart from her head, her hanging breast—if it is protruding it is part of her chest—the penis alone, the testicles without attaching them to it in the correct view, and what is between the navel and the pubis is a complete limb with the sides of the body, and every buttock is 'awrah, and the anus is the third of them in the correct view. The spread of exposure is like the exposure of something from the woman's vagina, something from her back, something from her thigh, something from her leg, which combine to prevent the permissibility of prayer; because the obstacle in 'awrah is the exposure of the amount that prevents. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 537/1. Prevent: He gave absolute prevention, and it is restricted to when the duration of exposure lasts for the time of performing a pillar. [Maraqi al-Falah: 243] And otherwise, i.e., if it does not reach a quarter of the smallest limb, or it reaches but the duration of exposure does not last, it does not prevent validity due to necessity, whether rich or poor. [Maraqi al-Falah: 243]
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the conditions for the invalidity of prayer due to uncovered 'awrah. The matn states that the 'awrah prevents validity of prayer. If exposure is spread over multiple limbs, the total must be at least a quarter of the smallest exposed limb to invalidate. The commentary clarifies that this is conditioned on the availability of a lawful covering; if none exists or only an impure one is available, the prayer remains valid. It also defines what constitutes a 'limb' for this measurement: the knee and thigh are one limb, a woman's ankle and shin are one, etc. Additionally, the exposure must last for the duration of at least one pillar (e.g., a rukn). If the uncovered area is less than a quarter or the exposure is brief, the prayer is valid due to necessity, and this applies equally to rich and poor.

Key Terms
العورة (al-'awrah): The parts of the body that must be covered in prayer.
تفرق الانكشاف (tafarruq al-inkishāf): Exposure spread over multiple limbs.
ربع أصغر الأعضاء (rub' aṣghar al-aʿḍā’): One quarter of the smallest limb among those exposed.
عضو (ʿuḍw): A limb; the text defines specific limbs for the purpose of measuring exposure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which condition is NOT required for the invalidity of prayer due to uncovered 'awrah?
A) The uncovered area must be at least a quarter of the smallest limb.
B) The exposure must last for the duration of a pillar.
C) The person must be wealthy.
D) The exposure must be of the actual 'awrah.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi law measures exposure of 'awrah by a proportional rule (quarter of smallest limb) and a duration rule (at least one pillar), with an exception for necessity.
