Facing Qibla for Those Unable: Direction of Ability and Safety
Ruling on facing qibla for those with valid excuses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the qibla direction for a person who is unable to face the Ka'ba due to illness, fear, or other valid excuses.

Core Idea
When you cannot face the Ka'ba, face the direction of your ability and safety.

The obligation to face the qibla is a condition for the validity of prayer. However, the Hanafi school recognizes that circumstances can make it impossible. This lesson explains what such a person must do: their qibla becomes the direction of their ability (e.g., where they can turn) or safety (away from danger).

Guided Path
1
Identify the excuses
List the excuses mentioned: sickness, inability to dismount from an animal, fear of an enemy, and fear of drowning. Note that 'fear' includes fear for self, animal, property, or trust.
2
State the general ruling
The qibla for such a person is the direction of their ability or safety. This is not arbitrary; they must face a direction they are capable of or that is safe.
3
Understand the two categories
The text uses 'laf wa nashr' (twist and spread): the incapable face direction of ability; the fearful face direction of safety. They are not the same.
E.g., a sick person may face their ability; a person fearing enemy may face away from the enemy even if that is not towards Mecca.
4
Apply the extreme case
If a person fears being seen by the enemy while sitting, he may pray lying down, gesturing toward his direction of safety. This shows the flexibility of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن عجز عن التي انكشف بعضها استقبال القبلة لمرض أو عجز عن النزول عن دابته أو خاف عدوا، فقبلته جهة أو خشية غرق قدرته وأمنه ومن اشتبهت عليه القبلة و لم يكن عنده مخبر ولا محراب تحرى، أو سأله فلم يخبره ماض من التحري أو خاف إلخ : أطلق الخوف، فشمل ما إذا خاف على نفسه أو على دابته أو على ماله أو على أمانته [مراقي الفلاح ٢٤٣] عدوا أطلق العدو، فشمل ما إذا كان آدميا أو سبعا جهة قدرته إلخ فيه لف ونشر ،مرتب، فقبلة العاجز جهة ،القدرة، وقبلة الخائف جهة الأمن، حتى أنه لو خاف أن يراه العدو إن قعد صلى مضطجعاً بالإيماء إلى جهة أمنه. ومن اشتبهت إلخ أي إذا عجز عن تعرف القبلة بأن انطمست أعلامها وتراكم الظلام وتضام الغمام لزمه التحري، وهو بذل المجهود لنيل المقصود قيد بالاشتباه؛ لأنه لو صلى في الصحراء إلى جهة من غير شك ولا تحر، إن تبين أنه أصاب أو كان أكبر رأيه أو لم يظهر من حاله شيء حتى ذهب عن الموضع فصلاته جائزة، وإن تبين أنه أخطأ أو كان أكبر رأيه فعليه الإعادة. 11 وقيد بقوله: "ولم يكن إلخ" فأفاد أنه لو قدر على تعرف القبلة بسؤال لا يجوز التحري، وأراد بالمخبر من هو من أهل المكان أو من له علم، وقيد بقوله : ولا محراب، فإنه لا يجوز التحري مع وضع المحاريب؛ لأن وضعها في الأصل بحق، وقيد بالتحري؛ لأن من صلى ممن اشتبهت عليه بلا تحر فعليه الإعادة، إلا إن علم بعد الفراغ أنه أصاب؛ لأن ما افترض بغيره يشترط حصوله لا تحصيله. ولا إعادة عليه لو أخطأ، وإن علم بخطئه في صلاته استدار وبنى، وإن شرع بلا تحرّ أو تبدل اجتهاده فعلم بعد فراغه أنه أصاب صحت وإن علم بإصابته فيها فسدت كما لو لم يعلم أي من الصلاة ولو بغالب الظن إصابته أصلا، ولو تحرى قوم جهات وجهلوا حال إمامهم تجزئهم. لو أخطأ: أي علم بعد فراغه أنه أخطأ. استدار أي من جهة اليمين لا اليسار. (مراقي الفلاح وبني لفظة ماض البناء أي بني على ما أداه بالتحري. مراقي الفلاح (٢٤٥] فسدت لأن أول صلاته كان مبنياً على ضعف، وهو التحري، وآخر صلاته صار مبنياً على قوة وهي حالة العلم، فلزم بناء القوي على الضعيف وهو لا يجوز، بخلاف الأول فإن الابتداء كالانتهاء. ولو :تحرى أي تحرى جماعة من الناس في ليلة مظلمة، فصلى إمامهم إلى جهة، وصلى كل واحد من المأمورين إلى جهة، ولا يدرون ما صنع الإمام يجزئهم إذا كانوا خلف الإمام؛ لأن كل واحد منهم متوجه إلى القبلة، وهي جهة التحري، وهذه المخالفة لا تمنع كما في جوف الكعبة، ومن علم منهم حال إمامه، تفسد صلاته؛ لاعتقاده أن إمامه على الخطأ، وكذا إذا كان متقدماً عليه؛ لتركه فرض المقام. [تبيين الحقائق: ٢٦٩/١]
And whoever is unable to face the qibla due to sickness or inability to dismount from his animal or fears an enemy, his qibla is the direction of his ability and safety, and whoever is in doubt about the qibla and has no informant or mihrab, he performs tahari, and if he asks and is not informed, he acts upon his tahari. 'Or fears' etc.: He made fear absolute, so it includes if he fears for himself, his animal, his money, or his trust. [Maraqi al-Falah: 243] 'Enemy': He made it absolute, so it includes whether human or beast. 'Direction of his ability' etc.: it is a [laf wa nashr] arranged. So the qibla of the incapable is the direction of ability, and the qibla of the fearful is the direction of safety. So much so that if he fears the enemy seeing him if he sits, he prays lying down, gesturing toward his direction of safety. 'And whoever is in doubt' etc.: i.e., if he is unable to know the qibla because its signs are obliterated, darkness accumulates, and clouds cover, it is necessary for him to perform tahari, which is exerting effort to obtain the goal. He restricted it with doubt; because if he prays in the desert toward a direction without doubt or tahari, if it becomes apparent that he was correct or his predominant opinion was correct, or nothing appears from his condition until he leaves the place, his prayer is valid. But if it becomes apparent that he was wrong or his predominant opinion was wrong, then he must repeat. 11 And he restricted with his saying: 'and he has no informant' so it gives that if he is able to know the qibla by asking, tahari is not allowed. And by 'informant' he means one who is from the people of the place or has knowledge. And he restricted with his saying: 'nor mihrab', so tahari is not allowed when there are mihrabs, because their placement is originally based on truth. And he restricted with tahari; because if one who is in doubt prays without tahari, he must repeat unless he knows after completion that he was correct, because what is assumed by others, obtaining it is required, not its acquisition. There is no repetition upon him if he is wrong. And if he knows his mistake during his prayer, he turns and builds [upon his prior acts]. And if he starts without tahari or his ijtihad changes, and he knows after completion that he was correct, it is valid. But if he knows his correctness during it, it becomes invalid, just as if he did not know he was correct at all, even if by predominant opinion. And if a group of people perform tahari in different directions and are ignorant of their imam's state, it suffices them. 'If he is wrong': i.e., he knows after completion that he was wrong. 'He turns': i.e., to the right, not the left. (Maraqi al-Falah] 'And he builds': the word is past tense meaning he builds upon what he performed with tahari. Maraqui al-Falah: 245) 'It becomes invalid': because the beginning of his prayer was based on weakness, i.e., tahari, and the end became based on strength, i.e., the state of knowledge, so building the strong upon the weak is not permissible, contrary to the first case because the beginning is like the end. 'And if they perform tahari': i.e., a group of people in a dark night, their imam prays toward one direction, and each of the followers prays toward a direction, and they do not know what the imam did, it suffices them if they are behind the imam; because each of them is facing the qibla, i.e., the direction of tahari, and this disagreement does not prevent, like inside the Kaaba. And whoever knows the state of his imam, his prayer is invalid because he believes his imam is in error, and similarly if he is ahead of him, because he abandons the obligation of standing. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 269/1]
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct rulings: facing the qibla for those with an excuse, and the procedure of tahari when the qibla is unknown. For the first, those unable to face qibla due to sickness, fear of an enemy, inability to dismount, or fear of drowning face the direction of their ability and safety. The 'fear' is general, including fear for self, animal, or property. For the second, when the qibla is unknown due to darkness or clouds, one must perform tahari (exert effort to determine the direction). Tahari is not allowed if one can ask a knowledgeable person or if there is a mihrab. If one prays without tahari, the prayer is valid only if it turns out they were correct; otherwise, they must repeat. If during prayer they realize they are facing the wrong direction, they turn to the correct one and continue. The commentary also discusses a scenario where a group prays behind an imam, each follower has performed tahari in a different direction, and they do not know the imam's direction—their prayer is valid because each is doing tahari. But if a follower knows the imam is wrong, the follower's prayer becomes invalid.

Key Terms
قبلة (qibla): The direction of the Ka'ba in Mecca.
استقبال القبلة (istiqbāl al-qibla): Facing the qibla during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should a person who fears an enemy do regarding qibla?
A) Face the direction of the enemy to show bravery.
B) Face the direction of safety away from the enemy.
C) Face any direction because fear overrides the obligation.
D) Wait until the enemy is gone then pray.

Key Takeaway
When unable to face the Ka'ba due to a valid excuse, the direction of ability or safety replaces the exact qibla.

Tahari: Determining the Qibla When Unknown
Ruling on tahari when qibla is unknown

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules of tahari to determine the qibla when its direction is unknown, and evaluate the validity of prayers based on tahari.

Core Idea
When you cannot know the qibla, you must perform tahari; your prayer is valid if you were correct, but you must repeat if you were wrong.

When the qibla is unknown due to darkness, clouds, or lost signs, the Hanafi school requires one to exert effort (tahari) to determine the direction. This lesson details the conditions for tahari, the validity of prayer based on tahari, and special scenarios involving groups and corrections during prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify when tahari is wajib
Tahari becomes wajib when the qibla is unknown and there is no informant (someone who knows) or mihrab, and one cannot ask. The text mentions 'signs obliterated, darkness, clouds'.
If a mihrab exists, it indicates the correct direction, so tahari is not allowed.
2
Define tahari
Tahari is exerting effort (bazl al-majhud) to reach the goal (of determining qibla). It is an intellectual effort, not guesswork.
3
Understand validity without tahari
If one prays without tahari (e.g., guesses), the prayer is only valid if it later turns out they were correct. Otherwise, they must repeat. The text states 'because what is assumed by others requires obtaining it, not its acquisition'.
4
Learn the correction scenarios
If during prayer one realizes they are wrong, they turn (to the right) and continue. If they become certain of the correct direction during prayer, the prayer becomes invalid because they built the strong (certainty) on weak (tahari). If after completion they learn they were correct, it is valid.
5
Examine the group prayer scenario
If followers each perform tahari in different directions and do not know the imam's direction, their prayer is valid. But if a follower knows the imam is wrong, his prayer invalid.
This is analogous to praying inside the Kaaba where directions differ but all are valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن عجز عن التي انكشف بعضها استقبال القبلة لمرض أو عجز عن النزول عن دابته أو خاف عدوا، فقبلته جهة أو خشية غرق قدرته وأمنه ومن اشتبهت عليه القبلة و لم يكن عنده مخبر ولا محراب تحرى، أو سأله فلم يخبره ماض من التحري أو خاف إلخ : أطلق الخوف، فشمل ما إذا خاف على نفسه أو على دابته أو على ماله أو على أمانته [مراقي الفلاح ٢٤٣] عدوا أطلق العدو، فشمل ما إذا كان آدميا أو سبعا جهة قدرته إلخ فيه لف ونشر ،مرتب، فقبلة العاجز جهة ،القدرة، وقبلة الخائف جهة الأمن، حتى أنه لو خاف أن يراه العدو إن قعد صلى مضطجعاً بالإيماء إلى جهة أمنه. ومن اشتبهت إلخ أي إذا عجز عن تعرف القبلة بأن انطمست أعلامها وتراكم الظلام وتضام الغمام لزمه التحري، وهو بذل المجهود لنيل المقصود قيد بالاشتباه؛ لأنه لو صلى في الصحراء إلى جهة من غير شك ولا تحر، إن تبين أنه أصاب أو كان أكبر رأيه أو لم يظهر من حاله شيء حتى ذهب عن الموضع فصلاته جائزة، وإن تبين أنه أخطأ أو كان أكبر رأيه فعليه الإعادة. 11 وقيد بقوله: "ولم يكن إلخ" فأفاد أنه لو قدر على تعرف القبلة بسؤال لا يجوز التحري، وأراد بالمخبر من هو من أهل المكان أو من له علم، وقيد بقوله : ولا محراب، فإنه لا يجوز التحري مع وضع المحاريب؛ لأن وضعها في الأصل بحق، وقيد بالتحري؛ لأن من صلى ممن اشتبهت عليه بلا تحر فعليه الإعادة، إلا إن علم بعد الفراغ أنه أصاب؛ لأن ما افترض بغيره يشترط حصوله لا تحصيله. ولا إعادة عليه لو أخطأ، وإن علم بخطئه في صلاته استدار وبنى، وإن شرع بلا تحرّ أو تبدل اجتهاده فعلم بعد فراغه أنه أصاب صحت وإن علم بإصابته فيها فسدت كما لو لم يعلم أي من الصلاة ولو بغالب الظن إصابته أصلا، ولو تحرى قوم جهات وجهلوا حال إمامهم تجزئهم. لو أخطأ: أي علم بعد فراغه أنه أخطأ. استدار أي من جهة اليمين لا اليسار. (مراقي الفلاح وبني لفظة ماض البناء أي بني على ما أداه بالتحري. مراقي الفلاح (٢٤٥] فسدت لأن أول صلاته كان مبنياً على ضعف، وهو التحري، وآخر صلاته صار مبنياً على قوة وهي حالة العلم، فلزم بناء القوي على الضعيف وهو لا يجوز، بخلاف الأول فإن الابتداء كالانتهاء. ولو :تحرى أي تحرى جماعة من الناس في ليلة مظلمة، فصلى إمامهم إلى جهة، وصلى كل واحد من المأمورين إلى جهة، ولا يدرون ما صنع الإمام يجزئهم إذا كانوا خلف الإمام؛ لأن كل واحد منهم متوجه إلى القبلة، وهي جهة التحري، وهذه المخالفة لا تمنع كما في جوف الكعبة، ومن علم منهم حال إمامه، تفسد صلاته؛ لاعتقاده أن إمامه على الخطأ، وكذا إذا كان متقدماً عليه؛ لتركه فرض المقام. [تبيين الحقائق: ٢٦٩/١]
And whoever is unable to face the qibla due to sickness or inability to dismount from his animal or fears an enemy, his qibla is the direction of his ability and safety, and whoever is in doubt about the qibla and has no informant or mihrab, he performs tahari, and if he asks and is not informed, he acts upon his tahari. 'Or fears' etc.: He made fear absolute, so it includes if he fears for himself, his animal, his money, or his trust. [Maraqi al-Falah: 243] 'Enemy': He made it absolute, so it includes whether human or beast. 'Direction of his ability' etc.: it is a [laf wa nashr] arranged. So the qibla of the incapable is the direction of ability, and the qibla of the fearful is the direction of safety. So much so that if he fears the enemy seeing him if he sits, he prays lying down, gesturing toward his direction of safety. 'And whoever is in doubt' etc.: i.e., if he is unable to know the qibla because its signs are obliterated, darkness accumulates, and clouds cover, it is necessary for him to perform tahari, which is exerting effort to obtain the goal. He restricted it with doubt; because if he prays in the desert toward a direction without doubt or tahari, if it becomes apparent that he was correct or his predominant opinion was correct, or nothing appears from his condition until he leaves the place, his prayer is valid. But if it becomes apparent that he was wrong or his predominant opinion was wrong, then he must repeat. 11 And he restricted with his saying: 'and he has no informant' so it gives that if he is able to know the qibla by asking, tahari is not allowed. And by 'informant' he means one who is from the people of the place or has knowledge. And he restricted with his saying: 'nor mihrab', so tahari is not allowed when there are mihrabs, because their placement is originally based on truth. And he restricted with tahari; because if one who is in doubt prays without tahari, he must repeat unless he knows after completion that he was correct, because what is assumed by others, obtaining it is required, not its acquisition. There is no repetition upon him if he is wrong. And if he knows his mistake during his prayer, he turns and builds [upon his prior acts]. And if he starts without tahari or his ijtihad changes, and he knows after completion that he was correct, it is valid. But if he knows his correctness during it, it becomes invalid, just as if he did not know he was correct at all, even if by predominant opinion. And if a group of people perform tahari in different directions and are ignorant of their imam's state, it suffices them. 'If he is wrong': i.e., he knows after completion that he was wrong. 'He turns': i.e., to the right, not the left. (Maraqi al-Falah] 'And he builds': the word is past tense meaning he builds upon what he performed with tahari. Maraqui al-Falah: 245) 'It becomes invalid': because the beginning of his prayer was based on weakness, i.e., tahari, and the end became based on strength, i.e., the state of knowledge, so building the strong upon the weak is not permissible, contrary to the first case because the beginning is like the end. 'And if they perform tahari': i.e., a group of people in a dark night, their imam prays toward one direction, and each of the followers prays toward a direction, and they do not know what the imam did, it suffices them if they are behind the imam; because each of them is facing the qibla, i.e., the direction of tahari, and this disagreement does not prevent, like inside the Kaaba. And whoever knows the state of his imam, his prayer is invalid because he believes his imam is in error, and similarly if he is ahead of him, because he abandons the obligation of standing. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 269/1]
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct rulings: facing the qibla for those with an excuse, and the procedure of tahari when the qibla is unknown. For the first, those unable to face qibla due to sickness, fear of an enemy, inability to dismount, or fear of drowning face the direction of their ability and safety. The 'fear' is general, including fear for self, animal, or property. For the second, when the qibla is unknown due to darkness or clouds, one must perform tahari (exert effort to determine the direction). Tahari is not allowed if one can ask a knowledgeable person or if there is a mihrab. If one prays without tahari, the prayer is valid only if it turns out they were correct; otherwise, they must repeat. If during prayer they realize they are facing the wrong direction, they turn to the correct one and continue. The commentary also discusses a scenario where a group prays behind an imam, each follower has performed tahari in a different direction, and they do not know the imam's direction—their prayer is valid because each is doing tahari. But if a follower knows the imam is wrong, the follower's prayer becomes invalid.

Key Terms
التحري (al-taḥarrī): Exerting effort to determine the qibla direction when uncertain.
قبلة (qibla): The direction of the Ka'ba in Mecca.
استقبال القبلة (istiqbāl al-qibla): Facing the qibla during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a person do if they realize they are facing the wrong qibla during prayer?
A) Continue and repeat the prayer later.
B) Stop and restart the entire prayer.
C) Turn to the correct qibla and continue from where they are.
D) Complete the prayer and repeat it.

Key Takeaway
Tahari is wajib when qibla is unknown; correct direction makes it valid, but wrong direction requires repetition.

First Two Wajibat of Prayer: Al-Fatiha and Adding a Surah
Introduction to wajibat and first two items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first two wajibat of prayer and identify the condition that affects the obligation of adding a surah.

Core Idea
The wajib in Hanafi fiqh is a distinct category; omission requires sajdah al-sahw but does not invalidate the prayer.

This lesson opens the chapter on the obligatory elements (wajibat) of prayer. The matn lists eighteen items, beginning with the recitation of Surah al-Fatiha and adding a surah (or equivalent) after it. However, the obligation of adding a surah is conditional on having sufficient time. Understanding these initial wajibat helps you internalize the Hanafi concept of 'wajib' — a binding duty that is less than fard in evidentiary strength.

Guided Path
1
Define wajib in Hanafi fiqh
Unlike fard, omission of a wajib does not nullify the prayer but requires sajdah al-sahw as compensation. This is a distinctive feature of the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the first two wajibat
From the matn, the first two wajibat are (1) reciting Surah al-Fatiha and (2) adding a surah (or three short verses) after it. In fard prayer, this applies to the first two rak'ats; in witr and nafl, to all rak'ats.
The text states 'two unspecified rak'ats' of fard — these are the first two.
3
Apply the condition of sufficient time
The commentary clarifies that the obligation of adding a surah is conditional: if one fears missing the prayer time (e.g., near sunrise), only al-Fatiha is required. Even a single verse per rak'at suffices.
This shows that wajib rulings can be suspended when necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في واجب الصلاة وهو ثمانية عشر شيئا قراءة الفاتحة، وضم سورة أو ثلاث آيات في ركعتين غير متعينتين من الفرض، وفي جميع ركعات الوتر والنفل، وتعيين القراءة في الأوليين، وتقديم الفاتحة واعلم أن الأدلة السمعية أنواع أربعة قطعي الثبوت والدلالة كالنصوص المتواترة أي المحكمة، وقطعي الثبوت ظني الدلالة كالآيات المؤولة، وظني الثبوت قطعي الدلالة كأخبار الآحاد التي مفهومها قطعي، وظني الثبوت والدلالة كأخبار الآحاد التي مفهومها ظني، فبالأول يثبت الفرض ،والحرام، وبالثاني والثالث يثبت الوجوب، وكراهة التحريم، وبالرابع يثبت السنة والاستحباب، وكراهة التنزيه؛ ليكون ثبوت الحكم بقدر دليله. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٤٧] ثمانية عشر: أي على ما ذكر هنا، وإلا فهي تزيد على ما ذكره، والتتبع ينفي الحصر. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٤٨] وضم سورة وجوب هذا وما قبله مقيد بما إذا كان في الوقت سعة، فإن خاف فوت الوقت لو قرأ الفاتحة والسورة أو قرأ الفاتحة أو أزيد من آية قرأ في كل ركعة آيةً في جميع الصلاة، وتقسيم القراءة إلى فرض وواجب وسنة بالنسبة لما قبل الإيقاع، أما بعده لو قرأ القرآن كله في ركعة واحدة لم تقع إلا فرضاً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٤٨] وتقديم الفاتحة حتى لو قرأ من السورة ابتداء فتذكر يقرأ الفاتحة ثم يقرأ السورة ويسجد للسهو كما لو كرر الفاتحة ثم قرأ السورة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٤٩]
Section on the obligatory elements of prayer. They are eighteen things: recitation of al-Fatiha, adding a surah or three verses in two unspecified rak'ats of the fard, and in all rak'ats of witr and nafl, specifying the recitation in the first two rak'ats, and giving precedence to al-Fatiha. Know that textual evidences are of four types: qat'i in thubut and dalala, like mutawatir texts i.e., definitive; qat'i in thubut, zanni in dalala, like interpreted verses; zanni in thubut, qat'i in dalala, like ahad hadith whose meaning is definitive; and zanni in thubut and dalala, like ahad hadith whose meaning is zanni. By the first, fard and haram are established; by the second and third, wujub and karaha tahrimiyya are established; by the fourth, sunna and istihbab and karaha tanzihiyya are established, so that the establishment of the ruling is proportionate to its evidence. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 247] 'Eighteen': i.e., according to what is mentioned here, otherwise they exceed what he mentioned, and investigation negates enumeration. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 248] 'And adding a surah': the obligation of this and what precedes it is conditional upon having sufficient time. If he fears missing the time if he recites al-Fatiha and the surah, or he recites al-Fatiha or more than a verse, he recites one verse in each rak'at throughout the prayer. And the division of recitation into fard, wajib, and sunna is before the performance; afterwards, if he recites the entire Quran in one rak'at, it counts only as fard. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 248] 'And giving precedence to al-Fatiha': even if he begins with the surah, then remembers, he recites al-Fatiha then recites the surah and performs sajda al-sahw, as if he repeated al-Fatiha then recited the surah. [Maraqi al-Falah: 249]
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on the obligatory elements (wajibat) of prayer. The matn lists eighteen items, starting with reciting Surah al-Fatiha, then adding a surah or three verses in two unspecified rak'ats of fard prayer (which are the first two rak'ats), and in all rak'ats of witr and nafl. The next wajib is specifying the recitation in the first two rak'ats and giving precedence to al-Fatiha over the surah. The commentary then provides a detailed Hanafi usul theory: the four levels of textual evidence (qat'i and zanni in both thubut and dalala) and how they determine the corresponding rulings (fard, wajib, sunna). The number eighteen is not exhaustive; other elements like tashahhud are also wajib. The obligation of adding a surah is conditional on having sufficient time; if time is short, one recites only al-Fatiha or even a single verse per rak'at. The classification of recitation as fard, wajib, or sunna applies before recitation; after recital it is fard. Finally, if one inadvertently begins with the surah before al-Fatiha, he should recite al-Fatiha then the surah and perform sajda al-sahw.

Key Terms
واجب الصلاة (wājib al-ṣalāh): Elements that are obligatory but not at the level of fard; omission requires sajdah al-sahw.
ضم سورة (ḍamm sūra): Adding a surah after al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ats of fard and all rak'ats of witr and nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a person do if they begin reciting a surah before al-Fatiha in prayer?
A) Continue the surah and omit al-Fatiha
B) Recite al-Fatiha, then the surah, and perform sajdah al-sahw
C) Restart the entire prayer
D) Recite al-Fatiha afterwards without sajdah al-sahw

Key Takeaway
The wajib is a Hanafi-specific category; omission requires sajda al-sahw but does not nullify the prayer.

The Hanafi Evidence Hierarchy: How Textual Proofs Determine Rulings
Usul classification within fiqh passage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify textual evidence into the four Hanafi categories based on thubut and dalala, and state which category establishes fard, wajib, or sunna.

Core Idea
The binding force of a ruling matches the strength of its evidence: qat'i categories yield fard/haram; zanni categories yield wajib/sunnah.

This lesson delves into the Hanafi usul al-fiqh framework that underlies the classification of rulings. The commentator al-Tahtawi inserts a concise but complete theory of evidence hierarchy. Understanding this will help you see why some obligations are called fard (e.g., five daily prayers) and others wajib (e.g., witr), even though both are binding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two axes of evidence strength
Thubut (certainty of transmission) and dalala (certainty of meaning) can each be qat'i (definitive) or zanni (probable). This creates four combinations.
2
Match each combination to its ruling
1) qat'i thubut + qat'i dalala → fard/haram. 2) qat'i thubut + zanni dalala → wajib/karaha tahrimiyya. 3) zanni thubut + qat'i dalala → same as 2. 4) zanni thubut + zanni dalala → sunna/istihbab/karaha tanzihiyya.
The second and third produce the same level of ruling.
3
Apply to a known example
The obligation of five daily prayers: mutawatir Quran (qat'i thubut + qat'i dalala) → fard. Witr: ahad hadith (zanni thubut) with clear imperative (qat'i dalala) → wajib.
This explains why witr is wajib but not fard in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في واجب الصلاة وهو ثمانية عشر شيئا قراءة الفاتحة، وضم سورة أو ثلاث آيات في ركعتين غير متعينتين من الفرض، وفي جميع ركعات الوتر والنفل، وتعيين القراءة في الأوليين، وتقديم الفاتحة واعلم أن الأدلة السمعية أنواع أربعة قطعي الثبوت والدلالة كالنصوص المتواترة أي المحكمة، وقطعي الثبوت ظني الدلالة كالآيات المؤولة، وظني الثبوت قطعي الدلالة كأخبار الآحاد التي مفهومها قطعي، وظني الثبوت والدلالة كأخبار الآحاد التي مفهومها ظني، فبالأول يثبت الفرض ،والحرام، وبالثاني والثالث يثبت الوجوب، وكراهة التحريم، وبالرابع يثبت السنة والاستحباب، وكراهة التنزيه؛ ليكون ثبوت الحكم بقدر دليله. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٤٧] ثمانية عشر: أي على ما ذكر هنا، وإلا فهي تزيد على ما ذكره، والتتبع ينفي الحصر. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٤٨] وضم سورة وجوب هذا وما قبله مقيد بما إذا كان في الوقت سعة، فإن خاف فوت الوقت لو قرأ الفاتحة والسورة أو قرأ الفاتحة أو أزيد من آية قرأ في كل ركعة آيةً في جميع الصلاة، وتقسيم القراءة إلى فرض وواجب وسنة بالنسبة لما قبل الإيقاع، أما بعده لو قرأ القرآن كله في ركعة واحدة لم تقع إلا فرضاً. Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on the obligatory elements (wajibat) of prayer. Key Terms
قطعي الثبوت (qaṭʿī al-thubūt): Certainty of transmission; the text is definitively from revelation (e.g., mutawatir).
ظني الدلالة (ẓannī al-dalāla): Probability of meaning; the text can be interpreted in more than one way.
المحكمة (al-muḥkama): Clear and definitive texts (muhkamat).

Checkpoint
According to the text, which type of evidence establishes the ruling of sunnah?
A) qat'i thubut, qat'i dalala
B) qat'i thubut, zanni dalala
C) zanni thubut, qat'i dalala
D) zanni thubut, zanni dalala

Key Takeaway
The strength of a ruling in Hanafi fiqh is proportionate to the certainty of its evidence.

Rulings on Qibla Error During Prayer
Ruling on what to do if one errs in qibla direction during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for different scenarios of qibla error during prayer and explain the reasoning behind the invalidity when certainty arises after ijtihad.

Core Idea
If you start with ijtihad and later become certain of the true qibla, the prayer breaks—you cannot build strength on weakness.

Determining the qibla is a condition for prayer validity, but what if you make a mistake? The Hanafi school provides detailed rules based on when you discover the error and whether you performed ijtihad. This lesson unpacks those rulings and the logical principle that underpins them, helping you apply them correctly in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenarios
List all the distinct cases mentioned: (a) error discovered after prayer, (b) error discovered during prayer, (c) started without ijtihad and later found correct, (d) started with ijtihad and later found correct during the prayer.
2
Extract the Ruling for Each
For each scenario, note whether the prayer is valid, requires repetition, or requires turning. Use the text: no repetition for error after; turn and continue if error during; valid if no ijtihad and later correct; invalid if ijtihad and later certain during prayer.
Pay attention to the contrast between cases (c) and (d).
3
Analyze the Rationale
The commentary explains the invalidity in case (d) using qiyas: the beginning is weak (taharrī) and the end is strong (certainty). Building the strong on the weak is impermissible. Understand why this does not apply to case (c) where the whole prayer is built on strength.
The principle لا يجوز بناء القوي على الضعيف is a qiyas derived from usul.
4
Apply to the Group Scenario
Consider the case where a congregation prays in different directions without knowing the imam's direction. The text rules it valid as long as they are behind the imam, analogizing to praying inside the Kaaba. Note that if a follower knows the imam is wrong, his prayer breaks.
This shows that ignorance of the imam's direction does not harm validity, but knowledge of his error does.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا إعادة عليه لو أخطأ، وإن علم بخطئه في صلاته استدار وبنى، وإن شرع بلا تحرّ أو تبدل اجتهاده فعلم بعد فراغه أنه أصاب صحت وإن علم بإصابته فيها فسدت كما لو لم يعلم أي من الصلاة ولو بغالب الظن إصابته أصلا، ولو تحرى قوم جهات وجهلوا حال إمامهم تجزئهم. لو أخطأ: أي علم بعد فراغه أنه أخطأ. استدار أي من جهة اليمين لا اليسار. (مراقي الفلاح وبني لفظة ماض البناء أي بني على ما أداه بالتحري. مراقي الفلاح (٢٤٥] فسدت لأن أول صلاته كان مبنياً على ضعف، وهو التحري، وآخر صلاته صار مبنياً على قوة وهي حالة العلم، فلزم بناء القوي على الضعيف وهو لا يجوز، بخلاف الأول فإن الابتداء كالانتهاء. ولو :تحرى أي تحرى جماعة من الناس في ليلة مظلمة، فصلى إمامهم إلى جهة، وصلى كل واحد من المأمورين إلى جهة، ولا يدرون ما صنع الإمام يجزئهم إذا كانوا خلف الإمام؛ لأن كل واحد منهم متوجه إلى القبلة، وهي جهة التحري، وهذه المخالفة لا تمنع كما في جوف الكعبة، ومن علم منهم حال إمامه، تفسد صلاته؛ لاعتقاده أن إمامه على الخطأ، وكذا إذا كان متقدماً عليه؛ لتركه فرض المقام. [تبيين الحقائق: ٢٦٩/١]
And there is no repetition upon him if he errs, and if he knows his error during his prayer he turns and builds, and if he begins without ijtihad or his ijtihad changes and he knows after completion that he was correct, it is valid, and if he knows of his correct direction during it, it becomes invalid, just as if he did not know at all from the prayer, even if by predominant guess his correct direction originally. And if a group of people make ijtihad regarding directions and are ignorant of the state of their imam, it suffices them.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on what happens if a person errs in determining the qibla direction during prayer. The main text states that if he makes a mistake and only realizes after finishing the prayer, no repetition is required. If he realizes during the prayer, he must turn to the correct direction and continue from that point. However, if he started without any ijtihad (personal reasoning) or his ijtihad changed during the prayer, and he finds out after completion that his initial direction was correct, his prayer is valid. But if he finds out during the prayer that he was right originally, the prayer becomes invalid. The commentary explains the reason: the beginning of the prayer was built on weakness (ijtihad/approximation), but the end became built on strength (certain knowledge), and building the strong on the weak is not permissible. However, if from the beginning he had certainty, the whole prayer is built on strength. The commentary also addresses a scenario where a group of people in a dark night each pray in different directions, not knowing the imam's direction. Their prayer is valid as long as they are behind the imam, because each one is facing their ijtihad direction, and this does not prevent validity, just like when praying inside the Kaaba. But if a follower knows that the imam is wrong, his prayer becomes invalid because he believes his imam is in error. Similarly, if a follower is ahead of the imam, his prayer invalidates due to missing the obligation of position.

Key Terms
التحري (al-taharrī): Personal reasoning and estimation to determine the qibla direction when it is unclear.
بناء القوي على الضعيف (binā' al-qawī 'alā al-ḍa'īf): Building the strong on the weak – a legal principle that invalidates an act if its foundation is weak and later becomes strong.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person prays using ijtihad to find qibla, and after completing the prayer he learns that he was facing the wrong direction, what is the ruling according to the passage?
A) He must repeat the prayer.
B) The prayer is invalid.
C) No repetition is required, the prayer is valid.
D) He must make prostrations of forgetfulness.

Key Takeaway
The validity of prayer when qibla is uncertain depends on when certainty is attained and whether the foundation was ijtihad or not; strong cannot be built on weak.

Introduction to the Obligatory Acts of Prayer and the First Three
Enumeration of the 18 wajibat of prayer with commentary on the first three and epistemological classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the first three wajibat of prayer, state the conditions for their obligation, and explain how the Hanafi school classifies rulings based on the strength of textual evidence.

Core Idea
Omission of a wajib requires compensation, but does not invalidate the prayer — and the strength of the ruling matches the strength of its proof.

This passage from Nur al-Idah introduces the concept of wajib (obligatory but not fard) in prayer. It lists the initial wajibat — reciting al-Fatiha, adding a surah, specifying the first two rak'ahs, and presenting al-Fatiha — and then provides a crucial Hanafi framework: the level of a ruling (fard, wajib, sunnah) is determined by the type of evidence (qat'i or zanni in transmission and meaning). Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correctly evaluating the binding force of each act in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the listed wajibat
Name the first three wajibat mentioned: recitation of al-Fatiha, adding a surah/verses, and specifying the recitation to the first two rak'ahs.
The fourth listed is presenting al-Fatiha before the surah.
2
Understand the condition for the wajibat
Note that the obligation of adding a surah (and possibly reciting al-Fatiha) is conditional on having ample time; if time is short, a single verse per rak'ah suffices.
This condition is mentioned in the commentary of Hashiyat al-Tahtawi.
3
Grasp the evidence classification
Learn the four types of textual evidence based on thubut (transmission) and dalala (meaning): qat'i/qat'i, qat'i/zanni, zanni/qat'i, zanni/zanni.
The passage explicitly defines these categories.
4
Connect evidence to ruling
Memorize which ruling level each evidence type establishes: qat'i/qat'i = fard/haram; qat'i/zanni or zanni/qat'i = wajib/karahah tahrimiyah; zanni/zanni = sunnah/mustahabb/karahah tanzihiyah.
This is the core talil (reasoning) of the passage.
5
Apply the principle to the listed wajibat
Recognize that the wajibat mentioned are established by zanni evidence (e.g., ahad hadith or interpreted verses), hence they are wajib not fard.
This explains why the actions are classified as wajib rather than fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو فصل في واجب الصلاة ثمانية عشر شيئا قراءة الفاتحة، وضم سورة أو ثلاث آيات في ركعتين غير متعينتين من الفرض، وفي جميع ركعات الوتر والنفل، وتعيين القراءة في الأوليين، وتقديم الفاتحة من واجب الصلاة: اعلم أن الأدلة السمعية أنواع أربعة قطعي الثبوت والدلالة كالنصوص المتواترة أي المحكمة، وقطعي الثبوت ظني الدلالة كالآيات المؤولة، وظني الثبوت قطعي الدلالة كأخبار الآحاد التي مفهومها قطعي، وظني الثبوت والدلالة كأخبار الآحاد التي مفهومها ظني، فبالأول يثبت الفرض ،والحرام، وبالثاني والثالث يثبت الوجوب، وكراهة التحريم، وبالرابع يثبت السنة والاستحباب، وكراهة التنزيه؛ ليكون ثبوت الحكم بقدر دليله. حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٤٧] ثمانية عشر: أي على ما ذكر هنا، وإلا فهي تزيد على ما ذكره، والتتبع ينفي الحصر. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٤٨] وضم سورة وجوب هذا وما قبله مقيد بما إذا كان في الوقت سعة، فإن خاف فوت الوقت لو قرأ الفاتحة والسورة أو قرأ الفاتحة أو أزيد من آية قرأ في كل ركعة آيةً في جميع الصلاة، وتقسيم القراءة إلى فرض وواجب وسنة بالنسبة لما قبل الإيقاع، أما بعده لو قرأ القرآن كله في ركعة واحدة لم تقع إلا فرضاً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٤٨] وتقديم الفاتحة حتى لو قرأ من السورة ابتداء فتذكر يقرأ الفاتحة ثم يقرأ السورة ويسجد للسهو كما لو كرر الفاتحة ثم قرأ السورة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٤٩]
And it is a chapter on the obligations of prayer: eighteen things: recitation of al-Fatiha, and adding a surah or three verses in two non-specific rak'ahs of the obligatory prayer, and in all rak'ahs of witr and supererogatory prayers, and specifying the recitation in the first two rak'ahs, and presenting al-Fatiha. From the obligations of prayer: Know that the transmitted evidences are four types: qat'i in transmission and meaning like mutawatir texts i.e. muhkam; qat'i in transmission and zanni in meaning like interpreted verses; zanni in transmission and qat'i in meaning like solitary hadith whose meaning is qat'i; and zanni in both transmission and meaning like solitary hadith whose meaning is zanni. By the first, obligation (fard) and prohibition (haram) are established; by the second and third, necessity (wujub) and prohibition of tahrimi; and by the fourth, sunnah, mustahabb, and prohibition of tanzih. This is so that the establishment of the ruling is proportional to its evidence. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 247] 'Eighteen': meaning according to what is mentioned here, otherwise they are more than what he mentioned, and investigation negates limitation. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 248] 'And adding a surah': the obligation of this and what precedes is conditioned upon having ample time; if he fears missing the time if he recites the Fatiha and surah, or recites the Fatiha or more than a verse, he recites one verse in each rak'ah for the entire prayer. And the division of recitation into fard, wajib, and sunnah is in relation to before occurrence; afterwards if he recites the entire Qur'an in one rak'ah, it only occurs as fard. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 248] 'And presenting al-Fatiha': even if he begins with a surah and then remembers, he recites al-Fatiha then recites the surah and performs sajdah al-sahw, just as if he repeated al-Fatiha then recited the surah. [Maraqi al-Falah: 249]
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the obligatory acts (wajibat) of prayer. It first lists eighteen items, beginning with the recitation of Surah al-Fatiha, adding a surah or equivalent verses, specifying the recitation to the first two rak'ahs, and presenting the Fatiha before the surah. The commentary then provides an important framework for understanding how different levels of rulings (fard, wajib, sunnah) are derived from different types of textual evidence. According to the Hanafi school, the strength of a ruling corresponds to the strength of its proof. Four categories of evidence are identified: (1) qat'i in both transmission and meaning (like muhkam verses) establish fard and haram; (2) qat'i in transmission but zanni in meaning (interpreted verses) and (3) zanni in transmission but qat'i in meaning (solitary hadith with clear meaning) establish wujub and karahah tahrimiyah; (4) zanni in both transmission and meaning establishes sunnah, mustahabb, and karahah tanzihiyah. The commentary then clarifies that the list of eighteen is not exclusive; there are more wajibat, and the author only mentioned these. Regarding adding a surah, the obligation is conditional upon having sufficient time; if time is short, one may suffice with a single verse per rak'ah. The division of recitation into fard, wajib, and sunnah pertains to the state before initiating the prayer; after initiating, any recitation is considered fard. Finally, the commentary on presenting the Fatiha explains that if one inadvertently begins with the surah and then remembers, one must recite the Fatiha, then the surah, and perform sajdah al-sahw.

Key Terms
الواجب (al-wājib): A legal duty established by zanni evidence; omission requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw or dam) but does not invalidate the act.
الأدلة السمعية (al-adillah al-sam'iyyah): Textual evidences derived from revelation (Quran and Sunnah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in this passage, if an action is proven by a solitary hadith (khabar wahid) that is zanni in both transmission and meaning, what kind of ruling does it establish?
A) Fard or haram
B) Wajib or karahah tahrimiyah
C) Sunnah or mustahabb or karahah tanzihiyah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies rulings based on the strength of evidence: qat'i evidence gives fard/haram, zanni evidence gives wajib/sunnah, and the list of 18 wajibat in prayer is not exhaustive.

The Remaining Wajibat of Prayer and Their Details
List of wajibat with detailed commentary and procedural rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven wajibat of prayer listed in this passage, explain the procedure for rectifying a missed prostration, and identify the Hanafi ruling on the number of salam.

Core Idea
The wajibat of prayer are seven: nose with forehead, second sajdah, tuma'ninah, first sitting, tashahhud, standing without delay, and salam twice.

This passage from Nur al-Idah and its commentaries completes the list of obligatory acts (wajibat) in prayer, providing detailed rulings for each. Understanding these wajibat is crucial because their omission requires sajdah al-sahw, and distinguishing between wajib and fard is essential for valid prayer. We will walk through each item, examine the rectification procedure for missed prostration, and resolve the internal Hanafi dispute on the salam.

Guided Path
1
List the seven wajibat
Extract each wajib from the passage: nose with forehead in sujud, second sajdah before moving, tuma'ninah, first sitting, tashahhud in first and final sitting, standing for third rak'ah without delay, and wording of salam.
The final sitting is fard, not wajib; the others are wajib.
2
Analyze the nose-with-forehead requirement
Note that prayer is not valid if only the nose touches the ground without excuse. The forehead is primary; the nose is supplementary.
This is the correct view; a dispensation exists for those with forehead excused.
3
Understand the rectification for a missed second sajdah
If one forgets the second sajdah and remembers after the final sitting or salam before speaking, he must prostrate the missed sajdah, then repeat the final sitting and tashahhud, say salam, then perform sajdah al-sahw, and finally sit and recite tashahhud again.
Failure to repeat the sitting invalidates the prayer because the final sitting is fard.
4
Examine tuma'ninah and first sitting
Tuma'ninah means stillness of limbs for at least one tasbih; it is wajib. The first sitting (after two rak'ahs) is also wajib, while the final sitting is fard.
The correct view is that both the first sitting and its tashahhud are wajib, not sunnah.
5
Resolve the dispute on salam
Al-Tahtawi holds that saying salam twice is wajib; others say the second is sunnah. The relied-upon view is wajib, and turning the head is sunnah.
This difference affects whether sajdah al-sahw is required for omitting one salam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على سورة، وضم الأنف للجبهة في السجود، والإتيان بالسجدة الثانية في كل ركعة قبل الانتقال لغيرها، والاطمئنان في الأركان والقعود الأول، وقراءة التشهد فيه في الصحيح، وقراءته في الجلوس الأخير، والقيام إلى الثالثة من غير تراخ بعد التشهد، ولفظ وضم الأنف إلخ لا تجوز الصلاة بالاقتصار على الأنف في السجود على الصحيح ما لم يكن بالجبهة عذر. مراقي الفلاح: حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٤٩] لغيرها أي لغير السجدة من باقي أفعال الصلاة، فإن فات يسجدها ولو بعد القعود الأخير أو بعد السلام قبل الكلام، ثم يعيد القعود، وطريق الإتيان بها أنه إذا تذكرها بعد السلام أو قبله بعد القعود أن يسجد المتروكة، ثم يعيد القعود والتشهد ويسلّم ثم يسجد للسهو ثم يقعد ويتشهد؛ لأن العود إلى السجدة الصلبية يرفع القعود والتشهد وكذا السجدة التلاوية، فلو لم يعد القعود وسلم بمجرد رفعه من السجدة بطلت صلاته؛ لترك القعدة الأخيرة وهي فرضٌ بخلاف سجود السهو؛ فإنه يرفع التشهد فقط، حتى لو سلم بمجرد رفعه منه ولم يقعد صحت صلاته، ولكنه يكره؛ لتركه التشهد وهو واجب [مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٤٩] والاطمئنان في الأركان وهو التعديل في الأركان بتسكين الجوارح في الركوع والسجود حتى تطمئن مفاصله في الصحيح [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٤٩] ويستقر كل عضو في محله بقدر تسبيحة كما في القهستاني. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٤٩] والقعود الأول: أراد بالأول غير الآخر لا الفرد السابق؛ إذ لو أريد به السابق لم يفهم حكم القعدة الثانية التي هي ليست أخيرة؛ لأن القعدة في الصلاة قد تكون أكثر من اثنتين؛ فإن المسبوق بثلاث في الرباعية يقعد ثلاث قعدات كل من الأولى والثانية واجب، والثالثة هي الأخيرة وهي فرض. [البحر الرائق: ٥٧٧/١] وقراءة التشهد: فيسجد للسهو بترك بعضه ككله. وقوله: في الصحيح متعلق بكل من القعود والتشهد، وهو احتراز عن القول بسنيتهما أو سنية التشهد وحده، ولعل صاحب الكتاب إنما لم يأت بالتثنية و لم يقل: والتشهدان للإشارة إلى أن كل تشهد يكون في الصلاة، فهو واجب، سواء كان اثنين أو أكثر. [البحر الرائق: ٥٧٨/١] غير تراخ حتى لو زاد عليه بمقدار أداء ركن ساهيا يسجد للسهو؛ لتأخير واجب القيام للثالثة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٥١] قال الطحطاوي: قوله: بمقدار إلخ على الصحيح، وبينوه بما إذا قال: اللهم صلى على محمد، ولم يذكره في الشرح تباعداً عما يوهم المنع من ذكر الصلاة عليه . وقوله : ساهيا احترز به عن العمد، فإن الصلاة تكون به مكروهة تحريما. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۲۵۱] ولفظ السلام إلخ لم يذكر العدد للاختلاف الواقع فيه، فقيل: لفظ السلام مرتين واجب، قال الطحطاوي وهو الأصح، وقيل: الثانية سنة كما في الفتح. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٥١] وفي قوله: لفظ السلام إشارة إلى أن الالتفات به يمينا ويسارا ليس بواجب، وإنما هو سنة. [البحر الرائق: ٥٧٨/١] ثم الخروج من الصلاة بسلام واحد عند العامة، وقيل: هما كما في مجمع الأنهر، فلو اقتدى به بعد لفظ
Upon a surah, and joining the nose to the forehead in prostration, and performing the second prostration in every rak'ah before moving to something else, and composure in the pillars, and the first sitting, and reciting the tashahhud therein according to the correct view, and reciting it in the final sitting, and standing for the third rak'ah without delay after the tashahhud, and the wording of the salam... 'And joining the nose' etc. Prayer is not valid by limiting to the nose in prostration according to the correct view unless there is an excuse for the forehead. [Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 249] 'Before moving to something else' meaning to other actions of the prayer; if he misses it, he prostrates it even after the final sitting or after the salam before speaking, then repeats the sitting. The method of performing it is that if he remembers after the salam or before it after the sitting, he prostrates the missed one, then repeats the sitting and tashahhud and says salam, then prostrates for forgetfulness, then sits and recites tashahhud; because returning to the essential prostration nullifies the sitting and tashahhud, and likewise the prostration of recitation. So if he does not repeat the sitting and says salam immediately upon rising from the prostration, his prayer is invalid due to abandoning the final sitting which is fard, unlike the forgetfulness prostration which only nullifies the tashahhud, so that if he says salam immediately upon rising from it and does not sit, his prayer is valid but disliked due to abandoning the tashahhud which is wajib. [Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 249] 'And composure in the pillars' which is the adjustment in the pillars by stilling the limbs in bowing and prostration until his joints are at rest according to the correct view. [Maraqi al-Falah: 249] And each limb settles in its place for the measure of one glorification as in al-Qahstani. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 249] 'The first sitting': he meant by 'first' other than the last, not the preceding one; because if he meant the preceding one, the ruling of the second sitting which is not the last would not be understood, for the sitting in prayer may be more than two; indeed the one who is three rak'ahs behind in a four-rak'ah prayer sits three times; the first and second are wajib, and the third is the final and is fard. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 577/1] 'And reciting the tashahhud': he performs sajdah al-sahw for omitting part of it just as for omitting all of it. And his statement 'in the correct view' applies to both the sitting and the tashahhud, and it is a caution against the saying that they are sunnah or that the tashahhud alone is sunnah. Perhaps the author did not use the dual form and say 'the two tashahhuds' to indicate that every tashahhud in the prayer is wajib, whether two or more. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 578/1] 'Without delay' such that if he exceeds it by the measure of performing a pillar forgetfully, he performs sajdah al-sahw for delaying the wajib of standing for the third. [Maraqi al-Falah: 251] al-Tahtawi said: 'his statement 'by the measure' etc. is the correct view, and they explained it as when he says 'O Allah, send blessings upon Muhammad', and he did not mention it in the commentary to avoid suggesting the prohibition of mentioning the blessings upon him. And his statement 'forgetfully' is a precaution against intentional, for the prayer becomes makruh tahrimi by it. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 251] 'And the wording of the salam' etc. he did not mention the number due to the difference of opinion regarding it: it is said that the wording of the salam twice is wajib; al-Tahtawi said it is the most correct, and it is said that the second is sunnah as in al-Fath. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 251] And in his statement 'the wording of the salam' is an indication that turning right and left with it is not wajib but is sunnah. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 578/1] Then exiting from the prayer by one salam according to the general body, and it is said both are as in Majma' al-Anhur, so if he followed him after the wording...
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage completes the list of wajibat of prayer and provides detailed rulings for each. The wajibat covered are: including the nose with the forehead in prostration (if there is no excuse, prayer is not valid with nose alone); performing the second prostration in each rak'ah before moving to other actions; composure (tuma'ninah) in pillars—which means stillness of limbs for at least the duration of one tasbih; the first sitting (which is wajib except the final sitting which is fard); reciting the tashahhud in the first sitting (the correct view is that both the first sitting and its tashahhud are wajib, not sunnah); reciting tashahhud in the final sitting (also wajib); standing for the third rak'ah immediately after tashahhud (if one delays forgetfully, sajdah al-sahw is required; if intentional, it is makruh tahrimi); and the wording of salam (the number of salam is disputed: the relied-upon view is that saying salam twice is wajib, but the turning of the head is not wajib, it is sunnah). The passage also discusses the consequences of missing a prostration and the procedure to rectify it, including repetition of sitting and tashahhud. Finally, it mentions that exiting prayer by one salam is the view of the general body (the majority), but some say two salam are wajib.

Key Terms
الاطمئنان (al-iṭmi'nān): Composure in the prayer pillars: stillness of limbs until joints settle, at least for the duration of one tasbih.
القعود الأول (al-qu'ūd al-awwal): The first sitting in prayer after two rak'ahs; it is wajib except in the final sitting (which is fard).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person forgets the second prostration in a rak'ah and only remembers after the final sitting and salam before speaking, what must he do?
A) He must repeat the entire rak'ah and then perform sajdah al-sahw.
B) He must prostrate the missed prostration, then repeat the final sitting and tashahhud, then say salam, then perform sajdah al-sahw, then sit and recite tashahhud.
C) He does nothing; the prayer is valid because he already performed the first prostration.
D) He must perform sajdah al-sahw only.

Key Takeaway
The seven wajibat of prayer must be known and performed; omission requires sajdah al-sahw, but missing a fard (like the final sitting) invalidates the prayer unless rectified immediately.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
The Wajibat of Prayer: Obligations Requiring Sajdah al-Sahw
Lists wajibat of prayer with Hanafi conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the wajibat of prayer, distinguish them from arkan, and state the consequence of omitting any wajib.

Core Idea
Omission of a wajib does not break the prayer but requires sajdah al-sahw.

In the Hanafi school, the obligatory elements of prayer are divided into fard (pillars) and wajib (obligations). While missing a pillar invalidates the prayer, missing a wajib requires compensation through sajdah al-sahw. This lesson examines the specific wajibat listed in Nur al-Idah, including qunut, the extra takbirs of Eid, and the rules for audible and silent recitation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Hanafi concept of wajib
Recognize that wajib is a category between fard and sunnah, established by probable evidence. Omission does not invalidate the prayer but necessitates sajdah al-sahw.
This distinct category is unique to the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the specific wajibat listed
List each wajib mentioned: the first salam (with conditions), qunut al-witr, takbirat al-Eid, specifying the opening takbir, the takbir of bowing in the second rak'ah of Eid, and the rules for jahr/israr in various prayers.
Memorize these as they are a foundational part of prayer knowledge.
3
Note the conditions for jahr and israr
Understand the minimum for jahr (making at least one hear) and the specific prayers where jahr or israr is wajib. Also note the rule for the individual praying alone.
The imam's jahr is wajib; the munfarid has a choice.
4
Recognize the dispute over the opening takbir
The Hanafi position is that specifying the takbir 'Allahu Akbar' is wajib for every prayer, not just Eid. The text labels this as the soundest view.
The practical difference: if another wording is used, the prayer is makruh and requires sajdah al-sahw.
5
Apply the consequence of omitting a wajib
For any omitted wajib (e.g., qunut, extra takbirs, jahr), the prayer is still valid but sajdah al-sahw must be performed at the end.
This distinguishes wajib from fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة واجبات الصلاة السلام دون عليكم، وقنوت الوتر، وتكبيرات العيدين، وتعيين التكبير لافتتاح كل صلاة لا العيدين خاصة، وتكبيرة الركوع في ثانية العيدين، وجهر الإمام بقراءة الفجر وأوليي العشاءين ولو قضاء والجمعة والعيدين والتراويح والوتر في رمضان، والإسرار في الظهر والعصر وفيما بعد أوليي العشاءين ونفل النهار، والمنفرد مخير المغرب والعشاء فيما يجهر كمتنفل بالليل، = السلام الأول قبل "عليكم" لا يصح عند العامة، وقيل: إن أدركه بعد التسليمة الأولى قبل الثانية فقد أدرك معه الصلاة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٥١] السلام قال الطحطاوي لو أتى بلفظ آخر لا يقوم مقام "السلام" "عليكم ولو كان بمعناه، وقال في "البحر": الشارح نقل الإجماع على أن السلام لا يختص بلفظ عربي البحر الرائق: ٥٧٩/١] وقنوت الوتر أي ويجب قراءة قنوت الوتر عند أبي حنيفة، وكذا تكبيرة القنوت [مراقي الفلاح (۲۵۲] والمراد أنه واجب صلاة الوتر لا واجب مطلق الصلاة، والمراد مطلق الدعاء، وأما خصوص "اللهم إلخ" فسنة، حتى لو أتى بغيره جاز إجماعاً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٥٢] وتكبيرات العيدين أي ويجب التكبيرات الزوائد في صلاة العيدين، وهي في كل ركعة، يجب بتركها سجود السهو، وقال الطحطاوي: الأولى عدم سجود السهو في الجمعة والعيدين، وأما كون التكبيرات في الأولى قبل القراءة وفي الثانية بعدها فمندوب فقط. ثلاث وتعيين التكبير: أي ويجب تعيين لفظ "التكبير" لافتتاح كل صلاة، ويكره الشروع بغيره في الأصح، ولكون الأصح وجوب تعيين لفظ التكبير لافتتاح كل صلاة لا يختص وجوب الافتتاح بالتكبير في صلاة العيدين خاصة، خلافا لمن خصه بهما. [حاشية الطحطاوي ملخصا مراقي الفلاح (۲۵۲] وجهر الإمام إلخ الواجب منه أدناه، أن وهو يسمع غيره ولو واحدا، وإلا كان إسرارا، فلو أسمع اثنين كان من أعلى الجهر قالوا: والأولى أن لا يجهد نفسه بالجهر بل بقدر الطاقة؛ لأن إسماع بعض القوم يكفي، والمستحب أن يجهر بحسب الجماعة، فإن زاد فوق حاجة الجماعة فقد أساء كما لو جهر المصلي بالأذكار [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٥٢] والجمعة: أي ويجب الجهر بالقراءة في صلاة الجمعة والعيدين والتراويح والوتر في رمضان على الإمام. مراقي الفلاح (٢٥٣] سواء قدمه على التراويح أو أخره، بل ولو تركها، وقيد بكونه في رمضان؛ لأن صلاته بجماعة في غيره بدعة مكروهة. [حاشية الطحطاوي ملخصا : ٢٥٣] وفيما بعد إلخ الثالثة والرابعة من العشاء. (مراقي الفلاح) والمنفرد إلخ أي إن شاء جهر، وهو أفضل؛ ليكون الأداء على هيئة الجماعة، ولهذا كان أداؤه بأذان وإقامة أفضل، وإن شاء خافت؛ لأنه ليس خلفه من يسمعه، وقوله : "فيما يجهر" إشارة إلى أنه من المغرب، وهي ولو ترك السورة في أوليبي العشاء قرأها في الأخريين مع الفاتحة جهرا، ولو ترك الفاتحة لا يكررها في الأخريين.
The book of prayer. The obligatory elements of prayer: The first salam (without 'alaykum) is not valid according to the general view. Qunut al-witr, the extra takbirs of the two Eids, specifying the takbir for the opening of every prayer (not only for Eid), the takbir of bowing in the second rak'ah of Eid, the imam's audible recitation in Fajr and the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha (even if making up a prayer), Jumu'ah, the two Eids, Tarawih, and Witr in Ramadan; silent recitation in Zuhr and Asr, and after the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha, and in voluntary prayers of the day. The person praying alone has a choice in Maghrib and Isha regarding audible recitation like a voluntary night prayer. [First salam: The first salam before 'alaykum is not valid according to the general view. It is said: if a latecomer catches the first taslim before the second, he has caught the prayer with the imam. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 251] Regarding the salam, al-Tahtawi said: If one uses another wording, it does not suffice even if similar in meaning. It is said in al-Bahr: The commentator transmitted consensus that the salam is not restricted to Arabic wording. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 1:579] Qunut al-witr: It is obligatory to recite the qunut of witr according to Abu Hanifa, and likewise the takbir of qunut. [Maraqi al-Falah 252] The meaning is that it is an obligation of witr prayer, not an absolute obligation of prayer. The essential is absolute supplication; the specific wording 'Allahumma...' is sunnah, so if one recites something else, it is permissible by consensus. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 252] The extra takbirs of the two Eids: They are obligatory, and omitting them requires sajdah al-sahw. Al-Tahtawi said: It is preferable not to perform sajdah al-sahw for Jumu'ah and Eid. The placement of takbirs in the first rak'ah before recitation and in the second after recitation is merely recommended. Three [takbirs?] Specifying the takbir: It is obligatory to specify the word 'takbir' for the opening of every prayer, and it is makruh to start with other words in the soundest view. Because the soundest view is that specifying the takbir for opening is obligatory for every prayer, not confined to Eid prayers, contrary to those who restrict it to them. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi summarized from Maraqi al-Falah 252] The imam's audible recitation: The minimum obligation is that he makes others hear, even one person; otherwise it is silent. If he makes two hear, it is the highest degree of audible. They said: It is preferable not to strain oneself beyond capacity, because making some of the congregation hear is sufficient. It is recommended to recite audibly according to the congregation. If he exceeds the congregation's need, he has done wrong, like if he recites the dhikr audibly. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 252] Jumu'ah: It is obligatory for the imam to recite audibly in Jumu'ah, the two Eids, Tarawih, and Witr in Ramadan. [Maraqi al-Falah 253] Whether he prays Tarawih before Witr or after, even if he omits it. The restriction to Ramadan is because praying it in congregation outside Ramadan is an innovation and makruh. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi summarized: 253] And after the first two rak'ahs (of Maghrib and Isha) means the third and fourth. (Maraqi al-Falah) The person praying alone has a choice: If he wishes, he recites audibly, which is better to follow the congregation form; similarly, his prayer with adhan and iqamah is better. If he wishes, he recites silently because there is no one behind him. His statement 'in that which he recites audibly' indicates that it is from Maghrib, and it is. And if he omits the surah in the first two rak'ahs of Isha, he recites it in the last two with the Fatiha audibly. If he omits the Fatiha, he does not repeat it in the last two rak'ahs.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a listing of the obligatory elements (wajibat) of prayer according to the Hanafi school, drawn from the matn of Nur al-Idah with hashiyah commentary. The author begins by stating that the first salam (without 'alaykum) is not valid, but a latecomer who catches the first taslim before the second has caught the prayer. The first wajib mentioned is the qunut of witr. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, reciting the qunut is obligatory in witr prayer; however, the specific wording (e.g., 'Allahumma...') is sunnah, so any supplication suffices by consensus. Next, the extra takbirs in Eid prayer are wajib; omitting them requires sajdah al-sahw, though al-Tahtawi notes it is preferable not to perform sajdah al-sahw for Jumu'ah and Eid. The placement of these takbirs (before recitation in the first rak'ah, after in the second) is merely recommended (mandub). Specifying the word 'Allahu Akbar' for the opening takbir is wajib for every prayer, not only for Eid, contrary to the view of some scholars who restrict it. The imam's audible recitation (jahr) has a minimum: he must make at least one person hear; otherwise it is considered silent (israr). He should not strain beyond capacity. Audible recitation is required in Fajr, first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha (and their make-ups), Jumu'ah, Eid, Tarawih, and Witr in Ramadan. Silent recitation is required in Zuhr, Asr, and after the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha, and in voluntary day prayers. The individual praying alone has a choice in Maghrib and Isha regarding audible recitation, but the better option is to recite audibly to mimic congregation. Finally, the passage addresses a case: if one omits the surah in the first two rak'ahs of Isha (or Maghrib), he must recite it in the last two rak'ahs along with the Fatiha audibly. However, if he omits the Fatiha, he does not repeat it in the last two rak'ahs; instead, he performs sajdah al-sahw. These rulings underscore that the wajibat are distinct from the fard (pillars): omitting them does not invalidate the prayer but requires compensation through sajdah al-sahw.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): An obligatory element established by probable evidence, distinct from fard (definitive). Omission requires sajdah al-sahw but does not invalidate the prayer.
سجود السهو (sajdah al-sahw): Two prostrations performed at the end of prayer to compensate for error, omission of a wajib, or delay in a wajib.
قنوت الوتر (qunut al-witr): A supplication recited in the witr prayer after the bowing or before, which is wajib according to Abu Hanifa.
تكبيرات العيدين (takbirat al-'idayn): The extra takbirs recited in Eid prayer, three in the first rak'ah after the opening takbir and three in the second after the takbir of standing, which are wajib.
جهر (jahr): Audible recitation that can be heard by others; the minimum is making at least one person hear.
إسرار (israr): Silent recitation in which only the reciter hears himself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the required action if one forgetfully omits the qunut al-witr?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) Perform sajdah al-sahw at the end of the prayer.
C) Repeat the qunut after the prayer.
D) No action needed; the prayer is valid without compensation.

Key Takeaway
The wajibat of prayer are obligations whose omission requires sajdah al-sahw, preserving the validity of the prayer while ensuring compensation for the error.

The Sunnah Acts of Prayer (Fifty-One Sunnahs)
Enumerating the sunnah acts of prayer and their specific details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on omitting a sunnah act in prayer and identify the proper method for performing the first several sunnahs mentioned in the text.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, omitting a sunnah act does not invalidate prayer or require sajdah al-sahw; it is merely disliked.

This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates the sunnah acts of prayer, beginning with the first five. Understanding these sunnahs is crucial for achieving completeness in worship, but equally important is knowing their legal weight: they are recommended, not obligatory. The text clarifies that leaving a sunnah intentionally without contempt is only makruh tanzihi—a slight offense—and does not affect the validity of the prayer or necessitate the forgetfulness prostration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal category of sunnah
Understand that sunnah acts are recommended; their omission does not invalidate prayer or require sajdah al-sahw.
The text explicitly states: 'ترك السنة لا يوجب فسادا ولا سهوا'.
2
List the first five sunnahs from the passage
Identify: raising hands for takbir, spreading fingers, synchronizing with imam, placing right on left below navel, reciting Fatiha audibly/silently.
Others follow later in the original text.
3
Note the specific details for each sunnah
For raf' al-yadayn: man and slave woman to ears, free woman to shoulders. For nashr al-asabi': spread naturally. For muqaranat al-ihram: follower must not finish before imam.
These details are from the commentary (al-Tahtawi).
4
Apply the ruling on omission
If a sunnah is omitted, the prayer is still valid; no sajdah al-sahw is required. Deliberate omission without contempt is offensive (isa'ah).
This principle applies to all fifty-one sunnahs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في سننها وهي إحدى وخمسون رفع اليدين للتحريمة حذاء الأذنين للرجل والأمة، وحذاء المنكبين للحرة، ونشر الأصابع، ومقارنة إحرام المقتدي لإحرام إمامه، ووضع الرجل يده اليمنى على اليسرى تحت سرته، الفاتحة جهرا لا يجهر فيما لا يجهر فيه، بل يخافت فيه حتما، وهو الصحيح؛ لأن الإمام يتحتم عليه المخافتة، فالمنفرد أولى، والمراد بقوله: "فيما يجهر جهر الإمام، وفيه إشارة إلى أنه إذا فاتته صلاة يجهر فيها يخير المنفرد كما كان في الوقت، والجهر أفضل لأن القضاء يحكي الأداء، فلا يخالفه في الوصف، وقوله: "كمتنفل بالليل" يعني به المنفرد؛ لأن النوافل أتباع الفرائض، ولهذا يخفي في نوافل النهار ولو كان إماماً. تبيين الحقائق ملخصاً: ۳۲۷/۱] ولو ترك إلخ أي ولو ترك السورة في ركعة من أوليي المغرب أو في جميع أوليي العشاء عمدا أو سهوا، قرأ السورة وجوبا على الأصح في الأخريين من العشاء، والثالثة من المغرب مع را بهما على الأصح، ويقدم الفاتحة ثم يقرأ السورة ، وهو الأشبه [حاشية الطحطاوي، مراقي الفلاح: ٢٥٤] لا يكررها إلخ أي لو ترك الفاتحة في الأوليين لا يكررها في الأخريين عندهم، ويسجد للسهو؛ لأن قراءة الفاتحة في الشفع الثاني مشروعة، فإذا قرأها مرة وقعت عن الأداء؛ لأنها أقوى لكونها في محلها، ولو كررها خالف المشروع، بخلاف السورة ، فإن الشفع الثاني ليس محلا لها أداء فجاز أن يقع قضاءً؛ لأنه محل القضاء. مراقي الفلاح، تبيين الحقائق: ۳۲۹/۱] سننها : اعلم أن ترك السنة لا يوجب فسادا ولا سهوا، بل إساءة لو عامدا غير مستخف، وقالوا: الإساءة أدون من الكراهة التحريمية. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٥٦] ونشر الأصابع: وكيفيته أن لا يضم كل الضم ولا يفرج كل التفريج، بل يتركها على حالها منشورة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٥٧] ومقارنة إحرام إلخ لكن يشترط أن لا يكون فراغه من "الله" أو من "أكبر" قبل فراغ الإمام منهما، فلو فرغ من قوله: "الله" مع الإمام أو بعده وفرغ من قوله: "أكبر" قبل فراغ الإمام منه لا يصح شروعه في أظهر الروايات، على الأصح. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٥٧] ووضع الرجل إلخ : أي يضع على الكيفية المذكورة كما فرغ من التكبير للإحرام بلا إرسال لا كما يفعله جهال زماننا، فإنهم يرسلون اليدين بعد تكبيرة الإحرام =
Chapter on its sunnahs. They are fifty-one: Raising the hands for the takbir of ihram level with the earlobes for a man and a slave woman, and level with the shoulders for a free woman; spreading the fingers; the follower synchronizing his ihram with the imam's ihram; a man placing his right hand on his left below the navel; reciting the Fatiha audibly where audible recitation is prescribed, and silently where silent recitation is prescribed, and that is correct because the imam is obligated to recite silently; the individual is more entitled. The meaning of his statement: 'in that which he recites audibly' refers to the imam's audible recitation, and it indicates that if a person misses a prayer that is recited audibly, the individual has a choice as if in time, but audible is better because the make-up mimics the performance. His statement: 'like a voluntary night prayer' means the individual, because voluntary prayers follow obligatory prayers; hence one recites silently in voluntary day prayers even if an imam. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq summarized 1:327] And if he omits the surah: i.e., if he omits the surah in one rak'ah of the first two of Maghrib or in all the first two of Isha intentionally or forgetfully, he recites the surah obligatorily in the soundest view in the last two of Isha and the third of Maghrib along with their recitation, and he presents the Fatiha first, then recites the surah; that is most appropriate. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi, Maraqi al-Falah 254] He does not repeat it: i.e., if he omits the Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs, he does not repeat it in the last two according to them, and he performs sajdah al-sahw because reciting the Fatiha in the second pair of rak'ahs is prescribed; if he recites it once, it counts as performance because it is stronger in its place; if he repeats it, he goes against the prescribed. Unlike the surah, the second pair is not a place for surah as performance, so it is permissible as makeup because it is a place for makeup. [Maraqi al-Falah, Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1:329] Its sunnahs: Know that leaving a sunnah does not cause invalidity nor forgetfulness, but is offensive if intentional without underestimation. They said: Offensiveness is lesser than prohibition (karahah tahrimiyyah). [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi 256] Spreading the fingers: Its method is not to clench completely nor to spread completely, but to leave them naturally spread. [Maraqi al-Falah 257] Synchronizing ihram: But it is a condition that his completion of 'Allah' or 'Akbar' not be before the imam's completion of both. If he completes 'Allah' with the imam or after, and completes 'Akbar' before the imam completes it, his start is not valid in the most apparent narrations, according to the soundest view. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi 257] Placing the man's hands: He places them in the described manner as he finishes the takbir of ihram without letting them hang, not as the ignorant of our time do, for they let their hands hang after the takbir of ihram =
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the chapter on the sunnahs of prayer (fifty-one sunnahs). The author opens by stating that the sunnahs are fifty-one acts, then lists several: raising the hands for the opening takbir (level with earlobes for men and female slaves, shoulders for free women), spreading the fingers naturally, synchronizing one's ihram with the imam's, placing the right hand over the left below the navel, reciting the Fatiha audibly where required and silently where required, and more. It emphasizes that a person praying alone should not recite audibly in silent prayers; the imam is obligated to be silent in such prayers. The passage then delves into a case: if one omits the surah in the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib or Isha, he must recite it in the remaining rak'ahs (third for Maghrib, last two for Isha) along with the Fatiha. However, if he omits the Fatiha, he does not repeat it in the last rak'ahs but performs sajdah al-sahw, because the Fatiha is prescribed in every rak'ah as a performance, while the surah can be made up as a qada'. The text concludes with a reminder that leaving a sunnah intentionally (without contempt) does not cause invalidity or require sajdah al-sahw; it is merely offensive (isa'ah), which is less than prohibiting dislike (karahah tahrimiyyah). The commentary by al-Tahtawi clarifies the method of spreading fingers and synchronizing ihram: the follower must not finish saying 'Allah' or 'Akbar' before the imam; if he finishes 'Allah' with the imam or later but finishes 'Akbar' before the imam, his prayer does not start validly in the most authentic narration. Finally, the proper placement of the hands is immediately after the takbir, not with a pause of letting them hang, as done by some ignorant people.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act; leaving it without contempt is makruh tanzihi, but does not invalidate the prayer or require sajdah al-sahw.
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands to the level of the ears (for men and slave women) or shoulders (for free women) when pronouncing the takbir of ihram.
مقارنة الإحرام (muqaranat al-ihram): The follower synchronizing his opening takbir with the imam's, not finishing before the imam finishes both words 'Allahu' and 'Akbar'.
نشر الأصابع (nashr al-asabi'): Spreading the fingers naturally without clenching or over-spreading when raising the hands for takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on omitting the sunnah of raising the hands for takbir al-ihram in prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid.
B) The prayer is valid but requires sajdah al-sahw.
C) The prayer is valid and no compensation is needed.
D) The prayer must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, omitting a sunnah act in prayer does not cause invalidity or require sajdah al-sahw; it is merely offensive if intentional.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Ruling on Sunnah Acts and Muqarana in Prayer
Commentary on rulings of sunan and muqarana

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intentionally leaving a sunnah and identify the condition for valid muqarana in congregational prayer.

Core Idea
Leaving a sunnah does not break prayer; muqarana requires follower to finish takbir after imam.

The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes sunnah from wajib. This lesson explains the legal status of sunan (recommended acts), the crucial condition of muqarana when following an imam, and the recommended formulations for thana' and ta'awwudh. Understanding these distinctions preserves valid prayer and proper adab.

Guided Path
1
Understand the category of sunnah
Identify that sunnah acts are recommended but not obligatory. Deliberate omission without contempt incurs isa'ah (blame), not invalidity or sajdat al-sahw.
Isa'ah is lighter than makruh tahrimi.
2
Learn the muqarana condition
The follower must complete saying 'Allah' and 'Akbar' after the imam finishes them. If the follower finishes 'Akbar' before the imam, the prayer start is invalid.
This is on the most apparent transmissions.
3
Review thana' and ta'awwudh
Thana' is recited until the imam begins recitation. The preferred wording for ta'awwudh is 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' according to the majority.
Al-Hidayah's preference for 'Asta'idhu' is weakened.

And if he leaves the surah in the first two of the night prayer, he recites it in the last two with the Fatihah aloud, and if he leaves the Fatihah, he does not repeat it in the last two. Section on its sunan: They are fifty-one: raising the hands for the takbir at the level of the ears for a man and a slave woman, and at the level of the shoulders for a free woman; spreading the fingers; the muqarana (alignment) of the follower's ihram with the imam's ihram; and the man placing his right hand on his left under his navel. The Fatihah aloud: He does not recite aloud where it is not recited aloud, but rather recites quietly necessarily, and this is correct; because the imam is obliged to recite quietly, so the individual is more entitled. The meaning of his statement: 'In what is recited aloud, the imam recites aloud'—and it contains an indication that if he misses a prayer in which recitation is aloud, the individual has a choice as if he were in the time, and aloud is better because the make-up resembles the performance. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, Maraqi al-Falah: 254] 'He does not repeat it, etc.' meaning if he leaves the Fatihah in the first two, he does not repeat it in the last two according to them, and he performs prostrations of forgetfulness; because recitation of the Fatihah in the second pair is prescribed, so if he recites it once, it counts as performance because it is stronger being in its place; if he repeated it, he would contradict the prescribed.
