[Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 257] Placing of the man, etc.: meaning he places in the described manner when he finishes the takbir for ihram without letting them hang—not as the ignorant of our time do, for they let their hands hang after the takbir of ihram = ... The description of placement is that he makes the palm of his right hand on the back of his left hand, forming a ring with the little finger and thumb on the wrist. And the woman places her hands on her chest without forming a ring. And the Thana' and Ta'awwudh. Then they place them, and one must know that there are four issues here: First, does he place his right hand on his left in prayer or not? Second, how does he place? Third, where does he place? Fourth, when does he place? As for the first, according to the statement of our three imams: the sunnah is that he supports his right hand on his left. As for the description of placement—the second issue—there is in the marfu' hadith the word 'taking', and in another hadith the word 'placing', and many of our teachers combine them by placing the palm of his right hand on the back of his left hand, forming a ring with the little finger and thumb on the wrist, to act upon both hadiths. As for the place of placement—the third issue—the best in our school is below the navel. Then, in the zahir al-madhhab, supporting is a sunnah of standing; and it is narrated from Muhammad that it is a sunnah for recitation, and this is evident in the one praying after the takbir. This is the fourth issue: according to Muhammad, he lets his hands hang during the Thana', and when he begins recitation, he supports; in the zahir al-riwayah, as soon as he folds his hands after the takbir, he supports al-Kifayah summary: 1/249 on the wrist and spreads three fingers on the forearm. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi) And the woman's placement: Know that the woman differs from the man in several issues: among them, she does not take her hands out of her sleeves during takbir, and she raises her hands to the level of her shoulders, and she does not spread her fingers in bowing, and she bows slightly so that she reaches the knees, not exceeding that because it is more concealing for her, and she sticks her elbows to her sides in bowing, and she sticks her belly to her thighs in prostration, and she sits mutawarrikan in every sitting by sitting on her left buttock, and she brings out both feet from the right side, and she places one thigh on the other, and she makes the right shin on the left shin, and she does not lead men, and her leading women is makruh, and the imam stands in the middle of them, and she does not recite aloud where aloud is prescribed, and al-isfar (praying at dawn in early light) is not recommended for her, and detailed enumeration negates limitation. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 259] And the Thana': Know that every person praying comes with the Thana'; the follower comes with it as long as the imam has not commenced recitation absolutely, whether he is a latecomer or a perceiver in a state of loud or quiet recitation. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 259] And Ta'awwudh i.e. the one praying says: 'I seek refuge with Allah from the accursed Shaytan'—and this is the choice of Abu 'Amr and 'Asim and Ibn Kathir, and it is the chosen view in our school; it is the statement of the majority, and it is his 'isti'adha' (seeking refuge). By this, what is chosen in al-Hidayah is weakened, that it is better to say 'Astaghfirullah'? No, 'A'udhu billah'... The objection is that the verse says 'fasta'idh' (imperative of isti'adha) and 'A'udhu' is from 'awdh' not isti'adha. The response as in Fath al-Qadir: that the word 'ista'idh' is a request for 'awdh, and his saying 'A'udhu' is a suitable response to it, but its proximity to the wording is overlooked. [Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/595]
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the sunan (recommended acts) of prayer from Nur al-Idah. It begins by stating a ruling: if a person misses reciting a surah (after Fatihah) in the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib or 'Isha', they must recite it in the remaining rak'ahs along with the Fatihah, and recite it aloud. However, if they miss the Fatihah itself, they do not repeat it in later rak'ahs but instead perform sajdat al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). The commentary then explains the jahr (loud recitation) rule: the imam must recite aloud where required and quietly where required; the individual follower can choose if they miss a prayer, but loud is better because the make-up prayer resembles the original. The passage then lists the 51 sunan of prayer, starting with raising hands for takbir (at ears for men/slave women, shoulders for free women), spreading fingers, and the follower's intention (muqarana) aligning with the imam. The commentary clarifies that leaving a sunnah is not sinful enough to require sajdat al-sahw, but it is considered 'isa'ah (blameworthy) if done intentionally without contempt, which is slightly less severe than makruh tahrimi. Detailed instructions follow for spreading fingers (neither fully closed nor fully spread) and muqarana (the follower must not finish saying 'Allahu Akbar' before the imam finishes, otherwise their prayer start is invalid in the most reliable narration). The longest section discusses placing the hands: the man places his right hand on the left (ruling from all three of our imams), with the palm on the back, forming a ring with little finger and thumb on the wrist, below the navel. The placement is a sunnah of standing (zahir al-madhhab) or according to Muhammad a sunnah of recitation. The woman places her hands on her chest without forming a ring. A separate section details women's prayer differences: they do not raise hands out of sleeves, raise to shoulders, bow less, sit mutawarrikan, do not lead men, etc. Finally, the passage covers Thana' (praise: 'Subhanaka Allahumma') and Ta'awwudh (seeking refuge). The follower recites Thana' until the imam starts reciting. For Ta'awwudh, the chosen wording is 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim', not 'Astaghfiru'? Actually, the text says the majority choose 'A'udhu', and this weakens the view in al-Hidayah that prefers 'Asta'idh'? Wait, the text says: the chosen view is 'A'udhu', and this weakens what al-Hidayah chose that it is better to say 'Asta'idh'? Actually, the text says: 'A'udhu' is the choice of many, and this weakens what al-Hidayah chose (that it is better to say 'Asta'idh'? Actually 'Asta'idh' is not mentioned; the text says 'Asta'idh'? No, the text says 'Asta'idh? Actually it says: 'أستعيذ بالله'? The translation says 'A'udhu billah...' and then 'Asta'idh'? Let's re-read: the Arabic says: 'استعادته' and 'أستعيذ' and 'أعوذ'. The point is about the wording: 'A'udhu' (أعوذ) vs. 'Ista'idh' (أستعيذ). The chosen view is 'A'udhu' because it matches the Qur'anic command 'fasta'idh' in meaning. The response from Fath al-Qadir supports 'A'udhu' as matching the command. So the commentary ends the section.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act in prayer; omitting it intentionally without contempt incurs isa'ah (blame) but does not invalidate prayer or require sajdat al-sahw.
إساءة (isa'ah): Blameworthy act, less severe than makruh tahrimi, incurred by deliberately leaving a sunnah without contempt.
مقارنة الإحرام (muqaranat al-ihram): The follower's synchronizing of their takbirat al-ihram with the imam's, specifically that the follower's completion of 'Allahu Akbar' must not be before the imam's completion.
تعوذ (ta'awwudh): Seeking refuge (isti'adha) with Allah from Satan, recommended at the start of recitation in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a follower finishes his 'Allahu Akbar' before the imam finishes his 'Akbar'?
A) The prayer is valid but the follower incurs isa'ah.
B) The follower's prayer start is invalid and he must repeat the takbir.
C) The follower must perform sajdat al-sahw after the prayer.
D) The prayer is invalid and the follower must restart the entire prayer from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
Sunnah acts in prayer are recommended; leaving them incurs isa'ah but does not invalidate; muqarana requires the follower's takbir to finish after the imam's.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Hand Placement for Men in Prayer
Detailed ruling on hand placement for men

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on hand placement for men, including the preferred position and the intra-madhhab difference on timing.

Core Idea
Men place right hand on left below navel, forming a ring; the timing is after takbir in the vivid narration.

The placement of hands in prayer is a sunnah with detailed rulings. This lesson examines the four questions: whether to place, how, where, and when. The Hanafi school has a clear preference, though a minor internal difference exists regarding whether it is a sunnah of standing or recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four issues
The text presents four sub-questions: (1) Is it sunnah to place hands at all? (2) How exactly? (3) Where? (4) When?
These are known as the 'four issues' in hand placement.
2
Answer the first issue: whether to place
According to all three founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), it is sunnah to support the right hand on the left.
This establishes the act as sunnah.
3
Answer the second and third: how and where
Place the palm of the right hand on the back of the left, form a ring with little finger and thumb on the wrist. The position is below the navel.
The ring (tahlilq) is specific to men.
4
Answer the fourth: when to place
In the vivid narration (zahir al-riwayah), hands are placed immediately after the takbir (sunnah of standing). According to Imam Muhammad, hands are placed after thana', during recitation (sunnah of recitation).
Both are sunnah, but the vivid narration is preferred.

لا يجهر فيما لا يجهر فيه، بل يخافت فيه حتما، وهو الصحيح؛ لأن الإمام يتحتم عليه المخافتة، فالمنفرد أولى، والمراد بقوله: "فيما يجهر جهر الإمام، وفيه إشارة إلى أنه إذا فاتته صلاة يجهر فيها يخير المنفرد كما كان في الوقت، والجهر أفضل لأن القضاء يحكي الأداء، فلا يخالفه في الوصف، وقوله: "كمتنفل بالليل" يعني به المنفرد؛ لأن النوافل أتباع الفرائض، ولهذا يخفي في نوافل النهار ولو كان إماماً. تبيين الحقائق ملخصاً: ۳۲۷/۱] ولو ترك إلخ أي ولو ترك السورة في ركعة من أوليي المغرب أو في جميع أوليي العشاء عمدا أو سهوا، قرأ السورة وجوبا على الأصح في الأخريين من العشاء، والثالثة من المغرب مع را بهما على الأصح، ويقدم الفاتحة ثم يقرأ السورة ، وهو الأشبه [حاشية الطحطاوي، مراقي الفلاح: ٢٥٤] لا يكررها إلخ أي لو ترك الفاتحة في الأوليين لا يكررها في الأخريين عندهم، ويسجد للسهو؛ لأن قراءة الفاتحة في الشفع الثاني مشروعة، فإذا قرأها مرة وقعت عن الأداء؛ لأنها أقوى لكونها في محلها، ولو كررها خالف المشروع، بخلاف السورة ، فإن الشفع الثاني ليس محلا لها أداء فجاز أن يقع قضاءً؛ لأنه محل القضاء. مراقي الفلاح، تبيين الحقائق: ۳۲۹/۱] سننها : اعلم أن ترك السنة لا يوجب فسادا ولا سهوا، بل إساءة لو عامدا غير مستخف، وقالوا: الإساءة أدون من الكراهة التحريمية. سنن الصلاة
وصفة الوضع أن يجعل باطن كف اليمنى على ظاهر كف اليسرى محلّقا بالخنصر والإبهام على الرسغ، ووضع المرأة يديها على صدرها من غير تحليق، والثناء، والتعوذ .
ثم يضعونها، ويجب أن يعلم أن ههنا أربع مسائل: إحداها أنه هل يضع يده اليمنى على اليسرى في الصلاة أم لا؟ والثانية: كيف يضع؟ والثالثة: أين يضع؟ والرابعة متى يضع؟ أما الأولى فعلى قول علمائنا الثلاثة: السنة أن يعتمد بيده اليمنى على اليسرى، وأما صفة الوضع وهي المسألة الثانية، ففي الحديث المرفوع لفظ الأخذ، وفي حديث عليه لفظ الوضع، ويتحسن كثير من مشايخنا الجمع بينهما بأن يضع باطن كفه اليمنى على ظاهر كفه اليسرى، ويحلق بالخنصر والإبهام على الرسغ؛ ليكون عاملا بالحديثين وأما موضع الوضع، وهو الثالثة، فالأفضل عندنا تحت السرة، ثم في ظاهر المذهب الاعتماد سنة القيام، وروي عن محمد : أنه سنة للقراءة، وتبين هذا في المصلي بعد التكبير وهي المسألة الرابعة، فعند محمد مه يرسل يديه في حالة الثناء، فإذا أخذ في القراءة اعتمد، وفي ظاهر الرواية كما يكف يديه بعد التكبير يعتمد الكفاية ملخصا: ٢٤٩/١] على الرسغ ويبسط ثلاثة أصابعه على الذراع. (حاشية الطحطاوي ووضع المرأة: اعلم أن المرأة تخالف الرجل في مسائل منها هذه، ومنها أنها لا تخرج كفيها من كميها عند التكبير، وترفع يديها حذاء منكبيها، ولا تفرج أصابعها في الركوع، وتنحني في الركوع قليلاً بحيث تبلغ الركوع، فلا تزيد على ذلك؛ لأنه أستر لها، وتلزق مرفقيها بجنبيها فيه وتلزق بطنها بفخذيها في السجود، وتجلس متوركة في كل قعود بأن تجلس على أليتها اليسرى، وتخرج کلتا رجليها من الجانب الأيمن، وتضع فخذيها على بعضهما، وتجعل الساق الأيمن على الساق الأيسر، ولا تؤم الرجال، وتكره جماعتهن، ويقف الإمام وسطهن ولا تجهر في موضع الجهر، ولا يستحب في حقها الإسفار بالفجر، والتتبع ينفي الحصر. [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٥٩] والثناء: اعلم أن الثناء يأتي به كل مصل فالمقتدي يأتي به ما لم يشرع الإمام في القراءة مطلقاً، سواء كان مسبوقاً أو مدركاً في حالة الجهر أو السر. [حاشية الطحطاوي (۲۵۹] والتعوذ أي قال المصلي: أعوذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم وهو اختيار أبي عمر وعاصم وابن كثير، وهو المختار عندنا، أصحابنا؛ قول الأكثر من وهو استعادته ، وبهذا يضعف ما اختاره في "الهداية" من أن الأولى أن يقول: "أستعيذ بالله" ليوافق من لأن المذكور فيه "فاستعذ بصيغة الأمر من الاستعاذة و"أستعيذ" مضارعها فيتوافقان بخلاف "أعوذ"، فإنه من العوذ لا الاستعاذة، وجوابه كما في "فتح القدير : أن لفظ "استعذ" طلب العوذ، وقوله: "أعوذ" من مثال مطابق لمقتضاه أما قربه من اللفظ فهدر [البحر الرائق: ٥٩٥/١]
Book of Prayer... AV... Sunnah of Prayer. And if he leaves the surah in the first two of the night prayer, he recites it in the last two with the Fatihah aloud, and if he leaves the Fatihah, he does not repeat it in the last two. Section on its sunan: They are fifty-one: raising the hands for the takbir at the level of the ears for a man and a slave woman, and at the level of the shoulders for a free woman; spreading the fingers; the muqarana (alignment) of the follower's ihram with the imam's ihram; and the man placing his right hand on his left under his navel. The Fatihah aloud: He does not recite aloud where it is not recited aloud, but rather recites quietly necessarily, and this is correct; because the imam is obliged to recite quietly, so the individual is more entitled. The meaning of his statement: 'In what is recited aloud, the imam recites aloud'—and it contains an indication that if he misses a prayer in which recitation is aloud, the individual has a choice as if he were in the time, and aloud is better because the make-up resembles the performance. His statement: 'like a voluntary performer at night' means the individual; because voluntary prayers are followers of the obligatory prayers, hence he recites quietly in voluntary prayers of the day even if he is an imam. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq summary: 3/327. 'And if he leaves, etc.' meaning if he leaves the surah in one rak'ah of the first two of Maghrib or in all of the first two of 'Isha' intentionally or forgetfully, he must recite the surah (on the soundest opinion) in the last two of 'Isha' and the third of Maghrib together with them [the Fatihah] on the soundest opinion, and he gives precedence to the Fatihah then recites the surah, and this is more appropriate. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, Maraqi al-Falah: 254] 'He does not repeat it, etc.' meaning if he leaves the Fatihah in the first two, he does not repeat it in the last two according to them, and he performs prostrations of forgetfulness; because recitation of the Fatihah in the second pair is prescribed, so if he recites it once, it counts as performance because it is stronger being in its place; if he repeated it, he would contradict the prescribed. Unlike the surah, because the second pair is not its place for performance, so it may occur as make-up because it is the place for make-up. Maraqi al-Falah, Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 3/329. Its sunan: Know that leaving a sunnah does not cause invalidity nor forgetfulness prostration, but is badness (isa'ah) if done intentionally without contempt, and they said: isa'ah is lesser than makruh tahrimi. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 256] Spreading the fingers: Its manner is that he does not squeeze them completely nor spread them completely, but leaves them as they are, spread. [Maraqi al-Falah: 257] Muqarana of ihram, etc., but the condition is that his finishing of 'Allah' or 'Akbar' is not before the imam finishes them; so if he finishes saying 'Allah' with the imam or after him, and finishes saying 'Akbar' before the imam finishes it, his commencing is not valid in the most apparent transmissions (al-azhar al-riwayat), on the soundest opinion. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 257] Placing of the man, etc.: meaning he places in the described manner when he finishes the takbir for ihram without letting them hang—not as the ignorant of our time do, for they let their hands hang after the takbir of ihram = ... [page 89] Book of Prayer 88 Sunnah of Prayer. The description of placement is that he makes the palm of his right hand on the back of his left hand, forming a ring with the little finger and thumb on the wrist. And the woman places her hands on her chest without forming a ring. And the Thana' and Ta'awwudh. Then they place them, and one must know that there are four issues here: First, does he place his right hand on his left in prayer or not? Second, how does he place? Third, where does he place? Fourth, when does he place? As for the first, according to the statement of our three imams: the sunnah is that he supports his right hand on his left. As for the description of placement—the second issue—there is in the marfu' hadith the word 'taking', and in another hadith the word 'placing', and many of our teachers combine them by placing the palm of his right hand on the back of his left hand, forming a ring with the little finger and thumb on the wrist, to act upon both hadiths. As for the place of placement—the third issue—the best in our school is below the navel. Then, in the zahir al-madhhab, supporting is a sunnah of standing; and it is narrated from Muhammad that it is a sunnah for recitation, and this is evident in the one praying after the takbir. This is the fourth issue: according to Muhammad, he lets his hands hang during the Thana', and when he begins recitation, he supports; in the zahir al-riwayah, as soon as he folds his hands after the takbir, he supports al-Kifayah summary: 1/249 on the wrist and spreads three fingers on the forearm. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi) And the woman's placement: Know that the woman differs from the man in several issues: among them, she does not take her hands out of her sleeves during takbir, and she raises her hands to the level of her shoulders, and she does not spread her fingers in bowing, and she bows slightly so that she reaches the knees, not exceeding that because it is more concealing for her, and she sticks her elbows to her sides in bowing, and she sticks her belly to her thighs in prostration, and she sits mutawarrikan in every sitting by sitting on her left buttock, and she brings out both feet from the right side, and she places one thigh on the other, and she makes the right shin on the left shin, and she does not lead men, and her leading women is makruh, and the imam stands in the middle of them, and she does not recite aloud where aloud is prescribed, and al-isfar (praying at dawn in early light) is not recommended for her, and detailed enumeration negates limitation. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 259] And the Thana': Know that every person praying comes with the Thana'; the follower comes with it as long as the imam has not commenced recitation absolutely, whether he is a latecomer or a perceiver in a state of loud or quiet recitation. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 259] And Ta'awwudh i.e. the one praying says: 'I seek refuge with Allah from the accursed Shaytan'—and this is the choice of Abu 'Amr and 'Asim and Ibn Kathir, and it is the chosen view in our school; it is the statement of the majority, and it is his 'isti'adha' (seeking refuge). By this, what is chosen in al-Hidayah is weakened, that it is better to say 'Astaghfirullah'? No, 'A'udhu billah'... The objection is that the verse says 'fasta'idh' (imperative of isti'adha) and 'A'udhu' is from 'awdh' not isti'adha. The response as in Fath al-Qadir: that the word 'ista'idh' is a request for 'awdh, and his saying 'A'udhu' is a suitable response to it, but its proximity to the wording is overlooked. [Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/595]

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the sunan (recommended acts) of prayer from Nur al-Idah. It begins by stating a ruling: if a person misses reciting a surah (after Fatihah) in the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib or 'Isha', they must recite it in the remaining rak'ahs along with the Fatihah, and recite it aloud. However, if they miss the Fatihah itself, they do not repeat it in later rak'ahs but instead perform sajdat al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). The commentary then explains the jahr (loud recitation) rule: the imam must recite aloud where required and quietly where required; the individual follower can choose if they miss a prayer, but loud is better because the make-up prayer resembles the original. The passage then lists the 51 sunan of prayer, starting with raising hands for takbir (at ears for men/slave women, shoulders for free women), spreading fingers, and the follower's intention (muqarana) aligning with the imam. The commentary clarifies that leaving a sunnah is not sinful enough to require sajdat al-sahw, but it is considered 'isa'ah (blameworthy) if done intentionally without contempt, which is slightly less severe than makruh tahrimi. Detailed instructions follow for spreading fingers (neither fully closed nor fully spread) and muqarana (the follower must not finish saying 'Allahu Akbar' before the imam finishes, otherwise their prayer start is invalid in the most reliable narration). The longest section discusses placing the hands: the man places his right hand on the left (ruling from all three of our imams), with the palm on the back, forming a ring with little finger and thumb on the wrist, below the navel. The placement is a sunnah of standing (zahir al-madhhab) or according to Muhammad a sunnah of recitation. The woman places her hands on her chest without forming a ring. A separate section details women's prayer differences: they do not raise hands out of sleeves, raise to shoulders, bow less, sit mutawarrikan, do not lead men, etc. Finally, the passage covers Thana' (praise: 'Subhanaka Allahumma') and Ta'awwudh (seeking refuge). The follower recites Thana' until the imam starts reciting. For Ta'awwudh, the chosen wording is 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim', not 'Astaghfiru'? Actually, the text says the majority choose 'A'udhu', and this weakens the view in al-Hidayah that prefers 'Asta'idh'? Wait, the text says: the chosen view is 'A'udhu', and this weakens what al-Hidayah chose that it is better to say 'Asta'idh'? Actually, the text says: 'A'udhu' is the choice of many, and this weakens what al-Hidayah chose (that it is better to say 'Asta'idh'? Actually 'Asta'idh' is not mentioned; the text says 'Asta'idh'? No, the text says 'Asta'idh? Actually it says: 'أستعيذ بالله'? The translation says 'A'udhu billah...' and then 'Asta'idh'? Let's re-read: the Arabic says: 'استعادته' and 'أستعيذ' and 'أعوذ'. The point is about the wording: 'A'udhu' (أعوذ) vs. 'Ista'idh' (أستعيذ). The chosen view is 'A'udhu' because it matches the Qur'anic command 'fasta'idh' in meaning. The response from Fath al-Qadir supports 'A'udhu' as matching the command. So the commentary ends the section.

Key Terms
التحليق (al-tahlilq): Forming a ring with the little finger and thumb around the wrist when placing hands; done by men but not women.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The vivid or well-known transmission within the Hanafi school, usually from the three imams.

Checkpoint
According to the vivid narration (zahir al-riwayah), when should a man place his hands in prayer?
A) After the thana' (opening supplication)
B) Before the takbirat al-ihram
C) Immediately after the takbirat al-ihram
D) After reciting the Fatihah

Key Takeaway
Men place right hand on left below the navel with a ring, immediately after takbir, according to the preferred Hanafi view.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
7 min
Women's Prayer Distinctions in Hanafi Fiqh
List of women's prayer distinctions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key differences in women's prayer postures and adhkar according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Women's prayer differs in hand position, bowing depth, sitting posture, and they do not lead men.

The Hanafi school prescribes specific postures for women to maintain modesty. This lesson covers the differences in hand placement, raising hands, bowing, prostration, sitting, and the ruling on women leading prayer. Understanding these ensures women pray correctly according to the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify hand placement and takbir
Women do not take hands out of sleeves for takbir, raise hands to shoulder level, and place hands on chest without forming a ring.
The emphasis is on concealment.
2
Note bowing and prostration differences
Women bow minimally (just enough to touch knees) and keep elbows close to sides. In prostration, they stick belly to thighs.
This prevents exposing the body.
3
Learn the sitting posture (tawarruk)
Women sit on their left buttock with both feet out to the right side in every sitting.
Tawarruk is for all sittings for women.
4
Review leadership and recitation rulings
Women do not lead men in prayer; leading women is makruh. They do not recite aloud where jahr is prescribed, and al-isfar (early dawn) is not recommended for them.
These rulings preserve hierarchy and modesty.

لا يجهر فيما لا يجهر فيه، بل يخافت فيه حتما، وهو الصحيح؛ لأن الإمام يتحتم عليه المخافتة، فالمنفرد أولى، والمراد بقوله: "فيما يجهر جهر الإمام، وفيه إشارة إلى أنه إذا فاتته صلاة يجهر فيها يخير المنفرد كما كان في الوقت، والجهر أفضل لأن القضاء يحكي الأداء، فلا يخالفه في الوصف، وقوله: "كمتنفل بالليل" يعني به المنفرد؛ لأن النوافل أتباع الفرائض، ولهذا يخفي في نوافل النهار ولو كان إماماً. تبيين الحقائق ملخصاً: ۳۲۷/۱] ولو ترك إلخ أي ولو ترك السورة في ركعة من أوليي المغرب أو في جميع أوليي العشاء عمدا أو سهوا، قرأ السورة وجوبا على الأصح في الأخريين من العشاء، والثالثة من المغرب مع را بهما على الأصح، ويقدم الفاتحة ثم يقرأ السورة ، وهو الأشبه [حاشية الطحطاوي، مراقي الفلاح: ٢٥٤] لا يكررها إلخ أي لو ترك الفاتحة في الأوليين لا يكررها في الأخريين عندهم، ويسجد للسهو؛ لأن قراءة الفاتحة في الشفع الثاني مشروعة، فإذا قرأها مرة وقعت عن الأداء؛ لأنها أقوى لكونها في محلها، ولو كررها خالف المشروع، بخلاف السورة ، فإن الشفع الثاني ليس محلا لها أداء فجاز أن يقع قضاءً؛ لأنه محل القضاء. مراقي الفلاح، تبيين الحقائق: ۳۲۹/۱] سننها : اعلم أن ترك السنة لا يوجب فسادا ولا سهوا، بل إساءة لو عامدا غير مستخف، وقالوا: الإساءة أدون من الكراهة التحريمية. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٥٦] ونشر الأصابع: وكيفيته أن لا يضم كل الضم ولا يفرج كل التفريج، بل يتركها على حالها منشورة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٥٧] ومقارنة إحرام إلخ لكن يشترط أن لا يكون فراغه من "الله" أو من "أكبر" قبل فراغ الإمام منهما، فلو فرغ من قوله: "الله" مع الإمام أو بعده وفرغ من قوله: "أكبر" قبل فراغ الإمام منه لا يصح شروعه في أظهر الروايات، على الأصح. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٥٧] ووضع الرجل إلخ : أي يضع على الكيفية المذكورة كما فرغ من التكبير للإحرام بلا إرسال لا كما يفعله جهال زماننا، فإنهم يرسلون اليدين بعد تكبيرة الإحرام =

كتاب الصلاة
۸۸
سنن الصلاة
وصفة الوضع أن يجعل باطن كف اليمنى على ظاهر كف اليسرى محلّقا بالخنصر والإبهام على الرسغ، ووضع المرأة يديها على صدرها من غير تحليق، والثناء، والتعوذ .
ثم يضعونها، ويجب أن يعلم أن ههنا أربع مسائل: إحداها أنه هل يضع يده اليمنى على اليسرى في الصلاة أم لا؟ والثانية: كيف يضع؟ والثالثة: أين يضع؟ والرابعة متى يضع؟ أما الأولى فعلى قول علمائنا الثلاثة: السنة أن يعتمد بيده اليمنى على اليسرى، وأما صفة الوضع وهي المسألة الثانية، ففي الحديث المرفوع لفظ الأخذ، وفي حديث عليه لفظ الوضع، ويتحسن كثير من مشايخنا الجمع بينهما بأن يضع باطن كفه اليمنى على ظاهر كفه اليسرى، ويحلق بالخنصر والإبهام على الرسغ؛ ليكون عاملا بالحديثين وأما موضع الوضع، وهو الثالثة، فالأفضل عندنا تحت السرة، ثم في ظاهر المذهب الاعتماد سنة القيام، وروي عن محمد : أنه سنة للقراءة، وتبين هذا في المصلي بعد التكبير وهي المسألة الرابعة، فعند محمد مه يرسل يديه في حالة الثناء، فإذا أخذ في القراءة اعتمد، وفي ظاهر الرواية كما يكف يديه بعد التكبير يعتمد الكفاية ملخصا: ٢٤٩/١] على الرسغ ويبسط ثلاثة أصابعه على الذراع. (حاشية الطحطاوي ووضع المرأة: اعلم أن المرأة تخالف الرجل في مسائل منها هذه، ومنها أنها لا تخرج كفيها من كميها عند التكبير، وترفع يديها حذاء منكبيها، ولا تفرج أصابعها في الركوع، وتنحني في الركوع قليلاً بحيث تبلغ الركوع، فلا تزيد على ذلك؛ لأنه أستر لها، وتلزق مرفقيها بجنبيها فيه وتلزق بطنها بفخذيها في السجود، وتجلس متوركة في كل قعود بأن تجلس على أليتها اليسرى، وتخرج کلتا رجليها من الجانب الأيمن، وتضع فخذيها على بعضهما، وتجعل الساق الأيمن على الساق الأيسر، ولا تؤم الرجال، وتكره جماعتهن، ويقف الإمام وسطهن ولا تجهر في موضع الجهر، ولا يستحب في حقها الإسفار بالفجر، والتتبع ينفي الحصر. [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٥٩] والثناء: اعلم أن الثناء يأتي به كل مصل فالمقتدي يأتي به ما لم يشرع الإمام في القراءة مطلقاً، سواء كان مسبوقاً أو مدركاً في حالة الجهر أو السر. [حاشية الطحطاوي (۲۵۹] والتعوذ أي قال المصلي: أعوذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم وهو اختيار أبي عمر وعاصم وابن كثير، وهو المختار عندنا، أصحابنا؛ قول الأكثر من وهو استعادته ، وبهذا يضعف ما اختاره في "الهداية" من أن الأولى أن يقول: "أستعيذ بالله" ليوافق من لأن المذكور فيه "فاستعذ بصيغة الأمر من الاستعاذة و"أستعيذ" مضارعها فيتوافقان بخلاف "أعوذ"، فإنه من العوذ لا الاستعاذة، وجوابه كما في "فتح القدير : أن لفظ "استعذ" طلب العوذ، وقوله: "أعوذ" من مثال مطابق لمقتضاه أما قربه من اللفظ فهدر [البحر الرائق: ٥٩٥/١]
Book of Prayer... AV... Sunnah of Prayer. And if he leaves the surah in the first two of the night prayer, he recites it in the last two with the Fatihah aloud, and if he leaves the Fatihah, he does not repeat it in the last two. Section on its sunan: They are fifty-one: raising the hands for the takbir at the level of the ears for a man and a slave woman, and at the level of the shoulders for a free woman; spreading the fingers; the muqarana (alignment) of the follower's ihram with the imam's ihram; and the man placing his right hand on his left under his navel. The Fatihah aloud: He does not recite aloud where it is not recited aloud, but rather recites quietly necessarily, and this is correct; because the imam is obliged to recite quietly, so the individual is more entitled. The meaning of his statement: 'In what is recited aloud, the imam recites aloud'—and it contains an indication that if he misses a prayer in which recitation is aloud, the individual has a choice as if he were in the time, and aloud is better because the make-up resembles the performance. His statement: 'like a voluntary performer at night' means the individual; because voluntary prayers are followers of the obligatory prayers, hence he recites quietly in voluntary prayers of the day even if he is an imam. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq summary: 3/327. 'And if he leaves, etc.' meaning if he leaves the surah in one rak'ah of the first two of Maghrib or in all of the first two of 'Isha' intentionally or forgetfully, he must recite the surah (on the soundest opinion) in the last two of 'Isha' and the third of Maghrib together with them [the Fatihah] on the soundest opinion, and he gives precedence to the Fatihah then recites the surah, and this is more appropriate. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, Maraqi al-Falah: 254] 'He does not repeat it, etc.' meaning if he leaves the Fatihah in the first two, he does not repeat it in the last two according to them, and he performs prostrations of forgetfulness; because recitation of the Fatihah in the second pair is prescribed, so if he recites it once, it counts as performance because it is stronger being in its place; if he repeated it, he would contradict the prescribed. Unlike the surah, because the second pair is not its place for performance, so it may occur as make-up because it is the place for make-up. Maraqi al-Falah, Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 3/329. Its sunan: Know that leaving a sunnah does not cause invalidity nor forgetfulness prostration, but is badness (isa'ah) if done intentionally without contempt, and they said: isa'ah is lesser than makruh tahrimi. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 256] Spreading the fingers: Its manner is that he does not squeeze them completely nor spread them completely, but leaves them as they are, spread. [Maraqi al-Falah: 257] Muqarana of ihram, etc., but the condition is that his finishing of 'Allah' or 'Akbar' is not before the imam finishes them; so if he finishes saying 'Allah' with the imam or after him, and finishes saying 'Akbar' before the imam finishes it, his commencing is not valid in the most apparent transmissions (al-azhar al-riwayat), on the soundest opinion. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 257] Placing of the man, etc.: meaning he places in the described manner when he finishes the takbir for ihram without letting them hang—not as the ignorant of our time do, for they let their hands hang after the takbir of ihram = ... [page 89] Book of Prayer 88 Sunnah of Prayer. The description of placement is that he makes the palm of his right hand on the back of his left hand, forming a ring with the little finger and thumb on the wrist. And the woman places her hands on her chest without forming a ring. And the Thana' and Ta'awwudh. Then they place them, and one must know that there are four issues here: First, does he place his right hand on his left in prayer or not? Second, how does he place? Third, where does he place? Fourth, when does he place? As for the first, according to the statement of our three imams: the sunnah is that he supports his right hand on his left. As for the description of placement—the second issue—there is in the marfu' hadith the word 'taking', and in another hadith the word 'placing', and many of our teachers combine them by placing the palm of his right hand on the back of his left hand, forming a ring with the little finger and thumb on the wrist, to act upon both hadiths. As for the place of placement—the third issue—the best in our school is below the navel. Then, in the zahir al-madhhab, supporting is a sunnah of standing; and it is narrated from Muhammad that it is a sunnah for recitation, and this is evident in the one praying after the takbir. This is the fourth issue: according to Muhammad, he lets his hands hang during the Thana', and when he begins recitation, he supports; in the zahir al-riwayah, as soon as he folds his hands after the takbir, he supports al-Kifayah summary: 1/249 on the wrist and spreads three fingers on the forearm. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi) And the woman's placement: Know that the woman differs from the man in several issues: among them, she does not take her hands out of her sleeves during takbir, and she raises her hands to the level of her shoulders, and she does not spread her fingers in bowing, and she bows slightly so that she reaches the knees, not exceeding that because it is more concealing for her, and she sticks her elbows to her sides in bowing, and she sticks her belly to her thighs in prostration, and she sits mutawarrikan in every sitting by sitting on her left buttock, and she brings out both feet from the right side, and she places one thigh on the other, and she makes the right shin on the left shin, and she does not lead men, and her leading women is makruh, and the imam stands in the middle of them, and she does not recite aloud where aloud is prescribed, and al-isfar (praying at dawn in early light) is not recommended for her, and detailed enumeration negates limitation. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 259] And the Thana': Know that every person praying comes with the Thana'; the follower comes with it as long as the imam has not commenced recitation absolutely, whether he is a latecomer or a perceiver in a state of loud or quiet recitation. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 259] And Ta'awwudh i.e. the one praying says: 'I seek refuge with Allah from the accursed Shaytan'—and this is the choice of Abu 'Amr and 'Asim and Ibn Kathir, and it is the chosen view in our school; it is the statement of the majority, and it is his 'isti'adha' (seeking refuge). By this, what is chosen in al-Hidayah is weakened, that it is better to say 'Astaghfirullah'? No, 'A'udhu billah'... The objection is that the verse says 'fasta'idh' (imperative of isti'adha) and 'A'udhu' is from 'awdh' not isti'adha. The response as in Fath al-Qadir: that the word 'ista'idh' is a request for 'awdh, and his saying 'A'udhu' is a suitable response to it, but its proximity to the wording is overlooked. [Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/595]
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the sunan (recommended acts) of prayer from Nur al-Idah. It begins by stating a ruling: if a person misses reciting a surah (after Fatihah) in the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib or 'Isha', they must recite it in the remaining rak'ahs along with the Fatihah, and recite it aloud. However, if they miss the Fatihah itself, they do not repeat it in later rak'ahs but instead perform sajdat al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). The commentary then explains the jahr (loud recitation) rule: the imam must recite aloud where required and quietly where required; the individual follower can choose if they miss a prayer, but loud is better because the make-up prayer resembles the original. The passage then lists the 51 sunan of prayer, starting with raising hands for takbir (at ears for men/slave women, shoulders for free women), spreading fingers, and the follower's intention (muqarana) aligning with the imam. The commentary clarifies that leaving a sunnah is not sinful enough to require sajdat al-sahw, but it is considered 'isa'ah (blameworthy) if done intentionally without contempt, which is slightly less severe than makruh tahrimi. Detailed instructions follow for spreading fingers (neither fully closed nor fully spread) and muqarana (the follower must not finish saying 'Allahu Akbar' before the imam finishes, otherwise their prayer start is invalid in the most reliable narration). The longest section discusses placing the hands: the man places his right hand on the left (ruling from all three of our imams), with the palm on the back, forming a ring with little finger and thumb on the wrist, below the navel. The placement is a sunnah of standing (zahir al-madhhab) or according to Muhammad a sunnah of recitation. The woman places her hands on her chest without forming a ring. A separate section details women's prayer differences: they do not raise hands out of sleeves, raise to shoulders, bow less, sit mutawarrikan, do not lead men, etc. Finally, the passage covers Thana' (praise: 'Subhanaka Allahumma') and Ta'awwudh (seeking refuge). The follower recites Thana' until the imam starts reciting. For Ta'awwudh, the chosen wording is 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim', not 'Astaghfiru'? Actually, the text says the majority choose 'A'udhu', and this weakens the view in al-Hidayah that prefers 'Asta'idh'? Wait, the text says: the chosen view is 'A'udhu', and this weakens what al-Hidayah chose that it is better to say 'Asta'idh'? Actually, the text says: 'A'udhu' is the choice of many, and this weakens what al-Hidayah chose (that it is better to say 'Asta'idh'? Actually 'Asta'idh' is not mentioned; the text says 'Asta'idh'? No, the text says 'Asta'idh? Actually it says: 'أستعيذ بالله'? The translation says 'A'udhu billah...' and then 'Asta'idh'? Let's re-read: the Arabic says: 'استعادته' and 'أستعيذ' and 'أعوذ'. The point is about the wording: 'A'udhu' (أعوذ) vs. 'Ista'idh' (أستعيذ). The chosen view is 'A'udhu' because it matches the Qur'anic command 'fasta'idh' in meaning. The response from Fath al-Qadir supports 'A'udhu' as matching the command. So the commentary ends the section.

Key Terms
التورك (al-tawarruk): A sitting posture for women where she sits on her left buttock with both feet out to the right side.
الإسفار (al-isfar): Performing the Fajr prayer in early daylight (after dawn but with some light).

Key Takeaway
Women's prayer includes specific sunnah postures for modesty: hands on chest without ring, minimal bowing, tawarruk sitting, and they do not lead men.

The Ruling on Hand Placement in Prayer
States the first mas'ala: ruling on hand placement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the Hanafi ruling on placing the right hand on the left in prayer is sunnah muakkadah, and identify the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Placing the right hand on the left in prayer is a sunnah muakkadah, not wajib, based on ahad hadith.

Hand placement (al-wad') is a recommended act during prayer. The Hanafi school treats it as a sunnah, meaning it is meritorious but not obligatory. This lesson covers the first of four mas'ail: the ruling itself, and why it is not wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is placing the right hand on the left during prayer. The text says 'السنة أن يعتمد' – it is a sunnah. Understand that sunnah muakkadah is highly recommended but not obligatory.
2
Examine the dalil
The evidence comes from marfu' hadiths with the words 'الأخذ' and 'الوضع'. These are ahad hadiths, which in Hanafi usul produce zann, not certainty, hence the ruling is sunnah, not wajib or fard.
Thubut and dalala are both zanni.
3
Note the Hanafi consensus
All three founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree it is sunnah. There is no ikhtilaf within the school on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سنن الصلاة وصفة الوضع أن يجعل باطن كف اليمنى على ظاهر كف اليسرى محلّقا بالخنصر والإبهام على الرسغ، ووضع المرأة يديها على صدرها من غير تحليق، والثناء، والتعوذ . ثم يضعونها، ويجب أن يعلم أن ههنا أربع مسائل: إحداها أنه هل يضع يده اليمنى على اليسرى في الصلاة أم لا؟ والثانية: كيف يضع؟ والثالثة: أين يضع؟ والرابعة متى يضع؟ أما الأولى فعلى قول علمائنا الثلاثة: السنة أن يعتمد بيده اليمنى على اليسرى، وأما صفة الوضع وهي المسألة الثانية، ففي الحديث المرفوع لفظ الأخذ، وفي حديث عليه لفظ الوضع، ويتحسن كثير من مشايخنا الجمع بينهما بأن يضع باطن كفه اليمنى على ظاهر كفه اليسرى، ويحلق بالخنصر والإبهام على الرسغ؛ ليكون عاملا بالحديثين وأما موضع الوضع، وهو الثالثة، فالأفضل عندنا تحت السرة، ثم في ظاهر المذهب الاعتماد سنة القيام، وروي عن محمد : أنه سنة للقراءة، وتبين هذا في المصلي بعد التكبير وهي المسألة الرابعة، فعند محمد أنه يرسل يديه في حالة الثناء، فإذا أخذ في القراءة اعتمد، وفي ظاهر الرواية كما يكف يديه بعد التكبير يعتمد الكفاية ملخصا: ٢٤٩/١] على الرسغ ويبسط ثلاثة أصابعه على الذراع.
The sunnah of prayer and the description of placement: that he places the inner palm of the right hand on the back of the left hand, forming a ring with the little finger and thumb on the wrist, and the woman places her hands on her chest without forming a ring, and thana, and ta'awwudh. Then they place them. It is necessary to know that here there are four issues: first, whether he places his right hand on his left in prayer or not; second, how does he place; third, where does he place; fourth, when does he place. Regarding the first, according to the statement of our three scholars: it is sunnah to lean with the right hand on the left. Regarding the description of placement, which is the second issue, in the marfu' hadith there is the word 'taking', and in another hadith the word 'placing', and many of our mashayikh prefer to combine both by placing the inner palm of the right hand on the back of the left hand, forming a ring with the little finger and thumb on the wrist, in order to act upon both hadiths. Regarding the location of placement, which is the third, the best according to us is below the navel. Then, in the apparent madhhab, reliance is a sunnah of standing. It is related from Muhammad that it is a sunnah for recitation. And this is clarified that the praying person does it after takbir. That is the fourth issue: according to Muhammad, he releases his hands during thana, and when he begins recitation he relies. In the apparent narration, as he folds his hands after takbir, he relies on the wrist and spreads three fingers on the forearm.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah discusses the sunnah acts of prayer, specifically the placement of the hands (صفة الوضع). The author first gives a brief description: for men, the palm of the right hand is placed on the back of the left, with the little finger and thumb encircling the wrist; for women, hands are placed on the chest without circling. Then he raises four mas'ail (issues) regarding hand placement: whether to do it, how, where, and when. On the first, the Hanafi school unanimously considers it a sunnah (السنة), based on hadith evidence. On the how, the author mentions combining two hadiths by using both 'taking' and 'placing' motions. The preferred location is below the navel. On the when, there is a difference: Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that one releases the hands during thana (opening supplication) and then places them when starting qira'ah; the Zahir al-Riwayah states that they are placed immediately after takbir. The latter is the relied-upon view. The passage then lists other sunnahs like thana and ta'awwudh.

Key Terms
الوضع (al-wad'): The act of placing the hands in prayer, specifically the right hand on the left.
السنة (al-sunnah): A recommended act; omission does not incur sin or require compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Hand placement is a sunnah muakkadah; its omission does not invalidate the prayer.

The Method of Hand Placement (Sifat al-Wad')
Describes the how (sifat) of hand placement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi method of hand placement for men and women, and explain the rationale for combining two hadiths.

Core Idea
Men place right palm on left back and form a ring with thumb and little finger on wrist; women place hands on chest without a ring.

After establishing that hand placement is sunnah, the text explains the how. For men, a specific grip is described; for women, a different posture. The method combines two hadiths: one using 'taking', another using 'placing'.

Guided Path
1
Read the description for men
The inner palm of the right hand is placed on the back of the left hand, forming a ring with the little finger and thumb around the wrist.
This is called al-tahliq.
2
Read the description for women
Women place their hands on their chest without forming a ring.
Gender-specific ruling; women do not do tahliq.
3
Understand the combination of hadiths
One hadith uses 'taking' (al-akhdh), another uses 'placing' (al-wad'). The mashayikh combine both: 'placing' the palm and 'taking' with the grip on the wrist.
This harmonizes the two narrations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سنن الصلاة وصفة الوضع أن يجعل باطن كف اليمنى على ظاهر كف اليسرى محلّقا بالخنصر والإبهام على الرسغ، ووضع المرأة يديها على صدرها من غير تحليق، والثناء، والتعوذ . ثم يضعونها، ويجب أن يعلم أن ههنا أربع مسائل: إحداها أنه هل يضع يده اليمنى على اليسرى في الصلاة أم لا؟ والثانية: كيف يضع؟ والثالثة: أين يضع؟ والرابعة متى يضع؟ أما الأولى فعلى قول علمائنا الثلاثة: السنة أن يعتمد بيده اليمنى على اليسرى، وأما صفة الوضع وهي المسألة الثانية، ففي الحديث المرفوع لفظ الأخذ، وفي حديث عليه لفظ الوضع، ويتحسن كثير من مشايخنا الجمع بينهما بأن يضع باطن كفه اليمنى على ظاهر كفه اليسرى، ويحلق بالخنصر والإبهام على الرسغ؛ ليكون عاملا بالحديثين وأما موضع الوضع، وهو الثالثة، فالأفضل عندنا تحت السرة، ثم في ظاهر المذهب الاعتماد سنة القيام، وروي عن محمد : أنه سنة للقراءة، وتبين هذا في المصلي بعد التكبير وهي المسألة الرابعة، فعند محمد أنه يرسل يديه في حالة الثناء، فإذا أخذ في القراءة اعتمد، وفي ظاهر الرواية كما يكف يديه بعد التكبير يعتمد الكفاية ملخصا: ٢٤٩/١] على الرسغ ويبسط ثلاثة أصابعه على الذراع.
The sunnah of prayer and the description of placement: that he places the inner palm of the right hand on the back of the left hand, forming a ring with the little finger and thumb on the wrist, and the woman places her hands on her chest without forming a ring, and thana, and ta'awwudh. Then they place them. It is necessary to know that here there are four issues: first, whether he places his right hand on his left in prayer or not; second, how does he place; third, where does he place; fourth, when does he place. Regarding the first, according to the statement of our three scholars: it is sunnah to lean with the right hand on the left. Regarding the description of placement, which is the second issue, in the marfu' hadith there is the word 'taking', and in another hadith the word 'placing', and many of our mashayikh prefer to combine both by placing the inner palm of the right hand on the back of the left hand, forming a ring with the little finger and thumb on the wrist, in order to act upon both hadiths. Regarding the location of placement, which is the third, the best according to us is below the navel. Then, in the apparent madhhab, reliance is a sunnah of standing. It is related from Muhammad that it is a sunnah for recitation. And this is clarified that the praying person does it after takbir. That is the fourth issue: according to Muhammad, he releases his hands during thana, and when he begins recitation he relies. In the apparent narration, as he folds his hands after takbir, he relies on the wrist and spreads three fingers on the forearm.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah discusses the sunnah acts of prayer, specifically the placement of the hands (صفة الوضع). The author first gives a brief description: for men, the palm of the right hand is placed on the back of the left, with the little finger and thumb encircling the wrist; for women, hands are placed on the chest without circling. Then he raises four mas'ail (issues) regarding hand placement: whether to do it, how, where, and when. On the first, the Hanafi school unanimously considers it a sunnah (السنة), based on hadith evidence. On the how, the author mentions combining two hadiths by using both 'taking' and 'placing' motions. The preferred location is below the navel. On the when, there is a difference: Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that one releases the hands during thana (opening supplication) and then places them when starting qira'ah; the Zahir al-Riwayah states that they are placed immediately after takbir. The latter is the relied-upon view. The passage then lists other sunnahs like thana and ta'awwudh.

Key Terms
التحليق (al-tahliq): Forming a ring by circling the little finger and thumb around the wrist.
الرسغ (al-rasgh): The wrist area where the thumb and little finger are placed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how do men place their hands in prayer?
A) They place their right hand on their chest.
B) They form a ring with little finger and thumb around the wrist.
C) They keep their hands at their sides.
D) They clasp their hands together.

Key Takeaway
Men place right palm on left back and form a ring; women place hands on chest without ring.

Location and Timing of Hand Placement
Explains location and timing with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred location (below navel) and the relied-upon timing (immediately after takbir) of hand placement, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on timing.

Core Idea
The best location is below the navel, and the hands are placed immediately after takbir, not during thana – this is the mufta bihi view.

The third and fourth mas'ail concern where and when to place the hands. The Hanafi school prefers below the navel, and there is an internal difference on timing between Muhammad al-Shaybani and the Zahir al-Riwayah. This lesson clarifies both.

Guided Path
1
Identify the preferred location
The text says 'الأفضل عندنا تحت السرة' – below the navel is best. This is the established Hanafi position.
Some later Hanafis place hands above navel, but the text states under.
2
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute on timing
Muhammad al-Shaybani held that hands are placed during recitation (qira'ah), not during thana. The Zahir al-Riwayah states they are placed immediately after takbir.
Muhammad's view: hands are for recitation; others: hands are sunnah of standing.
3
Determine the mufta bihi (operative view)
The text gives weight to the Zahir al-Riwayah by saying 'في ظاهر الرواية'. This is the relied-upon position: immediate placement after takbir.

Source Text

Women's Posture and Position in Hanafi Salah
Enumeration of women's specific prayer rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight specific rulings that distinguish a woman's prayer from a man's according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A woman's prayer differs in posture, leadership, and voice for modesty.

This lesson enumerates the key differences in how women perform salah according to the Hanafi school, as recorded in Hashiat al-Tahtawi. These rulings emphasize modesty and distinct roles in congregational prayer. The list is not exhaustive but covers the most common distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Identify each difference
Read through the passage and list each distinct ruling for women: hands in takbir, raising hands, ruku', sujud, sitting, not leading men, congregation dislike, imam position, voice in jahr, isfar for Fajr.
There are eight differences explicitly mentioned, plus the concluding principle that enumeration does not exclude others.
2
Classify the hukm level
Determine whether each ruling is sunnah, makruh, or haram. Most postural differences are sunnah for modesty; not leading men is a prohibition; women's congregation is makruh tanzihi; no jahr and no isfar are sunnah.
The text uses phrases like 'لا تؤم' (does not lead) indicating prohibition, and 'تكره' (disliked) for congregation.
3
Compare with the man's ruling
For each difference, state what the man does instead. For example, man raises hands to ears, woman to shoulders; man spreads fingers in ruku', woman keeps them together; man sits iftirash, woman sits mutawarrikan.
Knowing the counterpart helps reinforce memorization.
4
Note the underlying principle
All differences serve modesty (astar) or practical gender roles. The text says 'لأنه أستر لها' (because it is more concealing for her) for ruku' bending.
Modesty is the key rationale for posture differences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووضع المرأة: اعلم أن المرأة تخالف الرجل في مسائل منها هذه، ومنها أنها لا تخرج كفيها من كميها عند التكبير، وترفع يديها حذاء منكبيها، ولا تفرج أصابعها في الركوع، وتنحني في الركوع قليلاً بحيث تبلغ الركوع، فلا تزيد على ذلك؛ لأنه أستر لها، وتلزق مرفقيها بجنبيها فيه وتلزق بطنها بفخذيها في السجود، وتجلس متوركة في كل قعود بأن تجلس على أليتها اليسرى، وتخرج كلتا رجليها من الجانب الأيمن، وتضع فخذيها على بعضهما، وتجعل الساق الأيمن على الساق الأيسر، ولا تؤم الرجال، وتكره جماعتهن، ويقف الإمام وسطهن ولا تجهر في موضع الجهر، ولا يستحب في حقها الإسفار بالفجر، والتتبع ينفي الحصر. [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٥٩]
And the placement of the woman: Know that the woman differs from the man in matters, including these: she does not bring out her palms from her sleeves at takbir, and she raises her hands level with her shoulders, and she does not spread her fingers in ruku', and she bends slightly in ruku' such that her hands reach her knees, and she does not exceed that because it is more concealing for her, and she adheres her elbows to her sides in ruku', and she adheres her belly to her thighs in sujud, and she sits mutawarrikan in every sitting by sitting on her left buttock, and she brings out both legs from the right side, and she places her thighs on each other, and she places the right shin on the left shin, and she does not lead men, and their congregation is disliked, and the imam stands in the middle of them, and she does not raise her voice in a place of raising voice, and it is not mustahabb for her to perform isfar at Fajr, and the enumeration does not preclude others.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This section from the hashiah explains the rulings specific to women in prayer. It covers differences in eight areas: 1) Hands: women do not remove hands from sleeves during takbir and raise them to shoulder level. 2) Ruku': they bend only enough for hands to reach knees and keep fingers together. 3) Sujud: they keep belly to thighs and elbows to sides. 4) Sitting: they sit mutawarrikan (on left buttock with legs out to the right). 5) Leadership: women cannot lead men and their jama'ah is makruh. 6) Imams stand in the middle when leading women. 7) No raising voice in loud prayers. 8) Isfar (delaying Fajr until clear light) is not recommended for women. The list ends with the principle that enumeration doesn't exclude other differences.

Key Terms
متوركة (mutawarrikan): A sitting posture where a woman sits on her left buttock with legs out to the right.
الإسفار (al-isar): Performing Fajr prayer in clear daylight (delay until light).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Tawarruk (on left buttock, legs out right)
B) Iftirash (on left foot)
C) Squatting
D) Cross-legged

Key Takeaway
Women in the Hanafi school have specific postures and positions in prayer to maintain modesty and distinct gender roles.

The Thamarah al-Khilaf of Ta'awwudh: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ta'awwudh with three practical outcomes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on ta'awwudh and identify the three practical differences (thamarah al-khilaf) between the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh is sunnah for recitation according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but sunnah for thana according to Abu Yusuf — three rulings change.

Understanding the intra-Hanafi dispute on ta'awwudh sharpens your ability to trace how a single difference in legal reasoning (sunnat al-qira'ah vs sunnat al-thana') cascades into multiple practical rulings. This passage from Nur al-Idah explains the positions and their consequences for the follower, the imam in Eid, and the masbuq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
What is the legal nature of ta'awwudh? Is it a sunnah attached to recitation (qira'ah) or to the opening praise (thana)?
The answer determines when and by whom it is recited.
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold it is sunnat al-qira'ah; Abu Yusuf holds it is sunnat al-thana'.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
For Abu Hanifa/Muhammad: ta'awwudh was prescribed as protection during recitation, so it is subsidiary to qira'ah. For Abu Yusuf: it is said immediately after thana, so it belongs to thana.
The reasoning is based on the purpose and position of ta'awwudh in prayer.
4
Work through the three thamarah al-khilaf
1) Follower (muqtadi): no ta'awwudh according to the majority (no qira'ah); yes according to Abu Yusuf (he recites thana). 2) First rak'ah of Eid: majority places ta'awwudh after the additional takbirs; Abu Yusuf places it after thana before takbirs. 3) Masbuq: majority recites ta'awwudh only when making up rak'ahs; Abu Yusuf recites it twice (upon joining and when making up).
These differences are practical outcomes of the core classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثناء: اعلم أن الثناء يأتي به كل مصل فالمقتدي يأتي به ما لم يشرع الإمام في القراءة مطلقاً، سواء كان مسبوقاً أو مدركاً في حالة الجهر أو السر. [حاشية الطحطاوي (۲۵۹] والتعوذ أي قال المصلي: أعوذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم وهو اختيار أبي عمر وعاصم وابن كثير، وهو المختار عندنا، أصحابنا؛ قول الأكثر من وهو استعادته ، وبهذا يضعف ما اختاره في "الهداية" من أن الأولى أن يقول: "أستعيذ بالله" ليوافق من لأن المذكور فيه "فاستعذ بصيغة الأمر من الاستعاذة و"أستعيذ" مضارعها فيتوافقان بخلاف "أعوذ"، فإنه من العوذ لا الاستعاذة، وجوابه كما في "فتح القدير : أن لفظ "استعذ" طلب العوذ، وقوله: "أعوذ" من مثال مطابق لمقتضاه أما قربه من اللفظ فهدر [البحر الرائق: ٥٩٥/١] لأنه المنقول يعني القرآن للقراءة: يعني أن التعوذ سنة القراءة، فيأتي به كل قارئ للقرآن؛ لأنه شرع لها صيانة عن وساوس الشيطان، فكان تبعا لها، وهو قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وعند أبي يوسف: هو تبع للثناء، وفائدة الخلاف في ثلاث مسائل: إحداها: أنه لا يأتي به المقتدي عندهما؛ لأنه لا قراءة عليه، ويأتي به عنده؛ لأنه يأتي بالثناء، ثانيتها: أن الإمام يأتي بالتعوذ بعد التكبيرات الزوائد في الركعة الأولى عندهما، ويأتي به الإمام والمقتدي بعد الثناء قبل التكبيرات عنده ثالثتها أن المسبوق لا يأتي به للحال ويأتي به إذا قام إلى القضاء عندهما، وعنده: يأتي به مرتين عند الدخول بعد الثناء وعند القراءة [البحر الرائق: ٥٩٩/١]
And thana: Know that thana is recited by every praying person. The follower recites it as long as the imam has not begun recitation, absolutely, whether he is a latecomer or one who caught the rak'ah, whether in loud or silent recitation. [Hashiat al-Tahtawi] And ta'awwudh: meaning that the praying person says: 'I seek refuge in Allah from the accursed Shaitan' - and this is the choice of Abu 'Amr, 'Asim, and Ibn Kathir, and it is the chosen view with us, our companions; it is the majority view. And by this is weakened what was chosen in al-Hidayah that it is better to say 'Asta'idh billah' to conform to the Quran because that which is mentioned in it is 'fa'sta'idh' with the imperative form, and 'asta'idh' is its present tense, so they correspond, unlike 'a'udh', for it is from 'audh' not 'isti'adhah'. The response to it, as in Fath al-Qadir, is that the word 'ista'idh' is a request for refuge, and his saying 'a'udh' is an example matching its requirement; but its closeness to the word is negligible. [Bahr al-Ra'iq 1:595] Because it is the transmitted meaning of the Quran. For recitation: meaning that ta'awwudh is the sunnah of recitation, so it is done by every reciter of the Quran; because it was prescribed for it as protection from the whisperings of Shaitan, so it is subsidiary to it. This is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. According to Abu Yusuf, it is subsidiary to thana. The practical difference of this dispute is in three issues: First, that the follower does not recite it according to the two of them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) because he has no recitation, but he recites it according to him (Abu Yusuf) because he recites thana. Second, that the imam recites ta'awwudh after the additional takbirs in the first rak'ah according to the two of them, and the imam and follower recite it after thana before the additional takbirs according to him. Third, that the latecomer does not recite it for the current situation but recites it when he stands to make up the missed part according to the two of them; according to him, he recites it twice: upon entering after thana and at the time of recitation. [Bahr al-Ra'iq 1:599]
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage covers two sunnan: thana (opening praise) and ta'awwudh (seeking refuge). Thana is recited by all worshippers, but the follower stops once the imam begins qira'ah. On ta'awwudh, there is a lexical preference: the majority of Hanafi scholars prefer 'A'udhu billah' over 'Asta'idh billah', contrary to al-Hidayah. The main intra-Hanafi dispute is about the legal ruling of ta'awwudh: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider it a sunnah for recitation (sunnat al-qira'ah), while Abu Yusuf considers it a sunnah for thana (sunnat al-thana'). This difference affects three practical issues: (1) whether the follower recites it (not according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; yes according to Abu Yusuf), (2) timing in the first rak'ah of Eid prayer (after additional takbirs vs before), and (3) whether a latecomer recites it once or twice.

Key Terms
الثناء (al-thana'): The opening praise recited by the worshipper after takbir, such as 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...'
التعوذ (al-ta'awwudh): The act of seeking refuge in Allah from the accursed Shaitan, usually by saying 'A'udhu billah...'
مسبوق (masbuq): A latecomer who missed part of the congregation prayer and makes it up after the imam's salam.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarah al-khilaf): The practical outcome or difference in rulings resulting from a theoretical dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), when should the imam recite ta'awwudh in the first rak'ah of Eid prayer?
A) After the additional takbirs
B) Before the additional takbirs, after thana
C) Immediately after takbirat al-ihram
D) At the beginning of the second rak'ah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that a single difference in usul (sunnat al-qira'ah vs sunnat al-thana') can produce three distinct practical rulings.

beginner
6 min
Amin, Basmalah, and Tasmi': Sunnahs of Prayer
Lists sunnah rulings for amin, basmalah, and tasmi'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for saying basmalah at the start of each rak'ah, amin after Fatiha, and tasmi' during ruku', and identify who says each according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Amin is general for all; basmalah is sunnah each rak'ah; tasmi' is for imam and munfarid, not follower.

In this lesson, we examine three sunnah practices of prayer: the basmalah at the beginning of each rak'ah, the saying of 'amin' after reciting Surah al-Fatiha, and the utterance 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' when rising from ruku'. The text from Nur al-Idah summarizes these rulings clearly.

Guided Path
1
Identify each sunnah act
The passage mentions three: tasmiyah (basmalah), ta'min (amin), and tasmi' (saying Sami'a Allahu...).
2
Determine who performs each
For basmalah, it is at the beginning of each rak'ah. For amin, it is general for all, including imam, follower, lone worshipper, and even reciter outside prayer. For tasmi', the imam and lone worshipper say it; the follower does not.
3
Understand the ruling level
All these are sunnah, not wajib.
The text uses 'yusann' in the original.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتسمية أول كل ركعة، والتأمين أطلقه فشمل الإمام والمأموم والمنفرد والقارئ خارج الصلاة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٦١] والتحميد : أي ويسن التحميد للمؤتم والمنفرد اتفاقاً، وللإمام عندهما أيضًا، ويحمد المنفرد مع التسميع، فيأتي بالتسميع حال الارتفاع، وبالتحميد حال الانخفاض، وقيل: حال الاستواء كما في "مجمع الأنهر"، وجزم به في "الدرر" وهو ظاهر الجواب وهو الصحيح. [مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي بتصرف: ٢٦١] والتسميع: أي قوله: سمع الله لمن حمده.
And tasmiyah at the beginning of every rak'ah, and amin: it is general, so it includes the imam, the follower, the one praying alone, and the reciter outside of prayer. [Maraqi al-Falah: 261] And tahmid: meaning that tahmid is sunnah for the follower and the lone worshipper unanimously, and for the imam according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) as well. The lone worshipper does hamd along with tasmi', so he recites tasmi' when rising and tahmid when lowering, and it is said: at the time of standing straight as in 'Majma' al-Anhar', and it was decided in 'al-Durar', and it is the apparent answer and it is correct. [Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiat al-Tahtawi adapted: 261] And tasmi': meaning his saying: 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage covers additional sunnan: reciting basmala at the start of each rak'ah, saying amin, saying tahmid ('Rabbana lakal hamd') after rising from ruku', and saying tasmi' ('Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'). Amin is said by all, including those outside prayer reciting Quran. Tahmid is unanimously sunnah for the follower (mu'tamm) and the lone worshipper (munfarid). There is a dispute regarding the imam: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is also sunnah for the imam (the text says 'عندهما أيضًا' meaning according to the two; Abu Hanifa's view is that the imam does not say tahmid). The passage then discusses the timing: a munfarid combines tasmi' while rising and tahmid while lowering, but the preferred view is that both are said at the moment of standing straight (i'tidal). Tasmi' is the statement said by the imam when rising from ruku'.

Key Terms
التأمين (al-ta'min): Saying 'Amin' after the Fatiha.
التسميع (al-tasmi'): Saying 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' when rising from ruku'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' (tasmi')?
A) Imam only
B) Follower only
C) Imam and munfarid
D) All

Key Takeaway
Amin, basmalah at start of each rak'ah, and tasmi' are sunnah acts in prayer, each with specific performers.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Imam's Tahmid
Details the intra-Hanafi dispute on imam's tahmid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding whether the imam says 'Rabbana lakal hamd' (tahmid) after rising from ruku', and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Tahmid is unanimously sunnah for follower and munfarid; the dispute concerns the imam, with Sahibayn considering it sunnah.

This lesson focuses on the sunnah of tahmid (saying 'Rabbana lakal hamd') after rising from ruku'. While it is agreed that the follower and lone worshipper say it, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the imam. The text from Nur al-Idah presents the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad that the imam also says it, implying Abu Hanifa's position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling level
Tahmid is saying 'Rabbana lakal hamd' after rising from ruku'. The text states it is sunnah ('yusann').
2
Determine the unanimous positions
The text says 'للمؤتم والمنفرد اتفاقاً' - it is sunnah for the follower and munfarid by consensus.
3
Locate the dispute
The text adds 'وللإمام عندهما أيضًا' - and for the imam according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) as well. This implies Abu Hanifa did not consider it sunnah for the imam.
The text does not explicitly state Abu Hanifa's view.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the imam omits tahmid, his prayer remains valid (since it's sunnah), but he misses the reward. The imam who follows Abu Hanifa would omit it; those following Sahibayn include it.
The text does not give tarjih, but later preferred views exist.

Divisions of Mufassal and Recitation Sunnah
Defines Mufassal divisions and recitation sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi division of the Mufassal surahs and apply the sunnah ruling for recitation lengths in prayer for a resident and a traveler.

Core Idea
Recite from the appropriate Mufassal section: long for Fajr/Zuhr, medium for Asr/Isha, short for Maghrib—except when it burdens the congregation.

This passage defines the Mufassal division of the Quran and the sunnah for reciting surahs after al-Fatiha in different prayers. The Hanafi school divides the Mufassal into three lengths: long, medium, and short. The ruling differs between a resident and a traveler, and an imam must consider his followers' endurance. Reciting outside the Mufassal is against the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mufassal section
The Mufassal starts from Surah al-Hujurat (49) to the end of the Quran (114).
This is the Hanafi definition.
2
Memorize the three divisions
Long (tiwal): from al-Hujurat to 'Wa as-sama dhat al-buruj' (85). Medium (awsat): from there to 'Lam yakun' (98). Short (qisar): from there to the end (114).
These boundaries are from the text and an-Niqaya.
3
State the sunnah ruling for a resident
A resident (muqim) should recite: long surahs for Fajr and Zuhr, medium for Asr and Isha, short for Maghrib.
This is the established sunnah.
4
State the ruling for a traveler
A traveler (musafir) may recite any surah he wishes; the division is only for residents.
The passage uses 'muqiman' to restrict the ruling.
5
Apply the exception for the imam
If the imam knows that reciting long surahs will burden the followers, he should avoid it.
This is a qualification (taqyid) of the general ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طوال المفصل: الطوال والقصار: بكسر أولهما جمع طويلة وقصيرة والطوال بالضم: الرجل الطويل [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٦٣] وبالفتح: المرأة الطويلة [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٦٢] والأوساط: جمع وسط بفتح السين، ما بين القصار والطوال، ولم يبين المصنف له المفصل للاختلاف فيه، والذي عليه أصحابنا أنه "الحجرات" إلى "والسماء ذات البروج" طوال ، ومنها إلى "لم يكن" أوساط، ومنها إلى آخر القرآن قصار، وبه صرح في "النقاية"؛ وسمي لكثرة الفصول فيه، وقيل: لقلة المنسوخ فيه، وأطلق فشمل الإمام والمنفرد، وأفاد أن القراءة في غير المفصل خلاف السنة. [حاشية الطحطاوي، مراقي الفلاح، البحر الرائق: ٦٤٣/١] مقيما أطلق فشمل المنفرد والإمام، وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يثقل على المقتدين بقراءته كذلك، أما إذا علم الثقل فلا يفعل ما تقدم.
The long surahs of Mufassal: 'at-tiwal' and 'al-qisar' - both with kasra on the first letter, plural of 'tawila' and 'qasira'. 'At-tiwal' (with damm on the first letter) means the tall man [Maraqi al-Falah:263]; with fatha, it means the tall woman [Hashiat al-Tahtawi:262]. And 'al-awsat' is plural of 'wasat' (with fatha on the sin), which is what is between the short and the long. The author did not define the Mufassal for him because of disagreement. What our companions hold is that from 'Al-Hujurat' to 'Wa as-sama dhat al-buruj' are long (tiwal), from there to 'Lam yakun' are medium (awsat), and from there to the end of the Quran are short (qisar). And this is clearly stated in 'an-Niqaya'. It is called Mufassal because of the many divisions in it, or it is said because of the few abrogated verses in it. And it (the ruling) is general, so it includes the imam and the lone worshipper. And it indicates that recitation in other than the Mufassal is contrary to the sunnah. [Hashiat al-Tahtawi, Maraqi al-Falah, Bahr ar-Ra'iq 1:643]. 'Muqiman' is general, so it includes the lone worshipper and the imam, but it is qualified by when he does not burden the followers with such recitation. If he knows of the burden, he should not do what preceded.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage discusses the sunnah of reciting surahs after al-Fatiha in different prayers. The Quran is divided into long (tiwal), medium (awsat), and short (qisar) surahs. The Mufassal section starts from Surah al-Hujurat (49) to the end of the Quran. Within Mufassal, the long surahs are from al-Hujurat to 'Wa as-sama dhat al-buruj' (85), medium from there to 'Lam yakun' (98), and short from there to the end. For a resident (muqim), the sunnah is to recite long during Fajr and Zuhr, medium during Asr and Isha, and short during Maghrib. A traveler may recite any surah he wishes. However, if the imam knows that reciting long surahs will burden the followers, he should avoid it. Recitation outside the Mufassal is considered contrary to the sunnah.

Key Terms
المفصل (al-mufassal): The section of the Quran from Surah al-Hujurat (49) to the end.
طوال (tiwal): The long surahs of Mufassal (49-85).
أوساط (awsat): The medium surahs of Mufassal (85-98).
قصار (qisar): The short surahs of Mufassal (98-114).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) From al-Hujurat to 'Wa as-sama dhat al-buruj'

D) From at-Tariq to al-Fatiha

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies Mufassal into three lengths and prescribes specific recitation lengths for each prayer; recitation outside Mufassal is against the sunnah.
