Ta'awwudh: Sunnah of Recitation vs. Sunnah of Prayer
Dispute within Hanafi school on ta'awwudh's subsidiary status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the status of ta'awwudh and identify the three practical consequences (thamarah) of the dispute.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh is sunnah of recitation, not the prayer; Abu Yusuf's opposing view changes three rulings.

The act of seeking refuge (ta'awwudh) before Quran recitation is a sunnah, but its placement in the prayer structure is disputed among the early Hanafi masters. This lesson unpacks the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on one side and Abu Yusuf on the other, focusing on how the difference affects the follower, the imam in Eid, and the latecomer.

Guided Path
1
State the main Hanafi position
Identify the ruling that ta'awwudh is a sunnah of recitation (sunnat al-qira'ah) because it was legislated to protect against Satan's whispers during recitation.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Identify the opposing view
Abu Yusuf considers ta'awwudh subsidiary to the thana' (opening praise), making it a sunnah of the prayer itself.
His rationale: it is part of the opening of prayer, not just recitation.
3
Analyse the three thamarah al-khilaf
Work through the three scenarios where the difference produces distinct rulings: (1) the follower, (2) the imam in Eid, (3) the latecomer. For each, state the ruling according to both views.
These are the practical consequences that a jurist must know.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as recorded in the zahir al-riwayah.
This is implied by the citation of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and other commentaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المصلي بالكسر للقراءة: يعني أن التعوذ سنة القراءة، فيأتي به كل قارئ للقرآن؛ لأنه شرع لها صيانة عن وساوس الشيطان، فكان تبعا لها، وهو قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وعند أبي يوسف: هو تبع للثناء، وفائدة الخلاف في ثلاث مسائل: إحداها: أنه لا يأتي به المقتدي عندهما؛ لأنه لا قراءة عليه، ويأتي به عنده؛ لأنه يأتي بالثناء، ثانيتها: أن الإمام يأتي بالتعوذ بعد التكبيرات الزوائد في الركعة الأولى عندهما، ويأتي به الإمام والمقتدي بعد الثناء قبل التكبيرات عنده ثالثتها أن المسبوق لا يأتي به للحال ويأتي به إذا قام إلى القضاء عندهما، وعنده: يأتي به مرتين عند الدخول بعد الثناء وعند القراءة [البحر الرائق: ٥٩٩/١] والتأمين أطلقه فشمل الإمام والمأموم والمنفرد والقارئ خارج الصلاة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٦١] والتحميد : أي ويسن التحميد للمؤتم والمنفرد اتفاقاً، وللإمام عندهما أيضًا، ويحمد المنفرد مع التسميع، فيأتي بالتسميع حال الارتفاع، وبالتحميد حال الانخفاض، وقيل: حال الاستواء كما في "مجمع الأنهر"، وجزم به في "الدرر" وهو ظاهر الجواب وهو الصحيح. [مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي بتصرف: ٢٦١] والتسميع: أي قوله: سمع الله لمن حمده. طوال المفصل: الطوال والقصار: بكسر أولهما جمع طويلة وقصيرة والطوال بالضم: الرجل الطويل مراقي الفلاح: ٢٦٣] وبالفتح: المرأة الطويلة [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٦٢] والأوساط: جمع وسط بفتح السين، ما بين القصار والطوال، ولم يبين المصنف له المفصل للاختلاف فيه، والذي عليه أصحابنا أنه "الحجرات" إلى "والسماء ذات البروج" طوال ، ومنها إلى "لم يكن أوساط، ومنها إلى آخر القرآن قصار، وبه صرح في "النقاية"؛ وسمي لكثرة الفصول فيه، وقيل: لقلة المنسوخ فيه، وأطلق فشمل الإمام والمنفرد، وأفاد أن القراءة في غير المفصل خلاف السنة. [حاشية الطحطاوي، مراقي الفلاح، البحر الرائق: ٦٤٣/١] مقيما أطلق فشمل المنفرد والإمام، وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يثقل على المقتدين بقراءته كذلك، أما إذا علم الصلاة من الثقل فلا يفعل ما تقدم.
The praying person [reciter] for recitation: meaning that the ta'awwudh is a sunnah of recitation, so every reciter of the Quran performs it because it was legislated for it as a protection from the whispers of Satan, thus it is subsidiary to it. This is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. According to Abu Yusuf: it is subsidiary to the thana'. The benefit of the difference is in three issues: First: the follower does not perform it according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) because there is no recitation upon him, but he performs it according to him (Abu Yusuf) because he performs the thana'. Second: the imam performs the ta'awwudh after the extra takbirs in the first rak'ah according to them, and the imam and follower perform it after the thana' before the takbirs according to him. Third: the latecomer does not perform it immediately and performs it when he rises to complete (the missed rak'ahs) according to them, and according to him: he performs it twice: at entry after thana' and at recitation. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/599] And 'al-tamin': he (the author) mentioned it in absolute terms so it includes the imam, the follower, the individual, and the reciter outside prayer. [Maraqi al-Falah: 261] And 'al-tahmid': meaning it is sunnah for the follower and individual by agreement, and for the imam according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) as well. The individual combines tasmi' and tahmid, so he says tasmi' during rising and tahmid during descending. It is said: during standing as in 'Majma' al-Anhur', and it is affirmed in 'al-Durar', and it is the apparent answer and it is correct. [Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiya al-Tahtawi adapted: 261] And 'al-tasmi'': meaning his saying: 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'. 'Tiwal al-Mufassal': 'al-tiwal' and 'al-qisar' with kasra on the first letter, plurals of 'tawila' and 'qasira'. 'al-tiwal' with damm: the tall man [Maraqi al-Falah: 263], and with fatha: the tall woman [Hashiya al-Tahtawi: 262]. And 'al-awsat': plural of 'wasat' with fatha on the seen, meaning between the short and long. The author did not define 'al-mufassal' due to differences. What our companions hold is that from 'al-Hujurat' to 'wa al-sama'i dhat al-buruj' are long, from there to 'lam yakun' are medium, and from there to the end of the Quran are short. This is stated explicitly in 'al-Niqayah'. It is named for the many divisions in it, or for the few abrogated parts. He (the author) mentioned it absolutely so it includes the imam and individual. And it indicates that recitation outside the mufassal is against the sunnah. [Hashiya al-Tahtawi, Maraqi al-Falah, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/643] 'Muqiman' (resident) he mentioned absolutely so it includes the individual and imam, and it is restricted to when he does not burden the followers with his recitation thus. But if he knows burden, he does not do what was mentioned.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the sunan of recitation in prayer, from the commentary of Nur al-Idah. It begins with the ruling on ta'awwudh (seeking refuge with Allah before reciting). The author clarifies that ta'awwudh is sunnah for every reciter, as it was prescribed to protect against Satan's whispers. However, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider it subsidiary to recitation (qira'ah), while Abu Yusuf considers it subsidiary to the thana' (opening praise). The practical consequences (thamarah) are three: (1) In congregational prayer, a follower (muqtadi) does not recite in the Hanafi school, so according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the follower does not say ta'awwudh since he doesn't recite; but according to Abu Yusuf, he says it because he says thana'. (2) In the first rak'ah of Eid prayer (where there are extra takbirs), the imam says ta'awwudh after the extra takbirs according to the first two, but after thana' before the takbirs according to Abu Yusuf. (3) For a latecomer (masbuq), the first two say he does not say ta'awwudh when joining but says it when he rises to complete the missed rak'ahs; Abu Yusuf says he says it twice: initially after thana' and later when reciting. Next, 'al-tamin' (saying Amin) is sunnah for all including the reciter outside prayer. 'Al-tahmid' (saying Rabbana laka al-hamd) is sunnah for follower and individual unanimously, and for the imam according to the Sahibayn. The individual combines tasmi' (Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah) when rising and tahmid when descending; some say during standing. 'Al-tasmi'' is defined as the phrase 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'. The passage then defines 'tiwal al-mufassal' (long surahs of the mufassal section): the long surahs are from Surah al-Hujurat to Surah al-Buruj; medium from there to Surah al-Bayyinah; short from there to end. This classification determines which surahs are recited in each prayer: long surahs in Fajr and Zuhr, medium in Asr and Isha, short in Maghrib for a resident. A traveler may recite any surah. Recitation from outside the mufassal is against sunnah. The resident's recitation is restricted to not burdening the followers; if it causes hardship, it's avoided.

Key Terms
التعوذ (al-ta'awwudh): Seeking refuge with Allah, i.e., saying 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim'. Here, it is considered a sunnah of recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, when does the latecomer (masbuq) perform ta'awwudh?
A) Immediately upon joining the prayer
B) When he rises to complete the missed rak'ahs
C) Both when joining and when reciting
D) He does not perform it at all

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds ta'awwudh as a sunnah of recitation; the intra-madhhab difference with Abu Yusuf produces three distinct practical outcomes.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Amin, Tahmid, Tasmi', and Classification of Mufassal Suwar
Explanation of sunnan and mufassal classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah rulings for amin, tahmid, tasmi', and classify the mufassal suwar according to the Hanafi madhhab.

Core Idea
The sunnah acts of recitation are fixed; the mufassal is divided into long, medium, and short surahs for proper recitation in each prayer.

Beyond ta'awwudh, the prayer includes other sunnan of recitation: saying amin after al-Fatiha, praising upon rising (tahmid), and declaring 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' (tasmi'). Additionally, the Hanafi school specifies which surahs to recite in each prayer based on the mufassal classification.

Guided Path
1
List the four sunnan of recitation
Identify ta'awwudh (already covered), ta'min (amin), tahmid (Rabbana laka al-hamd), and tasmi' (Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah).
Ta'awwudh was covered in the previous lesson; here we focus on the other three.
2
State the rulings for each
Amin is sunnah for all reciters including outside prayer. Tahmid is sunnah for follower and individual by agreement, and for the imam according to the Sahibayn. Tasmi' is said by the imam and individual when rising from ruku or bowing.
The text also mentions the combination for an individual: tasmi' while rising, tahmid while descending or while standing.
3
Classify the mufassal suwar
The mufassal section of the Quran is divided into three categories: long (from al-Hujurat to al-Buruj), medium (from there to al-Bayyinah), and short (from al-Bayyinah to end).
This classification determines which surahs to recite in each obligatory prayer.
4
Apply to prayer recitation
A resident (muqim) should recite long mufassal in Fajr and Zuhr, medium in Asr and Isha, and short in Maghrib. A traveller has more flexibility. Recitation outside the mufassal is against the sunnah.
The recitation should not burden the followers; if it causes hardship, shorter surahs are recommended.

Source Text

المصلي بالكسر للقراءة: يعني أن التعوذ سنة القراءة، فيأتي به كل قارئ للقرآن؛ لأنه شرع لها صيانة عن وساوس الشيطان، فكان تبعا لها، وهو قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وعند أبي يوسف: هو تبع للثناء، وفائدة الخلاف في ثلاث مسائل: إحداها: أنه لا يأتي به المقتدي عندهما؛ لأنه لا قراءة عليه، ويأتي به عنده؛ لأنه يأتي بالثناء، ثانيتها: أن الإمام يأتي بالتعوذ بعد التكبيرات الزوائد في الركعة الأولى عندهما، ويأتي به الإمام والمقتدي بعد الثناء قبل التكبيرات عنده ثالثتها أن المسبوق لا يأتي به للحال ويأتي به إذا قام إلى القضاء عندهما، وعنده: يأتي به مرتين عند الدخول بعد الثناء وعند القراءة [البحر الرائق: ٥٩٩/١] والتأمين أطلقه فشمل الإمام والمأموم والمنفرد والقارئ خارج الصلاة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٦١] والتحميد : أي ويسن التحميد للمؤتم والمنفرد اتفاقاً، وللإمام عندهما أيضًا، ويحمد المنفرد مع التسميع، فيأتي بالتسميع حال الارتفاع، وبالتحميد حال الانخفاض، وقيل: حال الاستواء كما في "مجمع الأنهر"، وجزم به في "الدرر" وهو ظاهر الجواب وهو الصحيح. [مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي بتصرف: ٢٦١] والتسميع: أي قوله: سمع الله لمن حمده. طوال المفصل: الطوال والقصار: بكسر أولهما جمع طويلة وقصيرة والطوال بالضم: الرجل الطويل مراقي الفلاح: ٢٦٣] وبالفتح: المرأة الطويلة [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٦٢] والأوساط: جمع وسط بفتح السين، ما بين القصار والطوال، ولم يبين المصنف له المفصل للاختلاف فيه، والذي عليه أصحابنا أنه "الحجرات" إلى "والسماء ذات البروج" طوال ، ومنها إلى "لم يكن أوساط، ومنها إلى آخر القرآن قصار، وبه صرح في "النقاية"؛ وسمي لكثرة الفصول فيه، وقيل: لقلة المنسوخ فيه، وأطلق فشمل الإمام والمنفرد، وأفاد أن القراءة في غير المفصل خلاف السنة. [حاشية الطحطاوي، مراقي الفلاح، البحر الرائق: ٦٤٣/١] مقيما أطلق فشمل المنفرد والإمام، وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يثقل على المقتدين بقراءته كذلك، أما إذا علم الصلاة من الثقل فلا يفعل ما تقدم.
The praying person [reciter] for recitation: meaning that the ta'awwudh is a sunnah of recitation, so every reciter of the Quran performs it because it was legislated for it as a protection from the whispers of Satan, thus it is subsidiary to it. This is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. According to Abu Yusuf: it is subsidiary to the thana'. The benefit of the difference is in three issues: First: the follower does not perform it according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) because there is no recitation upon him, but he performs it according to him (Abu Yusuf) because he performs the thana'. Second: the imam performs the ta'awwudh after the extra takbirs in the first rak'ah according to them, and the imam and follower perform it after the thana' before the takbirs according to him. Third: the latecomer does not perform it immediately and performs it when he rises to complete (the missed rak'ahs) according to them, and according to him: he performs it twice: at entry after thana' and at recitation. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/599] And 'al-tamin': he (the author) mentioned it in absolute terms so it includes the imam, the follower, the individual, and the reciter outside prayer. [Maraqi al-Falah: 261] And 'al-tahmid': meaning it is sunnah for the follower and individual by agreement, and for the imam according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) as well. The individual combines tasmi' and tahmid, so he says tasmi' during rising and tahmid during descending. It is said: during standing as in 'Majma' al-Anhur', and it is affirmed in 'al-Durar', and it is the apparent answer and it is correct. [Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiya al-Tahtawi adapted: 261] And 'al-tasmi'': meaning his saying: 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'. 'Tiwal al-Mufassal': 'al-tiwal' and 'al-qisar' with kasra on the first letter, plurals of 'tawila' and 'qasira'. 'al-tiwal' with damm: the tall man [Maraqi al-Falah: 263], and with fatha: the tall woman [Hashiya al-Tahtawi: 262]. And 'al-awsat': plural of 'wasat' with fatha on the seen, meaning between the short and long. The author did not define 'al-mufassal' due to differences. What our companions hold is that from 'al-Hujurat' to 'wa al-sama'i dhat al-buruj' are long, from there to 'lam yakun' are medium, and from there to the end of the Quran are short. This is stated explicitly in 'al-Niqayah'. It is named for the many divisions in it, or for the few abrogated parts. He (the author) mentioned it absolutely so it includes the imam and individual. And it indicates that recitation outside the mufassal is against the sunnah. [Hashiya al-Tahtawi, Maraqi al-Falah, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/643] 'Muqiman' (resident) he mentioned absolutely so it includes the individual and imam, and it is restricted to when he does not burden the followers with his recitation thus. But if he knows burden, he does not do what was mentioned.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the sunan of recitation in prayer, from the commentary of Nur al-Idah. It begins with the ruling on ta'awwudh (seeking refuge with Allah before reciting). The author clarifies that ta'awwudh is sunnah for every reciter, as it was prescribed to protect against Satan's whispers. However, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider it subsidiary to recitation (qira'ah), while Abu Yusuf considers it subsidiary to the thana' (opening praise). The practical consequences (thamarah) are three: (1) In congregational prayer, a follower (muqtadi) does not recite in the Hanafi school, so according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the follower does not say ta'awwudh since he doesn't recite; but according to Abu Yusuf, he says it because he says thana'. (2) In the first rak'ah of Eid prayer (where there are extra takbirs), the imam says ta'awwudh after the extra takbirs according to the first two, but after thana' before the takbirs according to Abu Yusuf. (3) For a latecomer (masbuq), the first two say he does not say ta'awwudh when joining but says it when he rises to complete the missed rak'ahs; Abu Yusuf says he says it twice: initially after thana' and later when reciting. Next, 'al-tamin' (saying Amin) is sunnah for all including the reciter outside prayer. 'Al-tahmid' (saying Rabbana laka al-hamd) is sunnah for follower and individual unanimously, and for the imam according to the Sahibayn. The individual combines tasmi' (Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah) when rising and tahmid when descending; some say during standing. 'Al-tasmi'' is defined as the phrase 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'. The passage then defines 'tiwal al-mufassal' (long surahs of the mufassal section): the long surahs are from Surah al-Hujurat to Surah al-Buruj; medium from there to Surah al-Bayyinah; short from there to end. This classification determines which surahs are recited in each prayer: long surahs in Fajr and Zuhr, medium in Asr and Isha, short in Maghrib for a resident. A traveler may recite any surah. Recitation from outside the mufassal is against sunnah. The resident's recitation is restricted to not burdening the followers; if it causes hardship, it's avoided.

Key Terms
التأمين (al-ta'min): Saying 'Amin' after al-Fatiha. The text states it includes imam, follower, individual, and reciter outside prayer.
طوال المفصل (tiwal al-mufassal): The long surahs of the mufassal section of the Quran, defined here as from Surah al-Hujurat to Surah al-Buruj.
التحميد (al-tahmid): Saying 'Rabbana laka al-hamd' after rising from ruku. It is sunnah for follower, individual, and imam according to the Sahibayn.
التسميع (al-tasmi'): Saying 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' when rising from ruku. It is sunnah for imam and individual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Surah al-Hujurat
B) Surah al-Buruj
C) Surah al-Tariq
D) Surah al-Ikhlas

Key Takeaway
Amin, tahmid, and tasmi' are sunnah for all reciters, and the mufassal classification guides the recommended surahs for each prayer.

Sunnahs of Prayer Actions: Standing, Bowing, Prostration, and Tashahhud
Listing and commentary on sunnah acts during standing, bowing, prostration, and sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnah acts of prayer from standing to tashahhud and explain the Hanafi ruling on pointing the index finger during tashahhud.

Core Idea
The sunnah acts of prayer perfect the salah; the pointing in tashahhud is a confirmed sunnah despite internal Hanafi ikhtilaf.

This lesson continues the enumeration of sunan al-salat from Nur al-Idah. It details the recommended postures and actions in ruku', sujud, and sitting, and concludes with a notable intra-madhhab dispute on whether to point the index finger during tashahhud. Understanding these sunnan helps perfect one's prayer and appreciate the depth of Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence of sunnah acts
The passage lists sunan in order: elongating first rak'ah, ruku' sunan, sujud sunan, sitting sunan. List them.
2
Distinguish male and female postures
Note the differences: spreading fingers, distancing belly, tawarruk for women.
3
Examine the ikhtilaf on pointing
Read the discussion on whether to point with the index finger. Identify the two positions and their proofs.
The ikhtilaf is intra-Hanafi.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
Understand why the pointing view is preferred in later Hanafi works like Fath al-Qadir.
This is the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإطالة الأولى في الفجر فقط، وتكبيرة الركوع، وتسبيحه ثلاثا، وأخذ ركبتيه بيديه، حال الركوع وتفريج أصابعه والمرأة لا تفرجها، ونصب ساقيه وبسط ظهره، وتسوية رأسه بعجزه، حال الركوع وقت الركوع مؤخرته والرفع من الركوع، والقيام بعده مطمئنا، ووضع ركبتيه ثم يديه ثم وجهه للسجود، أي ابتداء ويبدأ بوضع الأنف وعكسه للنهوض، وتكبير السجود، وتكبير الرفع منه، وكون السجود بين كفيه، القيام وتسبيحه ثلاثا، ومجافاة الرجل بطنه عن فخذيه ومرفقيه عن جنبيه، وذراعيه عن الأرض، وانخفاض المرأة، ولزقها بطنها ،بفخذيها ،والقومة والجلسة بين السجدتين، يعني تمامها ووضع اليدين على الفخذين فيما بين السجدتين كحالة التشهد، وافتراش رجله حال الجلسة اليسرى ونصب اليمنى، وتورك المرأة، والإشارة في الصحيح بالمسبحة عند الشهادة السبابة من اليمني فقط. وإطالة الأولى إلخ بها جرى التوارث من لدن رسول الله الله إلى يومنا هذا، وفيه إعانة للناس على إدراك الجماعة. [العناية: ۲۹۲/۱] فقط إشارة إلى قول محمد: "أحب إلي أن يطول الأولى في كل الصلوات". وتكره إطالة الثانية على الأولى اتفاقا بما فوق ،آيتين وفي النوافل الأمر أسهل مراقي الفلاح ٢٦٤] بعجزه: كرجل وكتف وسكون الجيم مع تثليث العين. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٦٦] وعكسه للنهوض [أي عكس ما ذكر للسجود بأن يرفع وجهه ثم يديه ثم ركبتيه إذا لم يكن به عذر، أما إذا كان ضعيفاً، أو لابس خف، يفعل ما استطاع مراقي الفلاح: ٢٦٧] وتورك : التورك: أن تجلس على أليتها، وتضع الفخذ، وتخرج رجلها من تحت وركها اليمنى مراقي الفلاح: ٢٦٩] في الصحيح: يقابله ما يروى من أنه لا يشير بالسبابة عند الشهادتين وهو قول كثير من المشايخ وفي "الولوالجية" و"التجنيس": وعليه الفتوى، ورجح في "فتح القدير القول بالإشارة، وأنه مروي عن أبي حنيفة كما قال محمد، فالقول بعدمها مخالف للرواية والدراية، رواها في "صحيح مسلم" من فعله ، وفي "المجتبى": لما اتفقت الروايات عن أصحابنا جميعا في كونها سنة، وكذا الكوفيين والمدنيين، وكثرة الأخبار والآثار كان العمل بها أولى. [البحر الرائق بتصرف] بالمسبحة سميت بذلك؛ لأنه يشار بها في التوحيد، وهو تسبيح أي تنزيه عن الشركاء، ويقال لها: السبابة أيضا؛ لأنه يشار بها عند السب؛ وخصت بذلك لأن لها اتصالا بنباط القلب . [ مراقي الفلاح، حاشية الطحطاوي بتصرف: ٢٦٩]
And elongating the first (rak'ah) only in Fajr, and the takbir of ruku', and its tasbih three times, and taking his knees with his hands while in ruku', and spreading his fingers – and a woman does not spread them – and straightening his shanks and spreading his back, and leveling his head with his buttocks while in ruku', and rising from ruku', and standing after it with tranquility, and placing his knees then his hands then his face for prostration, meaning beginning, and he begins by placing the nose, and the reverse for rising, and the takbir of sujud, and the takbir of rising from it, and that the prostration is between his hands, and its tasbih three times, and the man distancing his belly from his thighs and his elbows from his sides and his forearms from the ground, and the woman lowering and sticking her belly to her thighs, and the standing (after ruku') and the sitting between the two prostrations, meaning completing them, and placing the hands on the thighs during the sitting between the two prostrations like the state of tashahhud, and spreading his left leg (while sitting) and raising the right, and the woman sitting in tawarruk, and the gesture in the correct (view) with the index finger during the testimony (tashahhud), the index finger of the right hand only. And elongating the first (rak'ah) etc. – by this practice has been transmitted from the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) to our day, and it helps people to catch the congregation. [al-'Inayah: 1/292] 'Only' is an indication of Muhammad's saying: 'I prefer that he lengthen the first in all prayers.' And it is disliked to lengthen the second over the first by consensus if more than two verses, and in supererogatory prayers the matter is easier. [Maraqi al-Falah: 264] 'Bi-'ajzihi': like a man's [buttocks] and shoulder, with sukun on the jim and three vowels on the 'ayn. [Hashiya al-Tahtawi: 266] And its reverse for rising [meaning the opposite of what was mentioned for prostration: he raises his face then his hands then his knees if there is no excuse; if he is weak or wearing socks, he does what he can. Maraqi al-Falah: 267] And 'tawarruk': al-tawarruk is that she sits on her buttocks, places the thigh, and brings her leg out from under her right thigh. [Maraqi al-Falah: 269] 'fi al-sahih': what is transmitted that he does not point with the index finger at the two shahadahs is opposite to it, and this is the saying of many mashayikh. In 'al-Walwalijiyya' and 'al-Tajnish': and upon it is the fatwa. But in 'Fath al-Qadir' the saying of pointing is preferred, and it is narrated from Abu Hanifa as Muhammad said, so the saying of not pointing opposes the riwaya and diraya; it is narrated in Sahih Muslim from his action. And in 'al-Mujtaba': since the narrations from all our companions agree on it being a sunnah, as well as the Kufans and Madinans, and the abundance of traditions and athar, acting upon it is more appropriate. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq adapted] 'al-musabbiha' is named thus because one points with it in tawhid (declaring Allah's oneness), and it is called 'al-sabbaba' also because one points with it at cursing; and it is specified because it has connection to the heart. [Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiya al-Tahtawi adapted: 269]
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage continues the enumeration of sunan al-salat (sunnahs of prayer) from Nur al-Idah. It lists the sunnah acts in order of the prayer sequence. Starting with elongating the first rak'ah specifically in Fajr prayer, although Imam Muhammad prefers it in all prayers. It is disliked to lengthen the second rak'ah over the first. Then the takbir for ruku' and tasbih three times in ruku'. The man spreads his fingers when grasping his knees; the woman does not. In ruku', he straightens his shanks, spreads his back, and levels his head with his buttocks. After ruku', he rises and stands with tranquility. For prostration, he places knees, then hands, then face (starting with nose) to the ground. Rising from sujud is the reverse. The prostration is between the hands, and tasbih three times. The man distances his belly from his thighs, elbows from sides, forearms from ground; the woman lowers and sticks her belly to thighs. The sitting between the two prostrations is completed by placing hands on thighs like tashahhud. The man sits with left leg spread, right foot erect; the woman sits in tawarruk (on her buttocks with leg out). The final sunnah is the gesture with the index finger during tashahhud. This is a point of ikhtilaf: many mashayikh say no pointing, but the preponderant view (especially from Fath al-Qadir) is to point, as it is sunnah from the Prophet's practice and narrated from Abu Hanifa. Pointing is recommended as it is a sign of tawhid.

Key Terms
التورك (al-tawarruk): A sitting posture for women in prayer: sitting on the left buttock with the legs brought out from under the right thigh.
المسبحة (al-musabbiha): The index finger, called 'musabbiha' because it points in declaring Allah's oneness (tasbih).
القومة (al-qawma): Standing after ruku' (i'tidal) with tranquility, considered a sunnah in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a woman's sitting posture in prayer?
A) She sits like a man with iftirash
B) She sits in tawarruk on her buttocks with leg out
C) She sits cross-legged
D) She does not sit at all

Key Takeaway
The sunnah acts of prayer, including the pointing in tashahhud, are confirmed practices that perfect the salah, and the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is to point.

Sunnah Acts of Prayer and the Finger Pointing Dispute
List of sunnah acts with explanatory glosses and an intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnah acts of prayer according to the Hanafi school, explain the gender-specific rulings, and state the mufta bihi position on pointing the finger during tashahhud.

Core Idea
The sunnah acts perfect the prayer; knowing them elevates worship from valid to excellent.

Prayer has many voluntary components that complete its form. This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates these sunnah acts, providing a concise checklist for the worshipper. Additionally, it clarifies an important intra-madhhab dispute about pointing the index finger during tashahhud, affirming the relied-upon position. Mastery of these sunnan ensures your prayer reflects the Prophetic model as transmitted in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
Go through each item in the list. Determine whether it relates to posture (e.g., ruku, sujud), recitation (e.g., takbir, tasbih), or positioning (e.g., finger separation). Note that each is a sunnah, not fard or wajib.
Use the list as a memorization anchor; you are not expected to recall every detail immediately, but to know where to look.
2
Apply gender-specific differences
Note where the text distinguishes between men and women. Men separate their fingers in ruku, distance their arms from the ground in sujud, and spread the left foot while erecting the right. Women do not separate fingers, keep limbs close, and sit in tawarruk.
These differences are based on the principle of modesty and concealment.
3
Analyze the finger pointing dispute
The text presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. Some earlier mashayikh held that one should not point, but the mufta bihi position is to point with the index finger (al-musabbiha) when saying 'la ilaha' and lower it when saying 'illa Allah'. This is supported by hadith and the practice of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
The dispute is resolved by later authorities like the author of Fath al-Qadir and al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
4
Understand recitation options in latter rak'ahs
The text clarifies that after the first two rak'ahs, one may choose to recite al-Fatiha, perform tasbih, or remain silent. The zahir al-riwayah gives this choice, though some early scholars said recitation is wajib.
This applies to the third rak'ah of Maghrib and the last two of four-rak'ah prayers, not just the 'first two' literally.
5
Differentiate the rulings on salawat
The gloss classifies sending blessings upon the Prophet into six categories: fard (once in a lifetime), wajib (upon hearing his name, on kifayah), sunnah (in the final sitting), mustahabb (any time), makruh (during prayer except in final sitting), and haram (in impermissible contexts).
This shows how the same act can have different rulings depending on the context.

سنن الصلاة وإطالة الأولى في الفجر فقط، وتكبيرة الركوع، وتسبيحه ثلاثا، وأخذ ركبتيه بيديه، حال الركوع وتفريج أصابعه والمرأة لا تفرجها، ونصب ساقيه وبسط ظهره، وتسوية رأسه بعجزه، حال الركوع وقت الركوع مؤخرته والرفع من الركوع، والقيام بعده مطمئنا، ووضع ركبتيه ثم يديه ثم وجهه للسجود، أي ابتداء ويبدأ بوضع الأنف وعكسه للنهوض، وتكبير السجود، وتكبير الرفع منه، وكون السجود بين كفيه، القيام وتسبيحه ثلاثا، ومجافاة الرجل بطنه عن فخذيه ومرفقيه عن جنبيه، وذراعيه عن أي مباعدته الأرض، وانخفاض المرأة، ولزقها بطنها بفخذيها، والقومة والجلسة بين السجدتين، يعني تمامها ووضع اليدين على الفخذين فيما بين السجدتين كحالة التشهد، وافتراش رجله حال الجلسة اليسرى ونصب اليمنى، وتورك المرأة، والإشارة في الصحيح بالمسبحة عند الشهادة الشهادة السبابة من اليمني فقط وإطالة الأولى إلخ بها جرى التوارث من لدن رسول الله الله إلى يومنا هذا، وفيه إعانة للناس على إدراك الجماعة. [البحر الرائق بتصرف] بالمسبحة سميت بذلك؛ لأنه يشار بها في التوحيد، وهو تسبيح أي تنزيه عن الشركاء، ويقال لها: السبابة أيضا؛ لأنه يشار بها عند السب؛ وخصت بذلك لأن لها اتصالا بنباط القلب . [ مراقي الفلاح: ۲۷۰] عند الإثبات: أي إثبات الألوهية لله وحده بقوله إلا الله . [ مراقي الفلاح: ۲۷۰] الأوليين: أطلقه فشمل الثالثة من المغرب والأخيرتين من الرباعي، وهي أحسن من عبارة القدوري حيث قال: "ويقرأ في الأخريين بالفاتحة"؛ إذ لا تشمل المغرب، والشيخ جرى على الصحيح من المذهب وإلا فروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة وجوبها، وظاهر الرواية: أنه يخير بين القراءة والتسبيح ثلاثاً كما في "البدائع" و"الذخيرة"، والسكوت قدر تسبيحة كما في "النهاية"، أو ثلاثا كما ذكره الزيلعي [البحر الرائق بتصرف: ٦٢٢/١] والصلاة إلخ : فيقول مثل ما قال محمد الله لما سئل عن كيفيتها، فقال: يقول: اللهم صلى على محمد وعلى آل محمد كما صليت على إبراهيم وعلى آل إبراهيم وبارك على محمد وعلى آل محمد كما باركت على إبراهيم وعلى آل إبراهيم في العالمين إنك حميد مجيد، وزيادة في العالمين ثابتة في رواية "مسلم" وغيره، فالمنع منها ضعيف [مراقي الفلاح (۲۷۱] اعلم أن الصلاة على النبي على ستة أقسام فرض وواجب، وسنة، ومستحب، ومكروه، وحرام، فالأول في العمر مرة واحدة للآية، والثاني كلما ذكر اسمه على قول الطحاوي، والظاهر أنه واجب على الكفاية لحصول المقصود، وهو تعظيمه كما ذكره القرباني والثالث في القعود الأخير، والرابع في جميع أوقات الإمكان، والخامس في الصلاة ما عدا القعود الأخير والقنوت، والسادس عند عمل محرم، وعند فتح التاجر متاعه إن قصد بذلك الإعلام بجودته، ولا خصوصية للصلاة، بل كذلك جميع الأذكار في جميع الأحوال الدالة على استعمال الذكر في غير موضعه، صرح بذلك علماؤنا . [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٧١] والدعاء [أي لنفسه ولوالديه وللمؤمنين والمؤمنات. (حاشية الطحطاوي] أي الدعاء الموجود في القرآن، و لم يرد حقيقة المشابهة؛ إذ القرآن معجز لا يشابهه شيء، ولكن أطلقها لإرادته نفس الدعاء لا قراءة القرآن مثل: "ربنا لا تزغ"، وقوله: "والسنة" يجوز نصبه عطفا على "الفاظ"، أي دعا بما يشبه ألفاظ السنة، وهي الأدعية المأثورة، ومن أحسنها ما في "صحيح مسلم": "اللهم إني أعوذ بك من عذاب جهنم، ومن عذاب القبر، ومن فتنة المحيا والممات ومن فتنة المسيح الدجال، ويجوز جره عطفا على القرآن أي الدعاء بالسنة، وقد تقدم أن الدعاء آخرها سنة. [البحر الرائق ملخصا: ٦٢٧/١]
The sunnah acts of prayer: Lengthening the first [rak'ah] in Fajr only; the takbir for ruku'; glorifying three times; grasping his knees with his hands during ruku'; separating his fingers – and the woman does not separate them; straightening his shins and flattening his back; leveling his head with his posterior during ruku'; the rising from ruku'; standing afterwards with tranquillity; placing his knees, then his hands, then his face for prostration – i.e., beginning and he begins by placing the nose; and the opposite for rising; the takbir for prostration; the takbir for rising from it; that the prostration be between his palms; standing; glorifying three times; the man distancing his stomach from his thighs, his elbows from his sides, and his forearms from the ground – i.e., keeping them away; the woman lowering and sticking her belly to her thighs; the standing and sitting between the two prostrations – meaning its completion; placing the hands on the thighs during the sitting between the two prostrations like the posture of tashahhud; spreading his left foot and erecting the right foot during the sitting; the woman's tawarruk; pointing in the authentic [position] with the finger called 'mushabbiha' during the testimony – i.e., the index finger of the right hand only... [The glosses continue]
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates the sunnah acts of prayer, with explanatory glosses from later Hanafi works. The main text lists actions including lengthening the first rak'ah in Fajr, the takbir for ruku', tasbih thrice, hand placement, finger spreading (men separate, women do not), back and head posture in ruku', rising with tranquility, the order of going into sujud (knees, hands, face), and the reverse for rising. It also covers the sunnah of distancing body parts from the ground for men, while women keep limbs close. The sitting between prostrations, hand placement, foot posture (iftrash for men, tawarruk for women), and the pointing of the index finger during tashahhud are detailed. The glosses provide an important intra-madhhab clarification on the finger pointing: although some early Hanafi scholars said not to point, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is to point, as it is established from the Prophet's practice (narrated in Sahih Muslim) and reported from Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. The text then continues with recitation in the latter rak'ahs, where the author clarifies that the sunnah is to recite al-Fatiha, but there is a choice between reciting, doing tasbih, or remaining silent according to the zahir al-riwayah. The salawat on the Prophet is classified into six categories (fard, wajib, sunnah, mustahabb, makruh, haram). The du'a should be from Quran and Sunnah, and the turning for the two taslims is mentioned.

Key Terms
المسبحة (al-musabbiha): The index finger of the right hand, called that because it is used to point in declaring Allah's tawhid (exaltation from partners).
الأوليين (al-ūlayayn): The first two rak'ahs of a fard prayer; in the gloss, this term is clarified to include the first two of Maghrib and the last two of a four-rak'ah prayer (i.e., after the first two rak'ahs).
التورك (al-tawarruk): For a woman in prayer: sitting on her left buttock with both legs out to the right, or sitting on her hip with her legs emerging from under her right hip.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, what is the ruling regarding pointing the index finger during tashahhud?
A) It is wajib to point.
B) It is haram to point; the finger should be kept still.
C) It is sunnah to point, and the worshipper should raise it when saying 'la ilaha' and lower it when saying 'illa Allah'.
D) It is makruh to point; one should only look at the finger.

Key Takeaway
Memorize the sunnah acts of prayer and adopt the mufta bihi position of pointing the index finger during tashahhud.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Sunnahs of Prayer: Recitation, Salawat, Du'a, and Taslim
Lists sunnah acts with detailed commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six sunnah acts of prayer listed in the passage, state the relied-upon ruling on recitation in later rak'ahs, enumerate the six categories of salawat, and explain the intentions for taslim.

Core Idea
Prayer's sunnah acts include recitation options, salawat, du'a, and intentional taslim; their details reflect the precision of Hanafi fiqh.

This lesson from Nur al-Idah lists the sunnah acts of prayer, with a commentary that delves into the ruling on reciting al-Fatihah in later rak'ahs, the six categories of sending blessings on the Prophet, the proper wording for du'a, and the intentions for the concluding taslim. We will navigate the text and understand the relied-upon positions.

Guided Path
1
Locate the list of sunnah acts
The text opens by stating: raising hands, recitation in later rak'ahs, salawat, du'a, and turning for taslim. Identify each act from the passage.
The list is presented in matn style, followed by commentary.
2
Examine the ruling on recitation in later rak'ahs
The commentary reveals an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa (in a narration) held it wajib, but the relied-upon view (Sahibayn) is that it is sunnah with options to recite, glorify, or remain silent.
The options are: Fatihah, tasbih 3 times, or silence for a tasbih or three.
3
Understand the six categories of salawat
The text classifies sending blessings into six legal categories: fard (once in a lifetime), wajib (when name is mentioned), sunnah (in final sitting), mustahabb (other times), makruh (in prayer other than final sitting), and haram (in inappropriate contexts).
This shows the gradation of rulings within one act.
4
Analyze the conditions for du'a
The du'a must resemble Quranic and prophetic language, not ordinary speech. The commentary cites the hadith from Sahih Muslim as a sunnah wording.
The du'a is sunnah in the final sitting.
5
Study the intentions for taslim
The intention varies by role: imam includes the congregation, angels, and righteous jinn; follower includes the imam and those behind; the one praying alone only includes angels. Additional sunnahs include lowering voice in second taslim and beginning with the right.
The taslim is sunnah muakkadah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سنن الصلاة
يرفعها عند النفي، ويضعها عند الإثبات وقراءة الفاتحة فيما بعد الأوليين، والصلاة على النبي يعني في الفرائض في الجلوس الأخير، والدعاء بما يشبه ألفاظ القرآن والسنة لا كلام الناس والالتفات يمينا ثم يسارا بالتسليمتين مثل قوله: اللهم زوجني عند النفي أي نفي الألوهية عما سوى الله تعالى بقوله : لا إله . [ مراقي الفلاح: ۲۷۰] عند الإثبات: أي إثبات الألوهية لله وحده بقوله إلا الله . [ مراقي الفلاح: ۲۷۰] الأوليين: أطلقه فشمل الثالثة من المغرب والأخيرتين من الرباعي، وهي أحسن من عبارة القدوري حيث قال: "ويقرأ في الأخريين بالفاتحة"؛ إذ لا تشمل المغرب، والشيخ جرى على الصحيح من المذهب وإلا فروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة وجوبها، وظاهر الرواية: أنه يخير بين القراءة والتسبيح ثلاثاً كما في "البدائع" و"الذخيرة"، والسكوت قدر تسبيحة كما في "النهاية"، أو ثلاثا كما ذكره الزيلعي [البحر الرائق بتصرف: ٦٢٢/١]
والصلاة إلخ : فيقول مثل ما قال محمد الله لما سئل عن كيفيتها، فقال: يقول: اللهم صلى على محمد وعلى آل محمد كما صليت على إبراهيم وعلى آل إبراهيم وبارك على محمد وعلى آل محمد كما باركت على إبراهيم وعلى آل إبراهيم في العالمين إنك حميد مجيد، وزيادة في العالمين ثابتة في رواية "مسلم" وغيره، فالمنع منها ضعيف [مراقي الفلاح (۲۷۱] اعلم أن الصلاة على النبي على ستة أقسام فرض وواجب، وسنة، ومستحب، ومكروه، وحرام، فالأول في العمر مرة واحدة للآية، والثاني كلما ذكر اسمه على قول الطحاوي، والظاهر أنه واجب على الكفاية لحصول المقصود، وهو تعظيمه كما ذكره القرباني والثالث في القعود الأخير، والرابع في جميع أوقات الإمكان، والخامس في الصلاة ما عدا القعود الأخير والقنوت، والسادس عند عمل محرم، وعند فتح التاجر متاعه إن قصد بذلك الإعلام بجودته، ولا خصوصية للصلاة، بل كذلك جميع الأذكار في جميع الأحوال الدالة على استعمال الذكر في غير موضعه، صرح بذلك علماؤنا . [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٧١] والدعاء [أي لنفسه ولوالديه وللمؤمنين والمؤمنات. (حاشية الطحطاوي] أي الدعاء الموجود في القرآن، و لم يرد حقيقة المشابهة؛ إذ القرآن معجز لا يشابهه شيء، ولكن أطلقها لإرادته نفس الدعاء لا قراءة القرآن مثل: "ربنا لا تزغ"، وقوله: "والسنة" يجوز نصبه عطفا على "الفاظ"، أي دعا بما يشبه ألفاظ السنة، وهي الأدعية المأثورة، ومن أحسنها ما في "صحيح مسلم": "اللهم إني أعوذ بك من عذاب جهنم، ومن عذاب القبر، ومن فتنة المحيا والممات ومن فتنة المسيح الدجال، ويجوز جره عطفا على القرآن أي الدعاء بالسنة، وقد تقدم أن الدعاء آخرها سنة. [البحر الرائق ملخصا: ٦٢٧/١]
ونية الإمام الرجال والحفظة وصالح الجن بالتسليمتين في الأصح، ونية المأموم إمامه والنساء والصبيان والخناثي المقتدين في جهته، وإن حاذاه نواه في التسليمتين مع القوم والحفظة وصالح الجن، ونية المنفرد الملائكة فقط، وخفض الثانية عن الأولى، ومقارنته لسلام الإمام، والبداءة باليمين، وانتظار المسبوق فراغ الإمام.
Sunnahs of prayer: He raises them (his hands) when negating, and places them when affirming; and recitation of al-Fatihah in the two after the first two; and sending blessings upon the Prophet, meaning in the obligatory prayers, in the last sitting; and supplication with words resembling the Quran and Sunnah, not the speech of people; and turning the face right then left with the two taslims – like his saying: 'O Allah, marry me.' At negation: meaning negation of divinity from other than Allah by his saying: 'La ilaha.' At affirmation: meaning affirmation of divinity for Allah alone by his saying: 'Illa Allah.' [Maraqi al-Falah: 270] 'The first two': he released it so it includes the third of Maghrib and the last two of the four-rak'ah prayers, and this is better than the expression of al-Quduri where he said: 'and he recites al-Fatihah in the last two'; for it does not include Maghrib, and the author followed the soundest of the madhhab; otherwise, al-Hasan reported from Abu Hanifa its obligation, and the apparent narration is that he has a choice between recitation and glorifying three times as in al-Bada'i' and al-Dhakhirah, and silence for the duration of one glorification as in al-Nihayah, or three as mentioned by al-Zayla'i [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq adapted: 1/622]. 'And blessings etc.': so he says like what Muhammad (peace be upon him) said when asked about its manner: he said: 'O Allah, bless Muhammad and the family of Muhammad as You blessed Ibrahim and the family of Ibrahim, and have mercy on Muhammad and the family of Muhammad as You had mercy on Ibrahim and the family of Ibrahim in the worlds; indeed You are Praiseworthy and Glorious.' And the addition of 'in the worlds' is established in a narration of Muslim and others, so forbidding it is weak [Maraqi al-Falah: 271]. Know that sending blessings upon the Prophet is of six types: obligatory, necessary, sunnah, recommended, disliked, and forbidden. The first: once in a lifetime due to the verse; the second: every time his name is mentioned according to al-Tahawi, and apparently it is a collective obligation (wajib kifayah) because the purpose (glorifying him) is achieved, as mentioned by al-Qarabani; the third: in the final sitting; the fourth: in all possible times; the fifth: in prayer other than the final sitting and qunut; the sixth: when engaging in a forbidden act, or when a merchant opens his goods intending to boast about their quality. There is no particularity for prayer; rather all remembrances in all states that indicate using remembrance in an inappropriate place; our scholars explicitly stated that [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 271]. 'And supplication' [meaning for himself, his parents, the believing men and women (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi)] meaning the supplication found in the Quran; and the real resemblance is not intended; for the Quran is miraculous and nothing resembles it, but he used it metaphorically to mean the supplication itself, not the recitation of the Quran, such as 'Our Lord, do not cause our hearts to deviate.' And his saying: 'and the Sunnah' – it can be parsed as an accusative conjunction to 'words', i.e., he supplicated with words resembling the words of the Sunnah, which are transmitted supplications; among the best is what is in Sahih Muslim: 'O Allah, I seek refuge in You from the punishment of Hell, from the punishment of the grave, from the trials of life and death, and from the trial of the Dajjal'; and it can be parsed as a genitive conjunction to 'the Quran', i.e., supplication according to the Sunnah. It has preceded that supplication is a sunnah in the last sitting [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq summarized: 1/627]. And the intention of the imam: men, the guardian angels, and righteous jinn with the two taslims in the most correct view; and the intention of the follower: his imam, and women, boys, and hermaphrodites who are following if they are in his direction; but if he is opposite him, he intends them in the two taslims along with the people, guardian angels, and righteous jinn; and the intention of the one praying alone: only the angels; and lowering the second taslim (voice) more than the first; and his (the follower's) taslim being concurrent with the imam's taslim; and beginning with the right; and the one who missed a part waiting for the imam to finish.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates the sunnah acts within the prayer (salat). The author begins by listing: raising the hands (raf' al-yadayn) during the opening takbir—raising them when saying 'Allahu Akbar' (at the negation of divinity) and lowering them when saying the affirmation; reciting Surah al-Fatihah in the third rak'ah of Maghrib and the last two rak'ahs of four-rak'ah prayers (the commentary clarifies that 'after the first two' includes these, a more precise wording than al-Quduri's); sending blessings (salawat) upon the Prophet Muhammad in the final sitting for obligatory prayers; making supplication (du'a) with words that resemble Quranic and prophetic phrases, not ordinary human speech; and turning the face right then left for the two taslims. The commentary expands significantly: on the recitation in later units, it notes that al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifa that it is wajib (obligatory), but the relied-upon view (zahir al-riwaya) is that one has a choice between reciting al-Fatihah, glorifying Allah three times, or remaining silent for the duration of one glorification. On the salawat, the text provides the wording taught by the Prophet and notes that a version in Sahih Muslim includes 'fi al-'alamin' (in the worlds), which is accepted. It then categorizes sending blessings into six legal categories: fard (once in a lifetime, based on Q 33:56), wajib (whenever his name is mentioned, according to al-Tahawi, but it is a collective obligation), sunnah (in the final sitting of prayer), mustahabb (in all other times), makruh (in prayer except the final sitting and qunut), and haram (in inappropriate contexts like sinful acts). On du'a, the author clarifies that the supplication must be in words resembling the Quran and Sunnah, not the Quran itself (since the Quran is inimitable), and cites the famous hadith from Sahih Muslim. The passage then discusses the intention (niyyah) for the taslim: the imam intends by his two taslims the male congregation, guardian angels, and righteous jinn; the follower intends his imam, women, boys, and hermaphrodites if they are in his direction (if standing opposite, he intends them in both taslims); the one praying alone intends only the angels. Additional sunnahs include: lowering the voice in the second taslim more than the first, the follower making taslim concurrent with the imam's, beginning with the right side, and the one who missed a part (masbuq) waiting for the imam to finish before completing his own prayer.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet regularly performed without making it obligatory; omission does not invalidate prayer but is considered blameworthy.
الصلاة على النبي (al-salat 'ala al-nabi): Sending blessings upon the Prophet, specifically in the final sitting of prayer using the taught formula.
التسليمتان (al-taslimatayn): The two salutations (saying 'assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah') to the right and left to exit the prayer.
الحفظة (al-hafazah): The guardian angels who record deeds and protect humans; included in the intention of taslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting Surah al-Fatihah in the third rak'ah of Maghrib?
A) It is fard (obligatory).
B) It is wajib (necessary).
C) It is sunnah (recommended).
D) It is makruh (disliked).

Key Takeaway
The sunnah acts of prayer, including recitation in later rak'ahs, salawat, du'a, and taslim intentions, have detailed rulings in the Hanafi school that balance flexibility and fidelity to the prophetic practice.

Etiquettes of Prayer: Hands, Gaze, and the Masbuq Ruling
Lists recommended etiquettes and commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended etiquettes of prayer regarding hand placement and gaze, and apply the ruling for the masbuq's waiting period.

Core Idea
Adab completes the prayer; omission is not sinful but loses perfection.

This lesson covers the recommended etiquettes (adab) that perfect the prayer, including where to look and how to position hands during the opening takbir. We also examine the special case of the masbuq (latecomer) and the ruling if he stands before the imam completes the taslim. These etiquettes are mustahabb (recommended) but not obligatory or sunnah muakkadah.

Guided Path
1
Define 'adab' in the Hanafi school
Understand that adab are actions the Prophet performed once or twice but did not consistently maintain; they are legislated to complete the sunnah. This distinguishes them from sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
The commentary in Maraqi al-Falah gives this definition.
2
Compile the specific adab listed
List the five specific etiquettes: removing hands from sleeves during takbir, looking at the place of prostration while standing, at the top of the feet while bowing, at the tip of the nose while prostrating, and at the lap (garment) while sitting.
The commentary clarifies that for a sitting person, it is as if looking at the tip of the nose.
3
Analyze the ruling on the masbuq's waiting
The masbuq must wait for the imam to complete both taslims due to the obligation of following (wujub al-mutaba'ah). Standing prematurely is makruh tahrimi unless a necessity arises (e.g., fear of missing the prayer time).
This ruling is derived from the commentary and is an extension of adab into a higher category.
4
Apply the definition to other points
The commentary on guardian angels and the two taslims are not part of adab but show that the author did not exhaust all etiquettes. Understand that the passage is a selection, indicated by the partitive 'min'.
This helps recognize the scope of the chapter.

Source Text

فصل في آداب الصلاة
من آدابها: إخراج الرجل كفيه من كميه عند التكبير، ونظر المصلي إلى موضع سجوده قائماً رجلا كان أو امرأة، وإلى ظاهر القدم راكعا، وإلى أرنبة أنفه ساجدا، وإلى حجرة جالسا، ولو حكما كالقاعد طرف أنفه والحفظة: أي الملائكة الحفظة جمع حافظ؛ سموا به لحفظ ما يصدر من الإنسان من قول وعمل، فعن يمينه رقيب وهو كاتب الحسنات وعن يساره عتيد وهو كاتب السيئات أو لحفظهم إياه من الجن وأسباب المعاطب، ولا يعين عددا للاختلاف فيه [حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ٢٧٤] الأصح وقيل: ينويهم بالتسليمة الأولى، وقيل: تكفيه الإشارة إليهم مراقي الفلاح (۲۷٥] وإن حاذاه الخ: أي وإن كان الإمام بحذاء المقتدي نواه في التسليمتين؛ لأنه ذو حظ من الجانبين وخفض الثانية إلى أي ويُسنّ خفض صوته بالتسليمة الثانية عن الأولى مراقي الفلاح: ٢٧٦] مدة مسحه من وانتظار المسبوق إلخ لوجوب المتابعة حتى يعلم أن لا سهو عليه مراقي الفلاح: ٢٧٦] فإن قام قبله كره تحريما، وقد يباح له القيام ضرورة كما لو خشي إن انتظره يخرج وقت الفجر أو الجمعة أو العيد، أو تمضي أو يخرج الوقت وهو معذور، وكذا لو خشي مرور الناس بين يديه [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٧٦] آدابها: أشار بـ"من" التبعيضية إلى أنه لم يستوف أفراد الآداب، فمنها: انتظار الصلاة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٧٦] والأدب : ما فعله الرسول مرة أو مرتين و لم يواظب عليه كزيادة التسبيحات في الركوع والسجود، والزيادة على القراءة المسنونة، وقد شرع لإكمال السنة. [حاشية الطحطاوي بزيادة ٢٧٦] راكعا هذا لا يتأتى في المصلي قاعدا. حجره هو ما بين يديك من الثوب.
Chapter on the etiquettes of prayer. Among its etiquettes: a man removing his hands from his sleeves during the takbir; the one praying looking at his place of prostration while standing, whether man or woman; and at the top of the foot while bowing; and at the tip of his nose while prostrating; and at his lap while sitting; even if he is sitting, he looks at the tip of his nose. The guardian angels: they are the angels who guard, plural of 'guardian'; they are named thus for guarding what issues from a person of speech and deed; on his right is a watcher who records good deeds, and on his left is a ready one who records evil deeds; or for protecting him from jinn and causes of harm; and their number is not specified due to disagreement [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah: 274]. The most correct view: and it is said: he intends them in the first taslim; and it is said: the gesture towards them suffices [Maraqi al-Falah: 275]. 'And if he is opposite etc.': i.e., if the imam is standing in front of the follower, he intends him in the two taslims because it is beneficial from both sides. And lowering the second: i.e., it is sunnah to lower his voice in the second taslim more than the first [Maraqi al-Falah: 276]. The duration of his (the masbuq's) waiting: and waiting for the one who missed a part for the imam to finish, due to the obligation of following (the imam) until he knows that there is no forgetfulness upon him [Maraqi al-Falah: 276]. For if he stands up before that, it is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi), but it may be permissible for him to stand out of necessity, as if he fears that if he waits the time of Fajr, Jumu'ah, or Eid might pass, or the time may elapse while he is excused; similarly, if he fears people passing in front of him [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 276]. Its etiquettes: he indicated by the particle 'min' (partitive) that he did not exhaust all individual etiquettes; among them: waiting for the prayer [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 276]. And 'adab' (etiquette) is what the Prophet did once or twice but did not consistently maintain, such as increasing the tasbihat in bowing and prostration, and increasing beyond the sunnah recitation; it is legislated to complete the sunnah [Maraqi al-Falah: 276]. 'At the takbir': he meant by 'takbir' the takbirat al-ihram (opening takbir); and this indicates that it is not recommended (mandub) to do so in other than the state of ihram, but it is preferable to remove them in all states [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with addition: 276]. 'Bowing': this does not apply to the one praying sitting. 'His lap': it is what is in front of you of the garment.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This section, 'Chapter on the Etiquettes of Prayer', lists recommended actions (adab) that enhance the perfection of the prayer. The base text from Nur al-Idah mentions: removing the hands from the sleeves during the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram); looking at the place of prostration while standing; looking at the top of the feet while bowing; looking at the tip of the nose while prostrating; and looking at the lap (i.e., the garment in front of him) while sitting. The commentary expands on these: regarding the gaze, it notes that even a sitting person should look at the tip of his nose (metaphorically). A long note explains the 'guardian angels' (al-hafazah) who record deeds and protect from harm, noting that their number is unspecified. On the waiting of the masbuq (one who missed part of the prayer), the commentary explains that he must wait for the imam to finish taslim to ensure no forgetfulness (sahw) occurred; if he stands prematurely, it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), unless a necessity arises such as fear of missing the prayer time or people passing in front of him. The commentator also clarifies that 'adab' applies to acts the Prophet performed occasionally, not consistently, such as increasing tasbihat (glorifications) beyond the sunnah amount; these are meant to complete the sunnah. On the removal of hands from sleeves, it specifies that the recommendation (nadb) applies only at the opening takbir, but it is better to do so in all states of prayer.

Key Terms
آداب الصلاة (adab al-salah): Recommended behaviors and actions that perfect the prayer but are not obligatory or sunnah muakkadah.
تكبيرة التحريم (takbirat al-ihram): The opening takbir ('Allahu Akbar') that begins the prayer and prohibits worldly actions.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): One who misses one or more rak'ahs of a congregational prayer and joins later.
مكروه تحريماً (makruh tahrimi): A prohibited action but with a weaker proof than haram; doing it is sinful, but not as severe as haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) At the top of the feet.
C) At the tip of the nose.
D) At the lap.

Key Takeaway
Adab are recommended actions that perfect the prayer; omission does not affect validity but loses perfection, and the masbuq must wait for the imam's taslim before standing.

Adab al-Salat: Intention in Taslim and Physical Postures
List of recommended etiquettes for prayer with detailed intention rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the etiquettes of prayer (adab) according to the Hanafi school and explain their legal status as sunnah ghayr muakkadah.

Core Idea
Adab are recommended acts that perfect prayer but omitting them does not invalidate.

This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates the recommended etiquettes (adab) of prayer. While the obligations (fard) and necessities (wajib) of prayer are fixed, these adab enhance the quality and completeness of the prayer. The text covers the intention during the final taslim, physical postures, and additional practices such as suppressing coughs and timing of standing. Understanding these adab helps the believer approach prayer with the prophetic model of excellence.

Guided Path
1
Determine the legal status of adab
Read the passage to identify whether these practices are obligatory or recommended. The commentary defines adab as actions the Prophet performed occasionally, making them sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
Adab enhance prayer but do not invalidate if omitted.
2
Analyze the section on intention (niyyah) in taslim
Examine the different categories: imam, follower (mamum), masbuq (latecomer), and munfarid (alone). Note for each category who is included in the intention: men, women, angels, jinn.
The most correct view is to intend angels in both taslims.
3
List the recommended physical postures
From the text, extract where to look in each position: during standing (place of prostration), bowing (back of foot), prostrating (tip of nose), sitting (lap). Also note taking hands out of sleeves at takbir and turning shoulders during taslim.
The posture for bowing does not apply when praying seated.
4
Compile the remaining etiquettes
Note rules about suppressing coughs, closing mouth while yawning, standing for 'hayya ala al-falah', and imam starting at 'qad qamat al-salah'. Also mention the masbuq should wait for imam's taslim.
These are additional sunnan to perfect the prayer.

Etiquettes of Prayer: The intention of the imam is for the men, the guardian angels, and the righteous jinn with both taslims in the most correct view. The intention of the follower is for his imam, the women, boys, and hermaphrodites following in his direction. If the imam is opposite him, he intends them in both taslims along with the congregation, guardian angels, and righteous jinn. The intention of the one praying alone is only for the angels. Lowering the second taslim is lower than the first. He should be concurrent with the imam's salam, start with the right, and wait for the one who is preceded to finish his taslim. The two taslims of the one following. Section on the etiquettes of prayer: Among its etiquettes: a man should take his hands out of his sleeves at the takbir. The one praying should look at the place of his prostration when standing, whether man or woman; at the back of his foot when bowing; at the tip of his nose when prostrating; and at his lap when sitting, even if effectively, like the one sitting. The guardian angels are the angels who guard, plural of 'hafiz'; they are named for guarding what issues from a person of speech and action. On his right is a watcher who records good deeds, and on his left is one ready to record evil deeds, or for guarding him from jinn and causes of harm. Their number is not specified due to difference. The most correct view is that he intends them with the first taslim; it is said that pointing to them suffices. If the imam is opposite the follower, he intends them in both taslims because he has a share from both sides. It is recommended to lower his voice with the second taslim more than the first. Waiting for the one who is preceded, etc., is due to the obligation of following until he knows there is no forgetfulness upon him. If one stands before him, it is prohibitively disliked; it may be permissible to stand out of necessity, such as if he fears that waiting would cause him to miss the time of Fajr, Jumu'ah, or 'Eid, or if the time would pass while he is excused. Similarly, if he fears people passing in front of him. The term 'min' indicates partiality, meaning he has not covered all etiquettes; among them is waiting for prayer. 'Adab' is what the Messenger did once or twice and did not consistently perform, such as increasing the tasbihs in bowing and prostration, and increasing recitation beyond the sunna; it is legislated to complete the sunna. 'At the takbir' means the takbir of ihram, indicating that it is not recommended at other times, but it is better to do so in all cases. 'Riding' (raki'an) does not apply to the one sitting. His lap is the front of his garment. And at the shoulders while saying salam, suppressing coughing as much as possible, closing his mouth when yawning. Standing when the mu'adhdhin says 'hayya 'ala al-falah', and the imam's starting when the iqamah says 'qad qamat al-salah'.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage lists the etiquettes (adab) of prayer, which are recommended acts that perfect the prayer but are not obligatory. It begins with the intention (niyyah) during the taslim (final salutation). The imam should intend by his taslim the men praying behind him, the guardian angels, and the righteous jinn. The follower intends the imam, women, boys, and hermaphrodites in his direction. If the imam is directly opposite, the follower intends both taslims for the congregation, angels, and jinn. The one praying alone intends only the angels. The second taslim is lower in voice. The follower should coordinate with the imam’s taslim, start with the right side, and wait for the masbuq (latecomer) to finish his own taslim. Then the text lists physical etiquettes: taking hands out of sleeves at the takbir, looking at the place of prostration while standing, at the back of the foot while bowing (though this does not apply to a seated person), at the nose tip while prostrating, at the lap (the front of one's garment) while sitting. There follows a detailed explanation of 'guardian angels' and the rulings on intention for the taslim. The passage also covers waiting for the masbuq, mentioning that it is prohibitively disliked for a follower to stand ahead of the imam unless necessary to avoid missing the prayer time. Coughing should be suppressed unless it harms or distracts; closing the mouth during yawning is recommended. Finally, it states that the congregation should stand when the mu'adhdhin says 'hayya 'ala al-falah', and the imam begins when 'qad qamat al-salah' is said. These are all sunan (recommended practices) that enhance the prayer.

Key Terms
آداب الصلاة (adab al-salah): Recommended acts and postures that perfect the prayer but are not obligatory; derived from occasional actions of the Prophet.
مسبوق (masbuq): One who joins the congregation late and has missed part of the prayer; he follows the imam but completes his own taslim after the imam.
تسليم (taslim): The final salutation of prayer, saying 'al-salamu 'alaykum' to the right and left.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The guardian angels only
C) The righteous jinn
D) Both angels and jinn

Key Takeaway
The adab of prayer are recommended acts that enhance the prayer; understanding them helps perfect one's worship without burden of obligation.

The Method of Raising Hands at the Start of Prayer and the Timing of Takbir
Ruling on hand-raising and timing of takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands at the start of prayer and identify the preferred timing of the takbir relative to hand-raising.

Core Idea
Raising hands is sunnah, not wajib; the preferred view is to say takbir first, then raise.

When you begin prayer, the opening takbir is essential. But what about raising your hands? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on hand-raising and its timing, distinguishing between sunnah and wajib. We will explore the intra-Hanafi dispute on the sequence and determine the mufta bihi ruling for everyday practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Pinpoint the act being discussed—raising hands at the start of prayer. From the text, determine whether it is fard, wajib, or sunnah. The matn describes the manner, and the commentary confirms it is sunnah.
The takbir itself is wajib, but hand-raising is separate.
2
Understand the three opinions on timing
The text mentions three views: 1) concurrent (hand-raising and takbir simultaneously), 2) hand-raising before takbir, 3) takbir before hand-raising. Identify each view and its proponents.
The first view is attributed to some Hanafi scholars; the third is preferred by the commentator.
3
Evaluate the preferred (mufta bihi) view
The commentator states 'هو الأصح' (it is the most correct) for the third view—say takbir first, then raise hands. Understand why this is chosen: the report of Ibn 'Umar and other evidences support this sequence.
This reflects the authority of the later Hanafi masters.
4
Apply the ruling to cases of forgetfulness
If one forgets to raise hands until after the takbir, he should still raise them because the time for the sunnah has passed. If he remembers during the takbir, he raises immediately.
This shows that the sunnah is not invalidated by delay; it can be performed later within the opening.

فصل في كيفية تركيب الصلاة
إذا أراد الرجل الدخول في الصلاة أخرج كفيه من كميه ثم رفعهما حذاء أذنيه، ثم كبر بلا مد ناوياً، أي صلاة كانت
حذاء أذنيه حتى يحاذي بإبهاميه شحمتي أذنيه، ويجعل باطن كفيه نحو القبلة، ولا يفرج أصابعه ولا يضمها، والمرأة الحرة حذو منكبيها مراقي الفلاح بحذف: ۲۷۸]
يرفع مقارنا
ثم كبر إلخ أفاد تأخير التكبير عن رفع اليدين، وهو أحد الأقوال الثلاثة فيه، فالقول الأول أنه للتكبير، وفسر قاضي خان" المقارنة بأن تكون بداءته وختمه عند بداءته وختمه، والقول الثاني: وقته قبل التكبير، والقول الثالث: وقته بعد التكبير، فيكبر أولاً ثم يرفع يديه. قال الشارح: هو الأصح، فإذا لم يرفع يديه حتى فرغ من التكبير يأتي به لفوات محله، وإن ذكره في أثنائه رفع.
بلا مد إلخ: اعلم أن المد في التكبير إما أن يكون في لفظ "الله" أو في لفظ "أكبر"، فإن كان في لفظ "الله" فإما أن يكون في أوله أو في وسطه أو في آخره، فإن كان في أوله كان مفسداً؛ لأنه في صورة الاستفهام حتى لو تعمده يكفر؛ للشك في الكبرياء، وإن كان في وسطه فهو الصواب، إلا أنه لا يبالغ فيه، فإن بالغ زيادة على مده الطبعي، وهو قدر حركتين، كره، ولا تفسد على المختار، كما في ابن أمير حاج، وفي "السراج": أنه خلاف الأولى. فالكراهة للتنزيه، وإن كان في آخره بأن أشبع حركة الهاء فهو خطأ من حيث اللغة، ولا تفسد به الصلاة، =
Section on how to structure the prayer: When a man intends to enter the prayer, he takes his hands out of his sleeves, then raises them to the level of his ears, then says the takbir without prolongation, intending any prayer he wishes. He should raise his hands such that his thumbs are opposite the earlobes, his palms face the qiblah, his fingers are neither spread nor closed. The free woman raises her hands to the level of her shoulders. He raises them while saying the takbir, i.e., he should say the takbir and raise simultaneously. Then he says the takbir, etc. This indicates that the takbir is delayed after raising the hands. This is one of three opinions: the first is that the raising is for the takbir (concurrent), the second is that it is before the takbir, the third is that it is after the takbir (so say takbir first then raise). The commentator says the third is the most correct. If he forgets to raise his hands until after finishing the takbir, he still performs the raising because its time has passed; if he remembers during the takbir, he raises. About 'without prolongation': Know that the prolongation in the takbir can be in the word 'Allah' or in 'Akbar'. If it is in 'Allah', it can be at the beginning, middle, or end. If at the beginning, it invalidates because it resembles a question; if done intentionally, it is disbelief due to doubt in God's greatness. If in the middle, it is correct but not exaggerated; if exaggerated beyond the natural length (two vowel counts), it is disliked but does not invalidate according to the chosen view. In 'al-Siraj', it is said to be contrary to what is preferred. So the dislike is for tanzih (avoidance). If at the end by prolonging the vowel of 'ha', it is a linguistic error but does not invalidate the prayer.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This section details the proper way to begin prayer (tarkib al-salah), focusing on the actions of raising hands and saying the takbir. The matn states: a man takes his hands out of sleeves, raises them to his ears, then says the takbir without prolongation (madd), intending the specific prayer. The commentary expands: the thumbs should be at earlobes, palms toward qiblah, fingers normally spread. For a free woman, hands are raised to shoulders. On the timing of hand-raising vis-à-vis takbir, there are three views (the 'three opinions' known in the Hanafi school). The preferred view according to the commentator (Al-Sharih) is to first say the takbir, then raise the hands (i.e., takbir precedes raising). If one forgets to raise, it is done after the fact. Then the discussion turns to the rules of prolongation (madd) in the takbir. Prolonging the first alif of 'Allah' turns it into a question ('A-llah?'), which invalidates the prayer and can lead to disbelief if intentional. Normal prolongation in the middle is fine, but excessive prolongation (more than two vowel counts) is disliked (makruh tanzih) but not invalidating. Prolonging the final 'ha' is a linguistic mistake but does not break the prayer. The ikhtilaf on hand-raising timing is intra-Hanafi: Abu Hanifa and two companions have differing views, but the mufta bihi here is the third opinion (takbir first).

Key Terms
تكبير التحريمة (takbir al-tahrimah): The initial 'Allahu Akbar' said to enter the state of prayer, which renders worldly actions forbidden.
مقارنة (muqaranah): Simultaneity of hand-raising and takbir; some hold that both actions should start and end together.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, what is the correct sequence of hand-raising and takbir when starting prayer?
A) Raise hands first, then say takbir
B) Say takbir first, then raise hands
C) Raise hands and say takbir simultaneously
D) Hand-raising is not done

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the opening takbir precedes hand-raising, and hand-raising is a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation.

Salah — Prayer

Rules of Madd in the Opening Takbir
Rulings on prolongation (madd) in the takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the types of madd (prolongation) in the opening takbir and determine which invalidates the prayer and which is merely disliked.

Core Idea
Prolonging the first 'a' of 'Allah' invalidates the takbir; other madd is acceptable but some is disliked.

Saying the opening takbir correctly is essential for a valid prayer. This lesson dives into the detailed rulings on prolongation (madd) in the words 'Allah' and 'Akbar', explaining when it becomes an invalidating defect and when it is just a minor blunder.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the ruling
The passage discusses madd (prolongation) in the takbir, focusing on the words 'Allah' and 'Akbar'. Recognize that this is a commentary on the matn's phrase 'bila madd' (without prolongation).
The takbir is 'Allahu Akbar'.
2
Analyze madd in 'Allah' according to position
There are three possible positions for prolongation in 'Allah': at the beginning (the alif), in the middle (the lam), and at the end (the ha). Understand each case.
The beginning is the first alif: 'A-llah'.
3
Determine the ruling for each position
Prolonging the first alif turns it into a question form ('A-llah?'), which invalidates the takbir; if intentional, it leads to disbelief. Middle madd is correct but excessive prolongation (beyond two vowel counts) is disliked (makruh tanzih). Final madd (prolonging the ha) is a linguistic error but does not invalidate.
The text says 'لا تفسد على المختار' for excessive middle madd; final madd is purely linguistic.
4
Apply the ruling to madd in 'Akbar'
Although the passage only explicitly discusses 'Allah', similar reasoning applies to 'Akbar': the first letter is not prolongable in an invalidating way unless one adds extra sounds. The focus remains on the initial madd of 'Allah'.
The same principle of avoiding question-like intonation applies.
5
Understand the practical consequences
If one inadvertently prolongs the first alif, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated. If one intentionally does it, it is kufr. For excessive middle madd, it is disliked but the prayer is valid. For final madd, no effect.
This shows the precision required in pronunciation.

Source Text

حذاء أذنيه حتى يحاذي بإبهاميه شحمتي أذنيه، ويجعل باطن كفيه نحو القبلة، ولا يفرج أصابعه ولا يضمها، والمرأة الحرة حذو منكبيها مراقي الفلاح بحذف: ۲۷۸]
