Raising Hands (Raf' al-Yadayn) at the Start of Prayer
Fiqh ruling on method and timing of raising hands at prayer commencement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended method of raising hands for men and women, and compare the three Hanafi opinions on the timing of raising hands relative to the takbir.

Core Idea
Raising hands is sunnah; the most correct timing is to raise after the opening takbir.

In this lesson, we examine the opening act of raising the hands (raf' al-yadayn) when commencing prayer. The Hanafi school details the specific method for men and women, and a notable intra-madhhab dispute exists regarding whether the hands are raised before, during, or after the takbir. Understanding this helps you perform the sunnah correctly and appreciate the diversity of opinion within the school.

Guided Path
1
State the basic ruling
Identify that raising hands at the start of prayer is sunnah, not wajib. This means it is recommended but not obligatory for validity.
The ruling is derived from hadith and the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him).
2
Describe the method for men
Men should raise their hands to the level of their ears, with palms facing the qiblah, and fingers neither spread nor closed. The thumbs align with the earlobes.
This is based on the phrase 'حذاء أذنيه' (opposite his ears) and 'حتى يحاذي بإبهاميه شحمتي أذنيه' (until his thumbs align with his earlobes).
3
Describe the method for women
A free woman raises her hands to the level of her shoulders (حذو منكبيها). This is the Hanafi distinction based on modesty.
The difference is due to the woman's need for concealment; raising only to shoulders is less conspicuous.
4
Identify the three opinions on timing
There are three views: (1) hands raised simultaneously with the beginning and end of the takbir (muqaranah), (2) hands raised before the takbir, (3) hands raised after the takbir (the most correct according to the commentator).
The first opinion is attributed to Qadi Khan, the second is another view, and the third is preferred by the commentator (al-Sharih).
5
Determine the preferred view and its consequence
The commentator states that the third opinion (raising after the takbir) is the most correct (asahh). If one forgets to raise hands until after completing the takbir, he should still raise them because the sunnah time has passed; if he remembers during the takbir, he raises at that moment.
This indicates that the sunnah is flexible but the ideal is to raise after the takbir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة ۹۳ كيفية تركيب الصلاة وإلى المنكبين مسلّما، ودفع السعال ما استطاع، وكظم فمه عند التثاؤب، والقيام أي مدة استطاعتهم حين قيل حي على الفلاح، وشروع الإمام مذ قيل: قد قامت الصلاة. فصل في كيفية تركيب الصلاة إذا أراد الرجل الدخول في الصلاة أخرج كفيه من كميه ثم رفعهما حذاء أذنيه، ثم خرج به المرأة كبر بلا مد ناوياً، أي صلاة كانت إلى المنكبين: أي ومن آداب الصلاة نظر المصلي إلى منكبيه حال التسليم أطلقه، وهو مقيد بما إذا كان بصيراً، أما إذا كان أعمى أو في ظلمة فيلاحظ عظمة الله تعالى. مسلّما أي حال كونك قائلا: السلام عليكم. ما استطاع قيد باستطاعته فأفاد أنه إذا كان يحصل للمصلي من دفع السعال ضرر أو يشتغل قلبه بدفعه، فالأولى عدم دفعه كما في تنحنح محتاج إليه لدفع بلغم منعه عن القراءة، أو عن الجهر وهو إمام. وكظم فمه أي إمساكه وسده ولو بأخذ شفتيه بسنه، فإن أمكنه أخذ شفتيه بسنه فلم يفعل وغطاه بيده أو كمه كره. والتثاؤب: انفتاح الفم بريح يخرج من المعدة لمرض من الأمراض يحدث فيها، فيوجب ذلك. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٧٧] والقيام حين قيل إلخ : أي ومن الأدب قيام القوم والإمام إن كان حاضراً بقرب المحراب وقت قول المقيم: "حي على الفلاح"؛ لأن المقيم في ضمن قوله هذا أمر بالقيام فيجاب، وإن لم يكن حاضراً يقوم كل صف حين ينتهي إليه الإمام في الأظهر. مراقي الفلاح بتصرف: ۲۷۷] حذاء أذنيه حتى يحاذي بإبهاميه شحمتي أذنيه، ويجعل باطن كفيه نحو القبلة، ولا يفرج أصابعه ولا يضمها، والمرأة الحرة حذو منكبيها مراقي الفلاح بحذف: ۲۷۸] يرفع مقارنا ثم كبر إلخ أفاد تأخير التكبير عن رفع اليدين، وهو أحد الأقوال الثلاثة فيه، فالقول الأول أنه للتكبير، وفسر قاضي خان" المقارنة بأن تكون بداءته وختمه عند بداءته وختمه، والقول الثاني: وقته قبل التكبير، والقول الثالث: وقته بعد التكبير، فيكبر أولاً ثم يرفع يديه. قال الشارح: هو الأصح، فإذا لم يرفع يديه حتى فرغ من التكبير يأتي به لفوات محله، وإن ذكره في أثنائه رفع. بلا مد إلخ: اعلم أن المد في التكبير إما أن يكون في لفظ "الله" أو في لفظ "أكبر"، فإن كان في لفظ "الله" فإما أن يكون في أوله أو في وسطه أو في آخره، فإن كان في أوله كان مفسداً؛ لأنه في صورة الاستفهام حتى لو تعمده يكفر؛ للشك في الكبرياء، وإن كان في وسطه فهو الصواب، إلا أنه لا يبالغ فيه، فإن بالغ زيادة على مده الطبعي، وهو قدر حركتين، كره، ولا تفسد على المختار، كما في ابن أمير حاج، وفي "السراج": أنه خلاف الأولى. فالكراهة للتنزيه، وإن كان في آخره بأن أشبع حركة الهاء فهو خطأ من حيث اللغة، ولا تفسد به الصلاة، ويصح الشروع بكل ذكر خالص الله تعالى كـ سبحان الله، وبالفارسية، إن عجز عن العربية، وإن قدر لا يصح شروعه بالفارسية، ولا قراءته بها في الأصح، ثم وضع يمينه على يساره تحت سرته عقب التحريمة بلا مهلة مستفتحا وهو أن يقول: "سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك وتبارك اسمك وتعالى جدك ولا إله غيرك"، ويستفتح أو اسم من أسماء أولاد الشيطان، وفي "القنية": لا تفسد ؛ لأنه إشباع، وهو لغة ،قوم، واستبعده "الزيلعي" بأنه لا يجوز إلا في الشعر، ولو فعله المؤذن لا تجب إعادة الأذان؛ لأن أمر الأذان أوسع، وإن تعمده يكفر، أي مع قصد المعنى، وإلا لا، ويستغفر ويتوب، وإن كان في آخره فقيل تفسد صلاته وقياسه أن لا يصح الشروع به، وقيل: لا تفسد. ولو حذف المصلي أو الحالف أو الذابح المد الذي في اللام الثانية من الجلالة أو حذف الهاء، اختلف في صحة الشروع وانعقاد اليمين وحل الذبيحة، فلا يترك ذلك احتياطاً. (حاشية الطحطاوي ملخصا) خالص الله إلخ فلا يصح باللهم اغفر لي أي بذكر يخلص عن اختلاطه بحاجة الطالب وإن كره؛ لترك الواجب، وهو لفظ التكبير، وفي قوله: "كبر" و "بكل ذكر " إشارة إلى أنه لبد لصحة الشروع من جملة تامة، فإن التكبير "الله أكبر" وهو جملة، والذكر التام لا يكون إلا بجملة مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي بتصرف: ٢٧٩] وبالفارسية أو غيرها من الألسن [مراقي الفلاح (۲۸۰] والتقييد بالفارسية ليس للاحتراز عن غيرها، فإن الصحيح أن الفارسية وغيرها سواء، فحينئذ كان مراده من الفارسية غير العربية مراقي الفلاح، البحر الرائق: ٥٩١/١] عجز عن العربية إلخ الصحيح أنه يصح الشروع عنده بغير العربية ولو كان قادراً عليها مع الكراهة التحريمية للقادر ؛ لأن الشروع يتعلق بالذكر الخالص، وهو يحصل بكل لسان وفي بعض الكتب ما يفيد: أن صاحبيه رجعا إلى قوله هنا كرجوعه إلى قولهما في القراءة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٨٠] ولا قراءته إلخ لأنه لو كان قادراً، فإنه لا يصح اتفاقاً على الصحيح، وكان أبو حنيفة أولاً يقول بالصحة، ثم رجع عن هذا القول، ووافقهما في عدم الجواز، وهو الحق. [البحر الرائق: ٥٩٠/١] وضع يمينه إلخ لم يذكر كيفية الوضع؛ لأنها لم تذكر في ظاهر الرواية، واختلف فيها، والمختار: أنه يأخذ رسغها بالخنصر والإبهام؛ لأنه يلزم من الأخذ الوضع، ولا ينعكس؛ وهذا لأن الأخبار اختلفت، ذكر في بعضها: الوضع، وفي بعضها الأخذ فكان الجمع بينهما عملاً بالدليلين أولى. [البحر الرائق: ٥٩٢/١] مستفتحا حال من الضمير في "وضع " . ويستفتح إلخ ومعنى سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك": نزهتك . النقص بالتسبيح، وأثبت صفات الكمال لذاتك بالتحميد وتبارك" أي دام وثبت وتنزه اسمك، "وتعالى جدك" أي ارتفع سلطانك وعظمتك وغناك بمكانتك، ولا إله غيرك في الوجود معبوداً بحق. [مراقي الفلاح: ۲۸۱] عن صفات
The Book of Prayer. Page 93. How to compose the prayer. And to the shoulders while saying salam, and suppressing cough as much as possible, and closing his mouth when yawning, and standing (for any duration they can) when 'Hayya 'ala al-falah' is said, and the Imam's starting when 'Qad qamat al-salah' is said. Section on how to compose the prayer. When a man intends to enter the prayer, he takes his hands out from his sleeves, then raises them to the level of his ears, then... for women... he says the takbir without elongation, intending (whichever prayer it is). To the shoulders: i.e., from the etiquette of prayer is the worshiper looking at his shoulders during the salam, which is unrestricted, and is restricted to when he is sighted; if blind or in darkness, he observes the greatness of Allah. 'Musalliman' i.e., while saying 'Al-salamu alaykum'. 'Ma istata'a' is a condition of his ability, so it indicates that if suppressing cough causes harm or disturbs his heart, it is better not to suppress, as in clearing the throat needed to remove phlegm preventing recitation or loudness if he is imam. 'And closing his mouth' i.e., holding it shut, even by taking his lips with his teeth; if he can take his lips with his teeth and does not do so, and covers it with his hand or sleeve, it is disliked. Yawning: opening of the mouth from wind emerging from the stomach due to an illness that occurs in it, causing that. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 277] 'Al-qiyam hin qila' etc.: i.e., from the etiquette is the standing of the people and the Imam if present near the mihrab at the time the muqim says 'Hayya 'ala al-falah'; because the muqim in his statement commands standing, so it is answered. If not present, each row stands when the Imam reaches them in the most apparent view. Maraqi al-Falah with omission: 277. 'Hidha' udhunayhi' i.e., until his thumbs align with his earlobes, and he makes the palms of his hands facing the qiblah, and does not spread his fingers nor close them. The free woman aligns with her shoulders. Maraqi al-Falah abridged: 278. 'He raises concomitantly' Then 'he says takbir' etc. indicates delaying the takbir after raising the hands, which is one of three opinions on it. The first opinion is that it is for the takbir, and Qadi Khan interpreted 'muqaranah' as its beginning and end being at its beginning and end. The second opinion: its time is before the takbir. The third opinion: its time is after the takbir, so he first says takbir then raises his hands. The commentator said: it is the most correct. So if he did not raise his hands until he finished the takbir, he does it because its place has passed; if he remembers during it, he raises. 'Bila madd' etc.: Know that elongation in the takbir either occurs in the word 'Allah' or in the word 'Akbar'. If in 'Allah', then either at its beginning, middle, or end. If at its beginning, it invalidates because it takes the form of a question; even if intentional, he becomes a disbeliever due to doubt in the Majesty. If in its middle, it is correct, except one should not exaggerate; if he exaggerates beyond its natural length (which is the amount of two harakat), it is disliked and does not invalidate according to the chosen view, as in Ibn Amir Hajj; in al-Siraj, it is contrary to what is better. So the dislike is tanzih. If at its end, by fully pronouncing the vowel of the ha', it is a linguistic error and does not invalidate the prayer. And it is valid to start with any pure remembrance of Allah like 'Subhan Allah', and in Persian if unable to recite Arabic; but if able, his starting in Persian is not valid, nor his recitation in it according to the most correct. Then he places his right hand on his left below his navel immediately after the initiating takbir without delay, opening (with the supplication 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika wa tabaraka ismuka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghayruka'), and he opens (with) or the name of one of the children of shaytan. In al-Qunyah: it does not invalidate because it is a full pronunciation, and it is a language of a people. Al-Zayla'i deemed it unlikely, saying it is only permissible in poetry. If the mu'adhdhin does it, the adhan need not be repeated because the matter of adhan is broader. If he does it intentionally, he becomes a disbeliever when intending the meaning; otherwise not, and he seeks forgiveness and repents. If it is at its end, some say his prayer is invalid, and by analogy the start is not valid; some say it does not invalidate. If the worshiper or the swearer or the slaughterer omits the madd in the second lam of the divine name or omits the ha', there is disagreement on the validity of the start, the oath, and the permissibility of the slaughtered animal; so one should not leave that as a precaution. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi summarized). 'Pure for Allah' etc.: so it is not valid with 'Allahumma ighfir li', i.e., with a remembrance mixed with the need of the asker, even if disliked, due to abandoning the wajib which is the wording of takbir. In his saying 'he says takbir' and 'with every remembrance', there is an indication that for the validity of starting, a complete sentence is necessary. The takbir is 'Allahu Akbar', which is a sentence, and complete remembrance is only with a sentence. Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with variation: 279. And in Persian or other languages. [Maraqi al-Falah (280)] The restriction to Persian is not to exclude others, for the correct view is that Persian and others are equal. So then his meaning by Persian is non-Arabic. Maraqi al-Falah, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/591. 'Unable to recite Arabic' etc.: the correct view is that starting in non-Arabic is valid even if one is capable of Arabic, with karahah tahrim for the capable, because starting is related to pure remembrance, and that occurs in every language. In some books, it is indicated that his two students returned to his statement here as he returned to their statement in recitation. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 280] 'Nor recitation in it' etc.: because if he is capable, then it is not valid by consensus according to the correct view. Abu Hanifa initially said it is valid, then retracted from this statement and agreed with them in impermissibility; that is the truth. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/590] 'Placing his right hand on his left' etc.: he did not mention the manner of placement because it was not mentioned in the Zahir al-Riwaya, and there is disagreement on it. The chosen view is that he grasps the wrist with the little finger and thumb, because grasping necessitates placement, but not vice versa. This is because the reports differed; some mention placement, some mention grasping, so combining them by acting on both proofs is more appropriate. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/592] 'Mustaftihan' is a circumstantial accusative referring to the pronoun in 'placed'. 'And he opens' etc.: the meaning of 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika' is 'I declare you free from deficiency by glorification, and I affirm attributes of perfection for Your Essence by praise.' 'Tabaraka' means 'May Your name be permanent, established, and exalted.' 'Ta'ala jadduka' means 'Your sovereignty, magnificence, and self-sufficiency are elevated by Your status.' 'La ilaha ghayruka' means 'There is none worthy of worship in existence besides You.' [Maraqi al-Falah: 281] Regarding attributes.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation (sharh) of the rulings concerning the opening actions of the prayer (salah), specifically covering the raising of the hands, the takbir, the opening supplication (istiftah), and the placement of the hands. The author begins by discussing the etiquette of looking towards the shoulders during the salam and suppressing coughs and yawns, though these are from the preceding section on adab. The core legal content starts with the 'fasl' on how to compose the prayer. The passage first addresses the raising of the hands. The worshiper should raise his hands to the level of his ears, with palms facing the qiblah, fingers neither spread nor closed. This is for men; for free women, the hands are raised to the shoulders. There is an intra-madhhab dispute on the timing of raising the hands relative to the takbir: three views are mentioned — (1) raising hands simultaneously with beginning and ending of takbir (muqaranah), (2) raising before takbir, and (3) raising after takbir. The commentator states that the third view (raising after takbir) is the most correct (asahh). If one forgets to raise until after the takbir, he should still raise as the time has passed; if he remembers during the takbir, he raises. Next, the passage discusses the proper pronunciation of the takbir, specifically the elongation (madd). Elongation in the first letter of 'Allah' (as in alif madd al-istifham) invalidates the prayer and may lead to kufr if intentional. Elongation in the middle letter (the lam) is correct but should not be excessive; excessive elongation (beyond the natural two harakat) is makruh tanzihan but does not invalidate. Elongation at the end (the ha' of Allahu) is a linguistic error but does not invalidate. Detailed cases of omission of madd in specific letters are also mentioned. The passage then covers the validity of starting the prayer with other pure dhikr besides the takbir, and the permissibility of using Persian (or other non-Arabic) if one is unable to recite the Arabic. According to the relied-upon position, the opening (shuru') is valid with non-Arabic even if one is capable of Arabic, though it is makruh tahrimi for the capable. However, recitation of the Quran in non-Arabic by one who is capable is not valid by consensus, and Abu Hanifa later retracted his earlier view to agree with the two students. Finally, the passage addresses the placement of the right hand on the left below the navel after the takbir, without delay, and the recitation of the opening supplication (Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...). The method of placement is not specified in the zahir al-riwayah, but the preferred method is to grasp the wrist with the little finger and thumb. The meaning of the supplication is explained: glorification and praise of Allah, affirmation of the blessedness of His name, and exaltation of His majesty and sufficiency. Throughout, the passage draws on sources such as Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, Maraqi al-Falah, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, and al-Qunyah, indicating that the rulings are from the later authoritative works of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands to the ears or shoulders as a recommended act at the beginning of prayer.
تكبير (takbir): The utterance of 'Allahu Akbar' to commence the prayer; it is wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator in the passage, which opinion is the most correct (asahh) regarding the timing of raising hands?
A) Simultaneous with takbir
B) Before the takbir
C) After the takbir
D) It is not necessary to raise hands

Key Takeaway
The sunnah of raising hands is best performed after completing the opening takbir, though all three timings have valid basis within the Hanafi school.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Proper Pronunciation of the Takbir and Rulings of Madd
Fiqh rulings on the correct pronunciation of the opening takbir, focusing on elongation (madd) and its consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct pronunciation of the takbir, distinguish between permissible and invalidating elongation (madd), and apply the rulings of madd in different positions in the words 'Allah' and 'Akbar'.

Core Idea
Excessive or misplaced elongation in the takbir can invalidate the prayer; the safest pronunciation is a moderate madd in the middle of 'Allah'.

The opening takbir is a wajib act that requires precise pronunciation. This lesson focuses on the rulings of elongation (madd) in the words 'Allah' and 'Akbar', detailing what is permissible, what is disliked, and what may invalidate the prayer or even lead to disbelief if intentional. Understanding these nuances helps you safeguard the validity of your prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of madd in the takbir
Elongation can occur in the word 'Allah' at its beginning (alif), middle (lam), or end (ha'), and in the word 'Akbar' at its beginning.
The passage specifies three locations in 'Allah': first letter, middle, and last letter.
2
Analyze madd in the beginning of 'Allah'
Elongating the first alif turns it into a question form ('a-Allah'), which implies doubt. This invalidates the prayer and, if done intentionally with knowledge, can lead to disbelief.
This is because it sounds like an interrogative, casting doubt on Allah's greatness.
3
Analyze madd in the middle of 'Allah' (lam)
Natural elongation of the lam is correct; excessive elongation beyond two harakat is makruh tanzihan but does not invalidate the prayer.
The passage says 'لا تفسد على المختار' (does not invalidate according to the chosen view).
4
Analyze madd at the end of 'Allah' (ha') and in 'Akbar'
Elongating the ha' (e.g., 'Allahu' instead of 'Allah') is a linguistic error but does not invalidate the prayer. Similarly, madd in 'Akbar' is covered by the same rules.
Some early scholars said it might invalidate, but the preferred view is it does not.
5
Apply the precautionary principle
The passage warns against certain omissions of madd that affect the balance of the word, especially in the second lam of the divine name, and advises caution in oaths and slaughter as well.
The same ruling extends to the swearing of oaths and the slaughter of animals, showing the general legal principle.

كتاب الصلاة ۹۳ كيفية تركيب الصلاة وإلى المنكبين مسلّما، ودفع السعال ما استطاع، وكظم فمه عند التثاؤب، والقيام أي مدة استطاعتهم حين قيل حي على الفلاح، وشروع الإمام مذ قيل: قد قامت الصلاة. فصل في كيفية تركيب الصلاة إذا أراد الرجل الدخول في الصلاة أخرج كفيه من كميه ثم رفعهما حذاء أذنيه، ثم خرج به المرأة كبر بلا مد ناوياً، أي صلاة كانت إلى المنكبين: أي ومن آداب الصلاة نظر المصلي إلى منكبيه حال التسليم أطلقه، وهو مقيد بما إذا كان بصيراً، أما إذا كان أعمى أو في ظلمة فيلاحظ عظمة الله تعالى. مسلّما أي حال كونك قائلا: السلام عليكم. ما استطاع قيد باستطاعته فأفاد أنه إذا كان يحصل للمصلي من دفع السعال ضرر أو يشتغل قلبه بدفعه، فالأولى عدم دفعه كما في تنحنح محتاج إليه لدفع بلغم منعه عن القراءة، أو عن الجهر وهو إمام. وكظم فمه أي إمساكه وسده ولو بأخذ شفتيه بسنه، فإن أمكنه أخذ شفتيه بسنه فلم يفعل وغطاه بيده أو كمه كره. والتثاؤب: انفتاح الفم بريح يخرج من المعدة لمرض من الأمراض يحدث فيها، فيوجب ذلك. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٧٧] والقيام حين قيل إلخ : أي ومن الأدب قيام القوم والإمام إن كان حاضراً بقرب المحراب وقت قول المقيم: "حي على الفلاح"؛ لأن المقيم في ضمن قوله هذا أمر بالقيام فيجاب، وإن لم يكن حاضراً يقوم كل صف حين ينتهي إليه الإمام في الأظهر. مراقي الفلاح بتصرف: ۲۷۷] حذاء أذنيه حتى يحاذي بإبهاميه شحمتي أذنيه، ويجعل باطن كفيه نحو القبلة، ولا يفرج أصابعه ولا يضمها، والمرأة الحرة حذو منكبيها مراقي الفلاح بحذف: ۲۷۸] يرفع مقارنا ثم كبر إلخ أفاد تأخير التكبير عن رفع اليدين، وهو أحد الأقوال الثلاثة فيه، فالقول الأول أنه للتكبير، وفسر قاضي خان" المقارنة بأن تكون بداءته وختمه عند بداءته وختمه، والقول الثاني: وقته قبل التكبير، والقول الثالث: وقته بعد التكبير، فيكبر أولاً ثم يرفع يديه. قال الشارح: هو الأصح، فإذا لم يرفع يديه حتى فرغ من التكبير يأتي به لفوات محله، وإن ذكره في أثنائه رفع. بلا مد إلخ: اعلم أن المد في التكبير إما أن يكون في لفظ "الله" أو في لفظ "أكبر"، فإن كان في لفظ "الله" فإما أن يكون في أوله أو في وسطه أو في آخره، فإن كان في أوله كان مفسداً؛ لأنه في صورة الاستفهام حتى لو تعمده يكفر؛ للشك في الكبرياء، وإن كان في وسطه فهو الصواب، إلا أنه لا يبالغ فيه، فإن بالغ زيادة على مده الطبعي، وهو قدر حركتين، كره، ولا تفسد على المختار، كما في ابن أمير حاج، وفي "السراج": أنه خلاف الأولى. فالكراهة للتنزيه، وإن كان في آخره بأن أشبع حركة الهاء فهو خطأ من حيث اللغة، ولا تفسد به الصلاة، ويصح الشروع بكل ذكر خالص الله تعالى كـ سبحان الله، وبالفارسية، إن عجز عن العربية، وإن قدر لا يصح شروعه بالفارسية، ولا قراءته بها في الأصح، ثم وضع يمينه على يساره تحت سرته عقب التحريمة بلا مهلة مستفتحا وهو أن يقول: "سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك وتبارك اسمك وتعالى جدك ولا إله غيرك"، ويستفتح أو اسم من أسماء أولاد الشيطان، وفي "القنية": لا تفسد ؛ لأنه إشباع، وهو لغة ،قوم، واستبعده "الزيلعي" بأنه لا يجوز إلا في الشعر، ولو فعله المؤذن لا تجب إعادة الأذان؛ لأن أمر الأذان أوسع، وإن تعمده يكفر، أي مع قصد المعنى، وإلا لا، ويستغفر ويتوب، وإن كان في آخره فقيل تفسد صلاته وقياسه أن لا يصح الشروع به، وقيل: لا تفسد. ولو حذف المصلي أو الحالف أو الذابح المد الذي في اللام الثانية من الجلالة أو حذف الهاء، اختلف في صحة الشروع وانعقاد اليمين وحل الذبيحة، فلا يترك ذلك احتياطاً. (حاشية الطحطاوي ملخصا) خالص الله إلخ فلا يصح باللهم اغفر لي أي بذكر يخلص عن اختلاطه بحاجة الطالب وإن كره؛ لترك الواجب، وهو لفظ التكبير، وفي قوله: "كبر" و "بكل ذكر " إشارة إلى أنه لبد لصحة الشروع من جملة تامة، فإن التكبير "الله أكبر" وهو جملة، والذكر التام لا يكون إلا بجملة مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي بتصرف: ٢٧٩] وبالفارسية أو غيرها من الألسن [مراقي الفلاح (۲۸۰] والتقييد بالفارسية ليس للاحتراز عن غيرها، فإن الصحيح أن الفارسية وغيرها سواء، فحينئذ كان مراده من الفارسية غير العربية مراقي الفلاح، البحر الرائق: ٥٩١/١] عجز عن العربية إلخ الصحيح أنه يصح الشروع عنده بغير العربية ولو كان قادراً عليها مع الكراهة التحريمية للقادر ؛ لأن الشروع يتعلق بالذكر الخالص، وهو يحصل بكل لسان وفي بعض الكتب ما يفيد: أن صاحبيه رجعا إلى قوله هنا كرجوعه إلى قولهما في القراءة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٨٠] ولا قراءته إلخ لأنه لو كان قادراً، فإنه لا يصح اتفاقاً على الصحيح، وكان أبو حنيفة أولاً يقول بالصحة، ثم رجع عن هذا القول، ووافقهما في عدم الجواز، وهو الحق. [البحر الرائق: ٥٩٠/١] وضع يمينه إلخ لم يذكر كيفية الوضع؛ لأنها لم تذكر في ظاهر الرواية، واختلف فيها، والمختار: أنه يأخذ رسغها بالخنصر والإبهام؛ لأنه يلزم من الأخذ الوضع، ولا ينعكس؛ وهذا لأن الأخبار اختلفت، ذكر في بعضها: الوضع، وفي بعضها الأخذ فكان الجمع بينهما عملاً بالدليلين أولى. [البحر الرائق: ٥٩٢/١] مستفتحا حال من الضمير في "وضع " . ويستفتح إلخ ومعنى سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك": نزهتك . النقص بالتسبيح، وأثبت صفات الكمال لذاتك بالتحميد وتبارك" أي دام وثبت وتنزه اسمك، "وتعالى جدك" أي ارتفع سلطانك وعظمتك وغناك بمكانتك، ولا إله غيرك في الوجود معبوداً بحق. [مراقي الفلاح: ۲۸۱] عن صفات
The Book of Prayer. Page 93. How to compose the prayer. And to the shoulders while saying salam, and suppressing cough as much as possible, and closing his mouth when yawning, and standing (for any duration they can) when 'Hayya 'ala al-falah' is said, and the Imam's starting when 'Qad qamat al-salah' is said. Section on how to compose the prayer. When a man intends to enter the prayer, he takes his hands out from his sleeves, then raises them to the level of his ears, then... for women... he says the takbir without elongation, intending (whichever prayer it is). To the shoulders: i.e., from the etiquette of prayer is the worshiper looking at his shoulders during the salam, which is unrestricted, and is restricted to when he is sighted; if blind or in darkness, he observes the greatness of Allah. 'Musalliman' i.e., while saying 'Al-salamu alaykum'. 'Ma istata'a' is a condition of his ability, so it indicates that if suppressing cough causes harm or disturbs his heart, it is better not to suppress, as in clearing the throat needed to remove phlegm preventing recitation or loudness if he is imam. 'And closing his mouth' i.e., holding it shut, even by taking his lips with his teeth; if he can take his lips with his teeth and does not do so, and covers it with his hand or sleeve, it is disliked. Yawning: opening of the mouth from wind emerging from the stomach due to an illness that occurs in it, causing that. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 277] 'Al-qiyam hin qila' etc.: i.e., from the etiquette is the standing of the people and the Imam if present near the mihrab at the time the muqim says 'Hayya 'ala al-falah'; because the muqim in his statement commands standing, so it is answered. If not present, each row stands when the Imam reaches them in the most apparent view. Maraqi al-Falah with omission: 277. 'Hidha' udhunayhi' i.e., until his thumbs align with his earlobes, and he makes the palms of his hands facing the qiblah, and does not spread his fingers nor close them. The free woman aligns with her shoulders. Maraqi al-Falah abridged: 278. 'He raises concomitantly' Then 'he says takbir' etc. indicates delaying the takbir after raising the hands, which is one of three opinions on it. The first opinion is that it is for the takbir, and Qadi Khan interpreted 'muqaranah' as its beginning and end being at its beginning and end. The second opinion: its time is before the takbir. The third opinion: its time is after the takbir, so he first says takbir then raises his hands. The commentator said: it is the most correct. So if he did not raise his hands until he finished the takbir, he does it because its place has passed; if he remembers during it, he raises. 'Bila madd' etc.: Know that elongation in the takbir either occurs in the word 'Allah' or in the word 'Akbar'. If in 'Allah', then either at its beginning, middle, or end. If at its beginning, it invalidates because it takes the form of a question; even if intentional, he becomes a disbeliever due to doubt in the Majesty. If in its middle, it is correct, except one should not exaggerate; if he exaggerates beyond its natural length (which is the amount of two harakat), it is disliked and does not invalidate according to the chosen view, as in Ibn Amir Hajj; in al-Siraj, it is contrary to what is better. So the dislike is tanzih. If at its end, by fully pronouncing the vowel of the ha', it is a linguistic error and does not invalidate the prayer. And it is valid to start with any pure remembrance of Allah like 'Subhan Allah', and in Persian if unable to recite Arabic; but if able, his starting in Persian is not valid, nor his recitation in it according to the most correct. Then he places his right hand on his left below his navel immediately after the initiating takbir without delay, opening (with the supplication 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika wa tabaraka ismuka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghayruka'), and he opens (with) or the name of one of the children of shaytan. In al-Qunyah: it does not invalidate because it is a full pronunciation, and it is a language of a people. Al-Zayla'i deemed it unlikely, saying it is only permissible in poetry. If the mu'adhdhin does it, the adhan need not be repeated because the matter of adhan is broader. If he does it intentionally, he becomes a disbeliever when intending the meaning; otherwise not, and he seeks forgiveness and repents. If it is at its end, some say his prayer is invalid, and by analogy the start is not valid; some say it does not invalidate. If the worshiper or the swearer or the slaughterer omits the madd in the second lam of the divine name or omits the ha', there is disagreement on the validity of the start, the oath, and the permissibility of the slaughtered animal; so one should not leave that as a precaution. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi summarized). 'Pure for Allah' etc.: so it is not valid with 'Allahumma ighfir li', i.e., with a remembrance mixed with the need of the asker, even if disliked, due to abandoning the wajib which is the wording of takbir. In his saying 'he says takbir' and 'with every remembrance', there is an indication that for the validity of starting, a complete sentence is necessary. The takbir is 'Allahu Akbar', which is a sentence, and complete remembrance is only with a sentence. Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with variation: 279. And in Persian or other languages. [Maraqi al-Falah (280)] The restriction to Persian is not to exclude others, for the correct view is that Persian and others are equal. So then his meaning by Persian is non-Arabic. Maraqi al-Falah, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/591. 'Unable to recite Arabic' etc.: the correct view is that starting in non-Arabic is valid even if one is capable of Arabic, with karahah tahrim for the capable, because starting is related to pure remembrance, and that occurs in every language. In some books, it is indicated that his two students returned to his statement here as he returned to their statement in recitation. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 280] 'Nor recitation in it' etc.: because if he is capable, then it is not valid by consensus according to the correct view. Abu Hanifa initially said it is valid, then retracted from this statement and agreed with them in impermissibility; that is the truth. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/590] 'Placing his right hand on his left' etc.: he did not mention the manner of placement because it was not mentioned in the Zahir al-Riwaya, and there is disagreement on it. The chosen view is that he grasps the wrist with the little finger and thumb, because grasping necessitates placement, but not vice versa. This is because the reports differed; some mention placement, some mention grasping, so combining them by acting on both proofs is more appropriate. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 1/592] 'Mustaftihan' is a circumstantial accusative referring to the pronoun in 'placed'. 'And he opens' etc.: the meaning of 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika' is 'I declare you free from deficiency by glorification, and I affirm attributes of perfection for Your Essence by praise.' 'Tabaraka' means 'May Your name be permanent, established, and exalted.' 'Ta'ala jadduka' means 'Your sovereignty, magnificence, and self-sufficiency are elevated by Your status.' 'La ilaha ghayruka' means 'There is none worthy of worship in existence besides You.' [Maraqi al-Falah: 281] Regarding attributes.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation (sharh) of the rulings concerning the opening actions of the prayer (salah), specifically covering the raising of the hands, the takbir, the opening supplication (istiftah), and the placement of the hands. The author begins by discussing the etiquette of looking towards the shoulders during the salam and suppressing coughs and yawns, though these are from the preceding section on adab. The core legal content starts with the 'fasl' on how to compose the prayer. The passage first addresses the raising of the hands. The worshiper should raise his hands to the level of his ears, with palms facing the qiblah, fingers neither spread nor closed. This is for men; for free women, the hands are raised to the shoulders. There is an intra-madhhab dispute on the timing of raising the hands relative to the takbir: three views are mentioned — (1) raising hands simultaneously with beginning and ending of takbir (muqaranah), (2) raising before takbir, and (3) raising after takbir. The commentator states that the third view (raising after takbir) is the most correct (asahh). If one forgets to raise until after the takbir, he should still raise as the time has passed; if he remembers during the takbir, he raises. Next, the passage discusses the proper pronunciation of the takbir, specifically the elongation (madd). Elongation in the first letter of 'Allah' (as in alif madd al-istifham) invalidates the prayer and may lead to kufr if intentional. Elongation in the middle letter (the lam) is correct but should not be excessive; excessive elongation (beyond the natural two harakat) is makruh tanzihan but does not invalidate. Elongation at the end (the ha' of Allahu) is a linguistic error but does not invalidate. Detailed cases of omission of madd in specific letters are also mentioned. The passage then covers the validity of starting the prayer with other pure dhikr besides the takbir, and the permissibility of using Persian (or other non-Arabic) if one is unable to recite the Arabic. According to the relied-upon position, the opening (shuru') is valid with non-Arabic even if one is capable of Arabic, though it is makruh tahrimi for the capable. However, recitation of the Quran in non-Arabic by one who is capable is not valid by consensus, and Abu Hanifa later retracted his earlier view to agree with the two students. Finally, the passage addresses the placement of the right hand on the left below the navel after the takbir, without delay, and the recitation of the opening supplication (Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...). The method of placement is not specified in the zahir al-riwayah, but the preferred method is to grasp the wrist with the little finger and thumb. The meaning of the supplication is explained: glorification and praise of Allah, affirmation of the blessedness of His name, and exaltation of His majesty and sufficiency. Throughout, the passage draws on sources such as Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, Maraqi al-Falah, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, and al-Qunyah, indicating that the rulings are from the later authoritative works of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مد (madd): Elongation of a vowel sound in the takbir; improper extension can affect validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on elongating the middle lam of 'Allah' beyond its natural length (more than two harakat)?
A) It invalidates the prayer.
B) It is makruh tanzihan and does not invalidate.
C) It is permissible and even recommended.
D) It is wajib to avoid any elongation.

Key Takeaway
The critical point in takbir pronunciation is to avoid elongating the first alif of 'Allah'; moderate middle elongation is fine but excessive is disliked, and end elongation is a linguistic error that does not invalidate.

Validity of the Opening Takbir: Pure Dhikr and Language
Ruling on what suffices for the opening takbir and validity of Persian

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on what constitutes a valid opening takbir, distinguish between pure dhikr and mixed supplication, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the use of Persian.

Core Idea
The opening takbir is wajib; only pure dhikr suffices, and using Persian is invalid if one can say Arabic.

The opening takbir is the act that begins the prayer. This passage from Nur al-Idah and its commentary clarifies what phrases are valid for this takbir and whether one may use a language other than Arabic. The discussion reveals an interesting intra-Hanafi dispute where Imam Abu Hanifa initially held a different view before retracting it. Understanding this ruling ensures that your prayer's very first act is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify what constitutes a valid opening takbir
The takbir must be a pure dhikr (remembrance) dedicated solely to Allah, without any supplication or worldly intent. It must be a complete sentence, like 'Allahu Akbar' or 'Subhan Allah'.
A phrase like 'Allahumma ghfir li' is not pure because it includes a request.
2
Distinguish between pure dhikr and mixed supplication
Pure dhikr is praise of Allah without any element of asking. The passage explicitly states that 'Allahumma ghfir li' is invalid because it is mixed with the supplicant's need. This distinction is crucial for validity.
Even though 'Allahumma ghfir li' contains Allah's name, it is not considered pure dhikr.
3
Understand the ruling for the able vs. unable regarding language
If a person can pronounce the Arabic takbir, using any other language (such as Persian) invalidates the beginning of prayer. If unable (e.g., due to a speech impediment or ignorance), any language is valid, with prohibitive dislike (makruh tahrimi) for the able who still choose another language.
The commentary notes that even for the able, if one uses another language, the prayer is valid but severely disliked.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa originally held that Persian was valid even for the able. His two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, held it invalid. Later, Abu Hanifa retracted his view and agreed with them. This is a classic example of a tarjih within the madhhab.
The mufta bihi position follows the final agreement: for the able, only Arabic is valid.
5
Determine the mufta bihi ruling
The operative ruling for fatwa: if one can say 'Allahu Akbar' in Arabic, any other phrase (even 'Subhan Allah' in Arabic) is valid but makruh tahrimi because it abandons the wajib takbir. Using Persian is invalid for the able.
The later Hanafi authorities, like al-Marghinani, follow the final position of Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كيفية تركيب الصلاة ويصح الشروع بكل ذكر خالص الله تعالى كــ سبحان الله، وبالفارسية، إن عجز عن العربية، وإن قدر لا يصح شروعه بالفارسية، ولا قراءته بها في الأصح. (حاشية الطحطاوي ملخصا) خالص الله إلخ فلا يصح باللهم اغفر لي أي بذكر يخلص عن اختلاطه بحاجة الطالب وإن كره؛ لترك الواجب، وهو لفظ التكبير، وفي قوله: "كبر" و "بكل ذكر " إشارة إلى أنه لابد لصحة الشروع من جملة تامة، فإن التكبير "الله أكبر" وهو جملة، والذكر التام لا يكون إلا بجملة مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي بتصرف: ٢٧٩] وبالفارسية أو غيرها من الألسن [مراقي الفلاح (۲۸۰] والتقييد بالفارسية ليس للاحتراز عن غيرها، فإن الصحيح أن الفارسية وغيرها سواء، فحينئذ كان مراده من الفارسية غير العربية مراقي الفلاح، البحر الرائق: ٥٩١/١] عجز عن العربية إلخ الصحيح أنه يصح الشروع عنده بغير العربية ولو كان قادراً عليها مع الكراهة التحريمية للقادر ؛ لأن الشروع يتعلق بالذكر الخالص، وهو يحصل بكل لسان وفي بعض الكتب ما يفيد: أن صاحبيه رجعا إلى قوله هنا كرجوعه إلى قولهما في القراءة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٢٨٠] ولا قراءته إلخ لأنه لو كان قادراً، فإنه لا يصح اتفاقاً على الصحيح، وكان أبو حنيفة أولاً يقول بالصحة، ثم رجع عن هذا القول، ووافقهما في عدم الجواز، وهو الحق.
The manner of constructing the prayer. It is valid to begin with any pure remembrance of Allah, such as 'Subhan Allah', and in Persian if unable to Arabic. If he is able, beginning with Persian is not valid, nor reading in it according to the most correct. (Summary from Hashiyah al-Tahtawi) 'Pure for Allah' etc.: so it is not valid with 'Allahumma ghfir li' (O Allah forgive me) because it is a remembrance mixed with the need of the supplicant, even if disliked due to abandoning the obligation, which is the wording of takbir. In his statement 'takbir' and 'with every remembrance' there is an indication that for the validity of beginning (the prayer) a complete sentence is necessary, for the takbir is 'Allahu akbar' which is a sentence, and a complete remembrance is only with a sentence. (...) And regarding Persian or other languages, the correct view is that beginning (prayer) with other than Arabic is valid in his opinion even if one is able to do it (in Arabic), albeit with prohibitive dislike for the able one, because beginning (prayer) is connected to pure remembrance, and that is attained in every language. In some books it is reported that his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) reverted to his statement here just as he reverted to their statement regarding recitation. And regarding recitation: if he is able, it is not valid by agreement according to the correct view. Abu Hanifa initially said it was valid, then he retracted this statement and agreed with them on its impermissibility, and that is the truth.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the opening takbir of prayer. The author states that any pure dhikr dedicated to Allah is valid to begin prayer, but only if one is unable to recite the Arabic takbir. If one can say 'Allahu Akbar', using Persian or any other language is invalid. The commentary expands: the remembrance must be pure and not mixed with supplication. For example, 'O Allah forgive me' is mixed with one's need, so it is not suitable as a takbir. The takbir must be a complete sentence like 'Allahu Akbar'. The commentary discusses the use of Persian: even if one can say Arabic, beginning in Persian with the ability is valid but severely disliked (makruh tahrimi). Abu Hanifa initially held it valid, then retracted to agree with his companions on its impermissibility. This ruling shows the evolution of the madhhab on this issue.

Key Terms
ذكر خالص (dhikr khalis): Pure remembrance of Allah without any worldly intention or mixing with supplication.
الشروع (al-shuru'): The act of beginning the prayer with the opening takbir.
الكراهة التحريمية (al-karahah al-tahrimiyyah): Prohibitive dislike; an act that is closer to haram and should be avoided.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person is unable to pronounce Arabic due to a speech impediment, can he begin prayer with the Persian phrase 'Khuda Akbar'?
A) Yes, any language is valid for the unable.
B) No, only Arabic is valid for the takbir.
C) Yes, but only if he also says 'Allahu Akbar' silently.
D) No, because 'Khuda Akbar' is not a complete sentence.

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir is wajib; it must be pure dhikr in a complete sentence, and for those able to pronounce Arabic, only Arabic is valid; for the unable, any language suffices.

Hand Placement After Takbir: Sunnah and the Method of Taking the Wrist
Ruling on hand placement after takbir and the method of taking the wrist

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hand placement in salah, describe the preferred method of taking the wrist, and explain the evidence from conflicting hadith reports.

Core Idea
Placing the right hand on the left under the navel is sunnah; the chosen method combines both placement and taking the wrist.

This passage from Nur al-Idah states the ruling on hand placement after the opening takbir. While the basic act is sunnah, the exact manner was not specified in the core texts, leading to ikhtilaf. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi preferred method and the reasoning behind it, based on reconciling conflicting hadith reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is placing the right hand on the left after takbir. Its ruling is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
Omitting it does not invalidate the prayer but reduces reward.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence comes from multiple hadith reports; some mention 'placement', some mention 'taking'.
The texts are not directly quoted but inferred from general practice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Hanafi jurists combine both reports by requiring taking the wrist, because taking entails placement, but not vice versa.
This is an application of the principle of acting on all evidence when possible.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) place hands on the chest; Hanafi places under the navel. The method of taking the wrist is preferred to reconcile the hadith.
The mufta bihi is under navel with wrist grasping.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم وضع يمينه ونحوها أي لا يصح على يساره تحت سرته عقب التحريمة بلا مهلة مستفتحا وهو أن يقول: "سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك وتبارك اسمك وتعالى جدك ولا إله غيرك". (وضع يمينه إلخ لم يذكر كيفية الوضع؛ لأنها لم تذكر في ظاهر الرواية، واختلف فيها، والمختار: أنه يأخذ رسغها بالخنصر والإبهام؛ لأنه يلزم من الأخذ الوضع، ولا ينعكس؛ وهذا لأن الأخبار اختلفت، ذكر في بعضها: الوضع، وفي بعضها الأخذ فكان الجمع بينهما عملاً بالدليلين أولى. [البحر الرائق: ٥٩٢/١] مستفتحا حال من الضمير في "وضع" . ويستفتح إلخ ومعنى سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك: نزهتك النقص بالتسبيح، وأثبت صفات الكمال لذاتك بالتحميد. وتبارك أي دام وثبت وتنزه اسمك، وتعالى جدك أي ارتفع سلطانك وعظمتك وغناك بمكانتك، ولا إله غيرك في الوجود معبوداً بحق. [مراقي الفلاح: ۲۸۱]
Then he places his right hand (and the like) i.e. it is not valid, on his left hand under his navel immediately after the tahrimah without delay, opening (the supplication), which is that he says: 'Glory be to You, O Allah, and all praise is Yours; blessed is Your name, exalted is Your majesty, and there is no deity worthy of worship other than You.' This is because the reports differ: some mention 'placement' and some mention 'taking'; so combining both by acting on both proofs is better. He opens etc.: The meaning of 'Subhanakallahumma wa bihamdika' is: I declare You free from imperfection by tasbih, and I affirm attributes of perfection for Your essence by tahmid. 'Tabaraka' means enduring, established, and pure is Your name. 'Ta'ala jadduka' means high is Your authority, greatness, and self-sufficiency in Your station. There is no god other than You truly worshipped in existence. [Maraqi al-Falah]

Commentary
This passage explains the actions after the opening takbir. First, the worshiper places his right hand on his left hand below the navel immediately after takbir, without delay, and simultaneously begins the opening supplication (istiftah). The author notes that the exact manner of placing was not specified in the core texts (zahir al-riwayah), so there is ikhtilaf. The preferred method is to grasp the wrist of the left hand with the little finger and thumb of the right, as this combines both 'placing' and 'taking' reported in ahadith. The opening supplication is the well-known 'Subhanakallahumma...', which praises Allah, declares His attributes, and affirms His uniqueness. The passage emphasizes that the prayer begins with a pure remembrance of Allah.

Key Terms
الرَّسغ (al-rusgh): The wrist joint; the place where the hand meets the forearm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school chooses to take the wrist when placing hands to reconcile conflicting hadith reports.

The Opening Supplication (Istiftah) in Salah: Wording and Meaning
Ruling on reciting the opening supplication and its meaning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recite the Hanafi opening supplication, explain the meaning of its phrases, and state its ruling (sunnah muakkadah).

Core Idea
The opening supplication 'Subhanakallahumma wa bihamdika...' is sunnah muakkadah recited quietly after takbir.

After placing hands, the worshiper begins the opening supplication (istiftah). This lesson covers the specific wording used in the Hanafi school and the explanations of its phrases as given by the classical commentators. Understanding the meaning enhances khushu' in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Reciting the opening supplication is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
Omission does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Recite the exact wording
The Hanafi istiftah is: 'Subhanakallahumma wa bihamdika wa tabaraka ismuka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghayruk.'
This wording is from the Sunnah.
3
Understand the meaning
The commentary interprets each phrase: 'Subhanaka' is declaration of transcendence, 'wa bihamdika' is praise, 'tabaraka' means enduring and blessed, 'ta'ala jadduka' means exalted is Your majesty, 'la ilaha ghayruk' is the shahada.
Knowing the meaning increases presence of heart.
4
Apply the ruling
In every rak'ah (except the first, it is only after takbir), recite this silently before al-Fatihah.
If one forgets, there is no need for sujood as-sahw because it is sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم وضع يمينه ونحوها أي لا يصح على يساره تحت سرته عقب التحريمة بلا مهلة مستفتحا وهو أن يقول: "سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك وتبارك اسمك وتعالى جدك ولا إله غيرك". (وضع يمينه إلخ لم يذكر كيفية الوضع؛ لأنها لم تذكر في ظاهر الرواية، واختلف فيها، والمختار: أنه يأخذ رسغها بالخنصر والإبهام؛ لأنه يلزم من الأخذ الوضع، ولا ينعكس؛ وهذا لأن الأخبار اختلفت، ذكر في بعضها: الوضع، وفي بعضها الأخذ فكان الجمع بينهما عملاً بالدليلين أولى. [البحر الرائق: ٥٩٢/١] مستفتحا حال من الضمير في "وضع" . ويستفتح إلخ ومعنى سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك: نزهتك النقص بالتسبيح، وأثبت صفات الكمال لذاتك بالتحميد. وتبارك أي دام وثبت وتنزه اسمك، وتعالى جدك أي ارتفع سلطانك وعظمتك وغناك بمكانتك، ولا إله غيرك في الوجود معبوداً بحق. [مراقي الفلاح: ۲۸۱]
Then he places his right hand (and the like) i.e. it is not valid, on his left hand under his navel immediately after the tahrimah without delay, opening (the supplication), which is that he says: 'Glory be to You, O Allah, and all praise is Yours; blessed is Your name, exalted is Your majesty, and there is no deity worthy of worship other than You.' (Regarding placing his right hand etc.: the manner of placement was not mentioned because it was not mentioned in the zahir al-riwayah, and there is difference of opinion on it. The chosen opinion is that he takes the wrist with his little finger and thumb, because from taking, placement is entailed, but not vice versa. This is because the reports differ: some mention 'placement' and some mention 'taking'; so combining both by acting on both proofs is better. [Bahr al-Ra'iq 1/592] 'Opening' is a condition of the pronoun in 'he placed'. He opens etc.: The meaning of 'Subhanakallahumma wa bihamdika' is: I declare You free from imperfection by tasbih, and I affirm attributes of perfection for Your essence by tahmid. 'Tabaraka' means enduring, established, and pure is Your name. 'Ta'ala jadduka' means high is Your authority, greatness, and self-sufficiency in Your station. There is no god other than You truly worshipped in existence. [Maraqi al-Falah]
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage explains the actions after the opening takbir. First, the worshiper places his right hand on his left hand below the navel immediately after takbir, without delay, and simultaneously begins the opening supplication (istiftah). The author notes that the exact manner of placing was not specified in the core texts (zahir al-riwayah), so there is ikhtilaf. The preferred method is to grasp the wrist of the left hand with the little finger and thumb of the right, as this combines both 'placing' and 'taking' reported in ahadith. The opening supplication is the well-known 'Subhanakallahumma...', which praises Allah, declares His attributes, and affirms His uniqueness. The passage emphasizes that the prayer begins with a pure remembrance of Allah.

Key Terms
الاستفتاح (al-istiftah): The opening supplication said after the takbir tahrimah, specifically 'Subhanakallahumma...'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on reciting the opening supplication (istiftah) in salah?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah muakkadah
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi istiftah is a sunnah supplication that praises Allah and affirms His uniqueness.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Ta'awwudh and Basmalah: Rulings for Imam, Follower, and Latecomer
Rulings on ta'awwudh and basmalah in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on ta'awwudh and basmalah in prayer for the imam, muqtadi, and masbuq, and apply them to real scenarios.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh is sunnah for imam and munfarid; the muqtadi does not say it because he follows the imam's recitation.

This lesson examines the opening recitations in salah: the ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) and the basmalah. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the imam, the one praying alone, the latecomer, and the follower. Understanding these distinctions prevents common errors in congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify who recites ta'awwudh
The text states 'kull musallin' but then excludes the muqtadi. Identify the categories: imam, munfarid, masbuq, muqtadi.
The muqtadi does not recite any opening supplications.
2
Determine the ruling for the masbuq
The masbuq says ta'awwudh if he joins before the imam begins recitation. If the imam has begun, he leaves it.
The relied view is to omit ta'awwudh if the imam has started recitation, even silently.
3
Apply the ruling for basmalah
Basmalah is said before al-Fatihah in every rak'ah, not between al-Fatihah and the surah.
It is a sunnah, not a verse of the Fatihah in the Hanafi school.
4
Note the exception for Eid takbirs
Ta'awwudh is delayed until after the extra takbirs of the two Eid prayers.
This applies to Eid prayer only.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كل مصلّ، ثم يتعوّذ سرا، فيأتي به المسبوق لا المقتدي، ويؤخر عن تكبيرات العيدين، ثم يسمّي سرا، ويسمي في كل ركعة قبل الفاتحة فقط، ثم قرأ الفاتحة وأمن الإمام أي قال: آمين والمأموم سرًّا، ثم قرأ سورةً أو ثلاث آيات، ثم كبر راكعاً مطمئناً، مسوّيا رأسه بعجزه آخذا ركبتيه بيديه مفرّجا أصابعه وسبح فيه ثلاثا، وذلك أدناه، ثم رفع رأسه واطمأن قائلا: "سمع الله لمن حمده، ربنا لك الحمد" لو إماما أو منفردا، والمقتدي يكتفي بالتحميد، ثم كبر خاراً للسجود، ثم وضع ركبتيه ثم يديه ثم وجهه بين كفيه وسجد مطمئنا مسبحا ثلاثا، وذلك أدناه، وجافي بطنه عن فخذيه وعضديه عن إبطيه في غير زحمة موجها أصابع يديه ورجليه نحو القبلة، والمرأة تخفض، وتلزق بطنها بفخذيها، وجلس بين السجدتين واضعا يديه على فخذيه مطمئنا، ثم كبر وسجد مطمئنا وسجد فيه ثلاثا، وجافي بطنه عن فخذيه، وأبدى عضديه، كل مصل: عممه فشمل كل مصلّ، سواء كان مقتدياً أو غيره، وجهرية كانت الصلاة أو سرية، وإن أدركه راكعا تحرى، إن كان أكثر رأيه أنه إن أتى به أدركه في شيء منه أتى به وإلا لا وأطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يبدأ الإمام بالقراءة، وأما إذا بدأ ولو سرية على المعتمد تركه لا المقتدي: لأنه تابع للقراءة، ولا يقرأ المقتدي. مراقي الفلاح: ۲۸۲] ثم يسمّي [سواء صلى فرضا أو نفلا] كل من يقرأ في صلاته. [مراقي الفلاح: ۲۸۲] فقط أشار إلى أن التسمية لا تسن بين الفاتحة والسورة ولا كراهة فيها إن فعلها اتفاقاً للسورة، سواء جهر أو خافت بالسورة، وغلط من قال: لا يسمي إلا في الركعة الأولى. [مراقي الفلاح بتغيير: ٢٨٢] راكعاً: فيبتدئ بالتكبير الانحناء، ويختمه بختمه؛ ليشرع في التسبيح، فلا تخلو حالة من حالات الصلاة عن ذكر. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٨٢] ركبتيه إلخ ويكون الرجل مفرجاً أصابعه ناصباً ساقيه، وإحناؤهما شبه القوس مكروه، والمرأة لا تفرج أصابعها. مراقي الفلاح: ۲۸۲] ربنا لك الحمد والأفضل: اللهم ربنا ولك الحمد. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٨٣] خاراً: اسم فاعل من الخرور أي ساقطا مسبحاً ثلاثاً بأن يقول: سبحان ربي الأعلى. [مراقي الفلاح: ۲۸۳] وأبدى ماض من الإبداء وهو الإظهار.
Every praying person (then seeks refuge secretly; the masbuq (latecomer) brings it, not the muqtadi (follower); and it is delayed for the takbirs of the two 'Ids). Then he says the basmalah secretly, and he says the basmalah in every rak'ah only before al-Fatihah. Then he recites al-Fatihah and says 'Amin' – the imam says Amin aloud? Actually the text says 'the imam said: Amin and the follower secretly'. Then he recites a surah or three verses. Then he says takbir while bowing (raki'an), with tranquility, making his head level with his back, grasping his knees with his hands, spreading his fingers, and he says tasbih therein three times, and that is the minimum. Then he raises his head and stands with tranquility saying: 'Allah hears the one who praises Him, our Lord, to You is all praise' if he is an imam or alone; the follower suffices with the tahmid. Then he says takbir falling down for prostration, then places his knees, then his hands, then his face between his palms, and prostrates with tranquility, making tasbih three times, and that is the minimum; and he distances his stomach from his thighs and his arms from his sides unless there is crowding; directing the fingers of his hands and feet towards the qibla. The woman lowers herself, sticks her belly to her thighs, and sits between the two prostrations placing her hands on her thighs with tranquility; then says takbir and prostrates with tranquility and makes tasbih three times; distances his stomach from his thighs and exposes his arms. Every praying person: general, including muqtadi and others, whether the prayer is loud or silent. If he (the latecomer) catches the imam in ruku', he estimates; if his preponderant opinion is that if he (the imam) brings it he will catch something of it, he brings it, otherwise no. This is restricted to when the imam has not begun recitation; if he has, even silently according to the relied opinion, he leaves it. The muqtadi (does not recite) because he follows the recitation, and the muqtadi does not recite. Then he says the basmalah (whether praying fard or nafl) everyone who recites in his prayer. [Maraqi al-Falah 282] 'Only' indicates that the basmalah is not sunna between al-Fatihah and the surah, and there is no dislike if one does it. It is agreed for the surah, whether he recites aloud or quietly. And he is mistaken who says: one only says the basmalah in the first rak'ah. [Maraqi al-Falah 282] 'Bowing': he begins the takbir with the bending and concludes it with the completion of bending, so that he may begin the tasbih; thus no state of the prayer is without remembrance. [Maraqi al-Falah 282] 'His knees etc.': the man spreads his fingers and straightens his legs; bending them like a bow is disliked; the woman does not spread her fingers. [Maraqi al-Falah 282] 'Rabbana laka al-hamd', and better is 'Allahumma Rabbana wa laka al-hamd'. [Maraqi al-Falah 283] 'Khārran': active participle from al-khurur, meaning falling. 'Making tasbih three times' by saying 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la'. [Maraqi al-Falah 283] 'Abda' is past tense from al-ibda' meaning to expose.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This long passage describes the actions of prayer in sequence after the opening. First, the worshipper seeks refuge in Allah secretly (ta'awwudh). This is done by every praying person, but the latecomer (masbuq) says it when he joins, while the follower (muqtadi) does not say it because he is following the imam's recitation. It is delayed after the Eid takbirs. Then the basmalah is said secretly before al-Fatihah in every rak'ah. The basmalah is not said between al-Fatihah and the surah, but doing so is not disliked. Then al-Fatihah is recited, followed by Amin (silently according to the Hanafi school, even though the imam may say it aloud? The text clarifies that the imam says Amin and the follower says it secretly). Then a surah or three verses are recited. The ruku' follows with specific postures: the head level with the back, hands on knees, fingers spread. The minimum tasbih in ruku' is three times. After raising, the imam or alone person says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, Rabbana laka al-hamd', while the follower only says the tahmid. Then the prostration: falling down, placing knees first, then hands, then face, with tasbih three times. The stomach and arms are lifted, and fingers point towards qibla. Women are more compact. Between the two prostrations, one sits with tranquility, then a second sajdah. The passage includes details for the latecomer: he estimates the ruku' and joins if he thinks he can catch it, but if the imam started recitation, he should not start ta'awwudh.

Key Terms
التعوذ (al-ta'awwudh): Seeking refuge in Allah from shaytan by saying 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim'.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A latecomer who joins the prayer after the imam has already started.
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The follower who is praying behind the imam from the beginning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who does NOT recite ta'awwudh?
A) The imam
B) The munfarid (one praying alone)
C) The muqtadi (follower)
D) The masbuq (latecomer)

Key Takeaway
Ta'awwudh is sunnah for the imam and the one praying alone; the muqtadi omits it, and the masbuq recites it only if he catches the imam before recitation begins.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Recitation of Fatihah, Amin, and Additional Surah
Rulings on recitation of Fatihah, Amin, and surah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on reciting al-Fatihah, saying Amin, and reciting a surah after Fatihah, and distinguish the roles of imam and follower.

Core Idea
Al-Fatihah is wajib in every rak'ah; the imam says Amin aloud, the follower says it silently.

This lesson focuses on the core recitation component of salah: al-Fatihah, the Amin, and the additional surah. The Hanafi school treats al-Fatihah as a wajib, not a rukn, meaning its omission requires sujud al-sahw. The Amin is also wajib for the imam and follower, but with different modes.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling on al-Fatihah
Reciting al-Fatihah is wajib in every rak'ah of fard and nafl. Missing it invalidates the recitation and requires sujud al-sahw.
It is not a rukn; the prayer is still valid but must be compensated.
2
Explain the Amin
The imam says Amin aloud, the follower says it secretly. Amin is a supplication, not a verse of the Fatihah.
Saying Amin is also wajib; omitting it requires sujud al-sahw.
3
Determine the recitation of a surah
After Fatihah, a surah or three verses are recited in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayer, and in every rak'ah of nafl.
This is sunnah; omitting it does not require sujud al-sahw.
4
Note the follower's role
The muqtadi does not recite Fatihah or any other Quran; he listens silently to the imam.
This is based on the Quranic command 'When the Qur'an is recited, listen to it and be silent'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms
الفاتحة (al-Fatihah): The opening chapter of the Quran; its recitation is wajib in every rak'ah of prayer.
آمين (Amin): A supplication meaning 'O Allah, answer'; said after al-Fatihah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Aloud
B) Secretly
C) Not at all
D) Only if the imam is silent

Key Takeaway
Al-Fatihah is wajib and must be recited; the imam says Amin aloud, the follower says it secretly; recitation of a surah after Fatihah is sunnah.

Ruku' and Sujud: Postures, Tasbih, and the Latecomer's Role
Rulings on ruku' and sujud postures, tasbih, and masbuq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi postures and tasbih for ruku' and sujud, and apply the ruling for the latecomer joining the ruku'.

Core Idea
Ruku' and sujud are arkan; tranquility is wajib; the latecomer may join the ruku' if he catches the imam before he raises.

This lesson covers the physical postures of ruku' and sujud, the required tasbih, and a special ruling for the masbuq who joins the imam during ruku'. The Hanafi school emphasizes tranquility (itminan) and specific positions for men and women.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rukn and wajib in ruku'
Ruku' itself is a rukn; tranquility (itminan) and tasbih (at least once) are wajib.
Omitting tranquility makes the prayer deficient; omitting tasbih requires sujud al-sahw.
2
Describe the posture of ruku'
The man's head is level with his back, hands on knees with fingers spread, legs straight. Women do not spread fingers.
Bending legs like a bow is makruh.
3
Describe the posture of sujud
Place knees, then hands, then face. Prostrate on seven limbs. Men lift arms and stomach; women are compact. Fingers point to qibla.
In crowded conditions, men may relax the distancing.
4
Apply the ruling for the masbuq joining in ruku'
If the masbuq catches the imam in ruku' and believes he can join before the imam raises, he joins; otherwise he waits for the next rak'ah.
If the imam has begun recitation, the masbuq should not start ta'awwudh or Fatihah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[مراقي الفلاح: ۲۸۲] فقط أشار إلى أن التسمية لا تسن بين الفاتحة والسورة ولا كراهة فيها إن فعلها اتفاقاً للسورة، سواء جهر أو خافت بالسورة، وغلط من قال: لا يسمي إلا في الركعة الأولى. [مراقي الفلاح بتغيير: ٢٨٢] راكعاً: فيبتدئ بالتكبير الانحناء، ويختمه بختمه؛ ليشرع في التسبيح، فلا تخلو حالة من حالات الصلاة عن ذكر. [مراقي الفلاح: ٢٨٢] ركبتيه إلخ ويكون الرجل مفرجاً أصابعه ناصباً ساقيه، وإحناؤهما شبه القوس مكروه، والمرأة لا تفرج أصابعها. مراقي الفلاح: ۲۸۲] ربنا لك الحمد والأفضل: اللهم ربنا ولك الحمد. It is agreed for the surah, whether he recites aloud or quietly. And he is mistaken who says: one only says the basmalah in the first rak'ah. [Maraqi al-Falah 282] 'Bowing': he begins the takbir with the bending and concludes it with the completion of bending, so that he may begin the tasbih; thus no state of the prayer is without remembrance. Commentary
This long passage describes the actions of prayer in sequence after the opening. First, the worshipper seeks refuge in Allah secretly (ta'awwudh). This is done by every praying person, but the latecomer (masbuq) says it when he joins, while the follower (muqtadi) does not say it because he is following the imam's recitation. It is delayed after the Eid takbirs. Then the basmalah is said secretly before al-Fatihah in every rak'ah. The basmalah is not said between al-Fatihah and the surah, but doing so is not disliked. Then al-Fatihah is recited, followed by Amin (silently according to the Hanafi school, even though the imam may say it aloud? The text clarifies that the imam says Amin and the follower says it secretly). Then a surah or three verses are recited. The ruku' follows with specific postures: the head level with the back, hands on knees, fingers spread. The minimum tasbih in ruku' is three times. After raising, the imam or alone person says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, Rabbana laka al-hamd', while the follower only says the tahmid. Then the prostration: falling down, placing knees first, then hands, then face, with tasbih three times. The stomach and arms are lifted, and fingers point towards qibla. Women are more compact. Between the two prostrations, one sits with tranquility, then a second sajdah. The passage includes details for the latecomer: he estimates the ruku' and joins if he thinks he can catch it, but if the imam started recitation, he should not start ta'awwudh.

Key Terms
الركوع (al-rukū'): Bowing in prayer; a rukn of salah.
السجود (al-sujūd): Prostration; a rukn of salah performed on seven limbs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Ruku' and sujud are arkan; tranquility and tasbih are wajib; the latecomer may join ruku' if he estimates he can catch it.

Sequence of Prayer Actions in the First Rak'ah
Detailed description of compulsory and recommended actions from ta'awwudh to sitting between sujud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of compulsory and recommended actions in the first rak'ah and identify the legal status (wajib/sunnah) of each action.

Core Idea
Tranquility (ithmi'nan) is wajib in every posture, and the minimum tasbih in ruku and sujud is three.

This lesson walks you through the detailed sequence of the first rak'ah of prayer as described in Nur al-Idah. You will learn each action, from ta'awwudh to the second prostration, along with the specific rulings for the imam, follower, latecomer, and women. Pay close attention to the differences in posture and recitation, as these affect the validity of your prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequential stages
Break the first rak'ah into major stages: standing (qiyam), bowing (ruku), rising, prostrating (sujud) twice, and sitting between prostrations. List them in order.
The sequence begins after takbirat al-ihram, which is not detailed here, but is assumed.
2
Determine the legal status of each action
For each stage, note whether the action is wajib (obligatory) or sunnah (recommended) based on the text. For example, reciting al-Fatiha is wajib, while tasbih in ruku is sunnah with three as the minimum.
The text says 'وذلك أدناه' (that is its minimum) for tasbih, indicating sunnah.
3
Account for the role of the worshiper
Distinguish between the imam, follower (muqtadi), and latecomer (masbuq) regarding recitations like Ameen and ta'awwudh. The imam says Ameen aloud, the follower silently; the latecomer recites ta'awwudh, but not the follower.
The text explicitly says 'فيتعوذ سرا، فيأتي به المسبوق لا المقتدي'.
4
Note gender-specific variations
Identify how the woman's posture differs from the man's in ruku and sujud. The man spreads fingers and distances limbs; the woman is compact.
The text says 'والمرأة تخفض، وتلزق بطنها...'.
5
Synthesize the complete movement
Combine all the parts into a coherent sequence, ensuring tranquility at each posture. Summarize the first rak'ah from standing to standing again.
The second rak'ah is like the first except that thana' and ta'awwudh are omitted.

كيفية تركيب الصلاة كل مصلّ، ثم يتعوّذ سرا، فيأتي به المسبوق لا المقتدي، ويؤخر عن تكبيرات العيدين، التعوذ ثم يسمّي سرا، ويسمي في كل ركعة قبل الفاتحة فقط، ثم قرأ الفاتحة وأمن الإمام أي قال: آمين والمأموم سرًّا، ثم قرأ سورةً أو ثلاث آيات، ثم كبر راكعاً مطمئناً، مسوّيا رأسه بعجزه كل مصل اسم فاعل من التسوية آخذا ركبتيه بيديه مفرّجا أصابعه وسبح فيه ثلاثا، وذلك أدناه، ثم رفع رأسه واطمأن الركوع قائلا: "سمع الله لمن حمده، ربنا لك الحمد" لو إماما أو منفردا، والمقتدي يكتفي بالتحميد، ثم كبر خاراً للسجود، ثم وضع ركبتيه ثم يديه ثم وجهه بين كفيه وسجد بأنفه مطمئنا وجبهته مسبحا ثلاثا، وذلك أدناه، وجافي بطنه عن فخذيه وعضديه عن أي باعد إبطيه في غير زحمة موجها أصابع يديه ورجليه نحو القبلة، والمرأة تخفض، وتلزق بطنها فتضم عضديها لجنبيها ويضمها كل الضم بفخذيها، وجلس بين السجدتين واضعا يديه على فخذيه مطمئنا، ثم كبر وسجد مطمئنا وسبح فيه ثلاثا، وجافي بطنه في السجود أي باعد عن فخذيه، وأبدى عضديه، بعد التكبير كل مصل: عممه فشمل كل مصلّ، سواء كان مقتدياً أو غيره، وجهرية كانت الصلاة أو سرية، وإن أدركه راكعا تحرى، إن كان أكثر رأيه أنه إن أتى به أدركه في شيء منه أتى به وإلا لا وأطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يبدأ الإمام بالقراءة، وأما إذا بدأ ولو سرية على المعتمد تركه لا المقتدي: لأنه تابع للقراءة، ولا يقرأ المقتدي. [مراقي الفلاح: ۲۸۲] ثم يسمّي [سواء صلى فرضا أو نفلا] كل من يقرأ في صلاته. [مراقي الفلاح: ۲۸۲] فقط أشار إلى أن التسمية لا تسن بين الفاتحة والسورة ولا كراهة فيها إن فعلها اتفاقاً للسورة، سواء جهر أو خافت بالسورة، وغلط من قال: لا يسمي إلا في الركعة الأولى. [مراقي الفلاح بتغيير: ٢٨٢] راكعاً: فيبتدئ بالتكبير الانحناء، ويختمه بختمه؛ ليشرع في التسبيح، فلا تخلو حالة من حالات الصلاة عن ذكر. The manner of composing prayer. Every worshiper: then he seeks refuge silently. The latecomer brings it, not the follower. And it is delayed until after the Eid takbirs. Seeking refuge. Then he says the Basmala silently, and says it in every rak'ah only before al-Fatiha. Then he recited al-Fatiha and the imam says Ameen, i.e., says Ameen, and the follower silently. Then he recited a surah or three verses. Then he said takbir while bowing with tranquility, leveling his head with his back. Every worshiper: is the active participle from alignment. Taking his knees with his hands, spreading his fingers, and glorified in it three times, and that is its minimum. Then he raised his head and was tranquil while bowing saying: 'Allah hears whoever praises Him, our Lord to You is praise' if he is imam or alone. And the follower suffices with the tahmid. Then he said takbir falling down for prostration. Then he placed his knees, then his hands, then his face between his palms and prostrated on his nose with tranquility and his forehead, glorifying three times, and that is its minimum. And he distanced his stomach from his thighs and his upper arms from his armpits, i.e., he separated, except in crowding, pointing his fingers and toes towards the qibla. And the woman lowers herself and sticks her belly, so she brings her upper arms close to her sides and presses them all tightly to her thighs. And he sat between the two prostrations placing his hands on his thighs with tranquility. Then he said takbir and prostrated with tranquility and glorified in it three times. And he distanced his stomach in prostration, i.e., separated from his thighs, and exposed his upper arms. After the takbir: Every worshiper: general, so it includes every worshiper, whether follower or other, and whether the prayer is loud or silent. And if he catches him bowing, he estimates; if his dominant opinion is that if he performs it, he will catch him in some part of it, he performs it; otherwise no. And this is unrestricted, but restricted to when the imam has not started recitation. But if he has started, even silently according to the relied view, he leaves it, not the follower: because he is following the recitation, and the follower does not recite. [Maraqi al-Falah: 282] Then he says the Basmala [whether praying fard or nafl] everyone who recites in his prayer. [Maraqi al-Falah: 282] 'Only' indicates that the Basmala is not sunnah between al-Fatiha and the surah, and there is no dislike if he does it coinciding with the surah, whether he recites the surah loudly or silently. And mistaken is he who said: he does not say the Basmala except in the first rak'ah. [Maraqi al-Falah modified: 282] 'Bowing': he begins the takbir at bending and ends it at its end, to start the tasbih, so no state of prayer is devoid of remembrance. [Maraqi al-Falah: 282] 'His knees etc.': And the man spreads his fingers, straightens his shins, and curving them like a bow is disliked. The woman does not spread her fingers. [Maraqi al-Falah: 282] 'Our Lord to You is praise': and better is: O Allah our Lord to You is praise. [Maraqi al-Falah: 283] 'Falling down': active participle from khurur, i.e., falling, glorifying three times by saying: Glorified is my Lord the Most High. [Maraqi al-Falah: 283] 'Exposed' is past tense from ibda' meaning showing. Then he raised his head saying takbir to stand up, without leaning on the ground with his hands and without sitting. And the second rak'ah is like the first, except that he does not recite thana' and does not seek refuge.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah describes the sequence of actions in the first rak'ah of prayer. It begins by stating that every worshiper (whether imam, follower, or alone) recites ta'awwudh silently, but the latecomer (masbuq) recites it, not the follower (muqtadi), and it is delayed until after the Eid takbirs. Then he says the Basmala silently before al-Fatiha in every rak'ah. After reciting al-Fatiha, the imam says Ameen aloud, the follower silently. Then he recites a surah or at least three verses. The description continues with the bowing (ruku): he says takbir while starting to bow, levels his head with his back, grasps his knees with his fingers spread, and says 'Subhana Rabbi al-'Azim' at least three times. Then he rises and says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, Rabbana lakal hamd' if imam or alone; the follower only says 'Rabbana lakal hamd'. Then he goes into prostration (sujud) saying takbir, placing knees first, then hands, then face between palms, with tranquility, saying 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la' three times. He distances his stomach from thighs and arms from sides, except in crowded situations, and points fingers and toes to the qibla. Women are to be more compact: they lower themselves, stick belly to thighs, and bring arms close to sides. After the first prostration, he sits between the two prostrations with tranquility, then performs a second prostration similarly. The commentary then clarifies that the follower does not recite when the imam is reciting, and discusses the Basmala ruling. After the second prostration of the first rak'ah, he stands for the second rak'ah without leaning on hands and without a rest sitting, and the second rak'ah is like the first except that he omits the thana' (opening supplication) and ta'awwudh.

Key Terms
التعوذ (al-ta'awwudh): Saying 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' before recitation, done silently.
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' before al-Fatiha.
الاطمئنان (al-ithmi'nan): Tranquility and stillness in each posture, such that each limb settles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only after Eid takbirs

Key Takeaway
The first rak'ah of prayer consists of a precise sequence of standing, bowing, prostrating, and sitting, each with its own rulings on obligation and recommendation, and with specific roles for imam, follower, latecomer, and women.
